### Point 3 Criterion

Does the company have an above-average sales organization?

## Point 3 - Question 1

**How does the company’s sales, advertising, and distribution efficiency compare to that of its key competitors?**

### Research Findings

NVIDIA (ticker NVDA) — fiscal year ended Jan 26, 2025
- Revenue (FY2025): $130,497 million. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
- Sales, general and administrative (SG&A): $3,491 million, which is 2.7% of revenue. (This is the company’s selling and marketing plus general administrative spending reported in the 10‑K.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
- Advertising: NVIDIA’s filing does not report a separate “advertising” line; marketing and related costs are included inside SG&A. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
- Accounts receivable, net: $23,065 million. That amount equals about 64.5 days of sales on average (accounts receivable ÷ annual revenue × 365 = 23,065 ÷ 130,497 × 365 ≈ 64.5 days). (This measures how long customers take, on average, to pay NVIDIA.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
- Inventories: $10,080 million. That inventory level equals about 112.8 days of cost of goods sold on hand (inventories ÷ cost of goods sold × 365 = 10,080 ÷ 32,639 × 365 ≈ 112.8 days). (This shows how many days of product NVIDIA holds before selling.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
- Employees: ~36,000 total employees. Revenue per employee ≈ $3.63 million (revenue ÷ employees = 130,497 ÷ 36,000 ≈ $3.63M). (Revenue per employee is a simple measure of how much sales each worker, on average, produces.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

Advanced Micro Devices (AMD) — fiscal year ended Dec 28, 2024
- Revenue (FY2024): $25,785 million. ([ir.amd.com](https://ir.amd.com/financial-information/sec-filings/content/0000002488-25-000012/amd-20241228.htm))  
- Marketing and advertising expense (reported separately): ~$1,200 million for 2024. (AMD discloses “marketing and advertising” as a distinct amount in the 10‑K.) ([ir.amd.com](https://ir.amd.com/financial-information/sec-filings/content/0000002488-25-000012/amd-20241228.htm))  
- Marketing, general and administrative (M&G&A): $2,783 million (this is the broader selling/marketing and administrative total). That equals about 10.8% of revenue (2,783 ÷ 25,785 ≈ 10.8%). ([ir.amd.com](https://ir.amd.com/financial-information/sec-filings/content/0000002488-25-000012/amd-20241228.htm))  
- Accounts receivable, net: $6,192 million. That equals about 87.7 days of sales on average (6,192 ÷ 25,785 × 365 ≈ 87.7 days). (How long customers take to pay AMD.) ([ir.amd.com](https://ir.amd.com/financial-information/sec-filings/content/0000002488-25-000012/amd-20241228.htm))  
- Inventories: $5,734 million. That equals about 87.7 days of cost of goods sold on hand (5,734 ÷ 23,885 × 365 ≈ 87.7 days). (How many days of product AMD holds before selling.) ([ir.amd.com](https://ir.amd.com/financial-information/sec-filings/content/0000002488-25-000012/amd-20241228.htm))  
- Employees: ~28,000. Revenue per employee ≈ $0.92 million (25,785 ÷ 28,000 ≈ $0.921M). ([ir.amd.com](https://ir.amd.com/financial-information/sec-filings/content/0000002488-25-000012/amd-20241228.htm))

Intel Corporation — fiscal year ended Dec 28, 2024
- Revenue (FY2024): $53,101 million. ([scribd.com](https://www.scribd.com/document/904199629/Intel-4?utm_source=openai))  
- Marketing, general and administrative (MG&A): $5,507 million, about 10.4% of revenue. (Intel reports advertising costs inside MG&A.) ([scribd.com](https://www.scribd.com/document/904199629/Intel-4?utm_source=openai))  
- Advertising costs (reported separately): $856 million in 2024. (This number is included in Intel’s notes and shows the portion of MG&A that is direct advertising.) ([intc.com](https://www.intc.com/filings-reports/all-sec-filings/xbrl_doc_only/3815?utm_source=openai))  
- Accounts receivable, net: $3,478 million. That equals about 23.9 days of sales on average (3,478 ÷ 53,101 × 365 ≈ 23.9 days). ([intc.com](https://www.intc.com/filings-reports/all-sec-filings/content/0000050863-25-000074/intc-20250329.htm?utm_source=openai))  
- Inventories: $12,198 million. That equals about 124.6 days of cost of goods sold on hand (12,198 ÷ 35,756 × 365 ≈ 124.6 days). ([intc.com](https://www.intc.com/filings-reports/all-sec-filings/content/0000050863-25-000074/intc-20250329.htm?utm_source=openai))  
- Employees: 108,900 people as of Dec 28, 2024. Revenue per employee ≈ $0.49 million (53,101 ÷ 108,900 ≈ $0.488M). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/50863/000005086325000009/intc-20241228.htm?utm_source=openai))

Sources used (for the numbers above):
- NVIDIA Form 10‑K (fiscal year ended Jan 26, 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
- AMD Form 10‑K (fiscal year ended Dec 28, 2024). ([ir.amd.com](https://ir.amd.com/financial-information/sec-filings/content/0000002488-25-000012/amd-20241228.htm))  
- Intel Form 10‑K / SEC filings (fiscal year ended Dec 28, 2024). ([intc.com](https://www.intc.com/filings-reports/all-sec-filings/content/0000050863-25-000109/intc-20250628.htm))

(End of facts.)

---

## Point 3 - Question 2

**What is the opinion of the company’s customers and competitors regarding the effectiveness of its sales force?**

### Research Findings

- Several competitors and industry sources told U.S. regulators they believe NVIDIA pressures customers to buy multiple NVIDIA products together (for example GPUs plus networking or software), and that discounts or faster supply can be tied to bundled purchases. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/technology/nvidia-faces-us-doj-probe-over-complaints-rivals-information-reports-2024-08-02/?utm_source=openai))

- U.S. and European authorities opened inquiries asking customers and rivals about NVIDIA’s sales and bundling practices; EU regulators sent questionnaires to customers as part of a probe of whether bundling gives NVIDIA an unfair advantage. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/technology/eu-watchdog-probes-nvidia-hardware-bundling-it-scrutinises-runai-deal-2024-12-04/?utm_source=openai))

- A former and current competitor CEO (Tenstorrent’s Jim Keller) said NVIDIA’s sales tactics are “aggressive” and that some customers feel pressured to buy NVIDIA networking gear or other products to secure access to NVIDIA GPUs. ([theinformation.com](https://www.theinformation.com/articles/nvidias-aggressive-sales-tactics-will-backfire-says-rival?utm_source=openai))

- Reporting said some Microsoft managers felt pressured to buy NVIDIA networking cables or other NVIDIA products because they believed doing so would get them faster access to NVIDIA GPUs. ([theinformation.com](https://www.theinformation.com/articles/nvidia-faces-doj-antitrust-probe-over-complaints-from-rivals?utm_source=openai))

- Industry advocacy groups and some analysts warned that customers have complained NVIDIA leverages scarce GPUs to push customers toward buying an NVIDIA hardware-and-software package. ([arstechnica.com](https://arstechnica.com/tech-policy/2024/08/nvidias-dominance-puts-ai-industry-in-dire-danger-groups-warn-doj/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s public statements to media and regulators say the company “wins on merit,” that it competes legally, and that customers can choose other suppliers. NVIDIA said it would provide information to regulators when asked. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/technology/nvidia-faces-us-doj-probe-over-complaints-rivals-information-reports-2024-08-02/?utm_source=openai))

- Large cloud and enterprise customers and partners publicly announce deep technical partnerships with NVIDIA (for example Oracle’s multi-year integrations and co-marketing statements), showing close commercial relationships between NVIDIA sales/partner teams and big customers. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/oracle-and-nvidia-collaborate-to-help-enterprises-accelerate-agentic-ai-inference?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA operates a global partner program (NVIDIA Partner Network) with multiple partner types and levels (Registered, Preferred, Elite) to sell and support its products through distributors, system integrators, cloud partners and resellers. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/about-nvidia/partners/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA names and rewards channel partners (for example distributor awards), which industry announcements present as signs of active channel sales and enablement work. ([marketscreener.com](https://www.marketscreener.com/quote/stock/TD-SYNNEX-CORPORATION-14439/news/TD-SYNNEX-Recognized-as-Americas-Distributor-of-the-Year-by-NVIDIA-49377028/?utm_source=openai))

- Reporting and filings show NVIDIA has very large, concentrated customers: two unnamed customers were reported to account for about 39% of one quarter’s revenue, indicating NVIDIA’s sales and contracts reach very large buyers. ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2025/08/28/nvidias-top-two-mystery-customers-made-up-39percent-of-its-q2-revenue-.html?utm_source=openai))

- In earlier years, some hardware partners publicly criticized an NVIDIA partner program as potentially exclusive or coercive; NVIDIA later ended that specific program after partner and press pushback. ([theverge.com](https://www.theverge.com/2018/5/7/17326122/nvidia-geforce-partner-program-branding-shutdown?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 3 - Question 3

**Does the company make a significant and continuous investment in training its sales personnel to keep them effective and abreast of changing technology?**

### Research Findings

- At the end of fiscal 2024, NVIDIA reported about 29,600 employees worldwide, of which 7,400 worked in sales, marketing, operations, or administrative roles. ([media.felix.fe.training](https://media.felix.fe.training/sec-filings/2024/02/21/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm?utm_source=openai))

- At the end of fiscal 2025, NVIDIA reported about 36,000 employees worldwide, of which 8,900 worked in sales, marketing, operations, or administrative roles. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s annual filings say the company provides employee development through training courses, targeted development programs, mentoring and peer coaching, and a library of live and on‑demand learning experiences; it says it creates learning paths and “constantly upgrade[s]” content to keep employees exposed to current technologies. ([media.felix.fe.training](https://media.felix.fe.training/sec-filings/2024/02/21/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA runs a Certified Instructor Program that trains and certifies people to teach NVIDIA workshops; instructors must pass assessments, be reviewed periodically, and generally re‑certify when course content is updated. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/learn/certified-instructor-program/?utm_source=openai))

- The NVIDIA Partner Network (NPN) includes formal training and enablement requirements for partners; NPN materials say partners must complete specified training and exams (often within set timeframes) and follow joint training plans with NVIDIA. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/about-nvidia/partners/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA offers enterprise training services (hands‑on courses and training‑needs assessments) that are delivered by NVIDIA experts or NVIDIA‑certified instructors. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-in/learn/enterprise/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA posts and recruits for roles focused on sales enablement and sales training (for example: “Senior AI Instructor, Sales” and “Enablement Program Manager, Field Enablement”), with duties to develop and deliver sales training to internal sales teams and channel partners. ([illbeback.ai](https://illbeback.ai/job/senior-ai-instructor-sales/?utm_source=openai))

- External training companies and education partners (for example ExitCertified and Fast Lane) have joined NVIDIA’s partner program to deliver NVIDIA courses and workshops, including hands‑on AI and accelerated‑computing training. ([exitcertified.com](https://www.exitcertified.com/about/newsandawards/exitcertified-expands-portfolio-with-nvidia-training?utm_source=openai))

---

### Point 4 Criterion

Does the company's management have a determination to continue to develop products or processes that will sustain sales growth long after the potential of its current product lines has been exploited?

## Point 4 - Question 1

**What is the company's stated long-term strategy for developing new products or entering new markets? A company's official strategy reveals its forward-thinking and plans for growth beyond the immediate future.**

### Research Findings

- NVIDIA says its core long-term plan is to build “accelerated computing” platforms that combine its chips with software and systems so one technology base can be reused across many large markets (for example: data centers, gaming, professional design, automotive, robotics). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- The company says it will keep developing new families of data‑center computing solutions on a fast cadence (seeking to deliver new computing architectures and more product choices each year) to meet growing AI needs. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- NVIDIA states it will move beyond selling individual chips by expanding software, cloud services, and complete systems (examples named by the company include its AI software stacks, simulation and digital‑twin platform, and cloud/AI system offerings). These software and system products are used to help customers build, test, and run AI applications. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- The company describes entering new markets by creating platform toolkits and reference blueprints (for example, Omniverse blueprints and simulation tools) so partners and customers can build industry‑specific applications such as factory automation, robotics, and autonomous vehicles. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-expands-omniverse-with-generative-physical-ai?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA says it will grow through partnerships and ecosystems — working with cloud providers, software companies, carmakers, industrial firms, and governments — rather than only selling chips directly; these alliances help the company reach new industries and scale deployments. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- The company states it will invest heavily in research and development and in engineering talent to create new products and enter new markets; NVIDIA reported large R&D spending and said much of its workforce is focused on R&D to support new product introductions. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- NVIDIA says it will also expand by building or enabling large AI infrastructure (“AI factories” / systems and cloud instances) and by working with partners to provide full solutions (hardware, networking, and software) so customers can train and run larger AI models at scale. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-First-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 4 - Question 2

**Is there evidence of a continuous effort in research and development (R&D) aimed at improving existing products and creating new ones? Consistent investment and activity in R&D are tangible indicators of a commitment to developing future revenue streams.**

### Research Findings

- NVIDIA reported research and development (R&D) expenses of $8,675 million for the fiscal year ended January 28, 2024. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm))

- NVIDIA’s R&D expense rose by $1,336 million (18%) from fiscal 2023 to fiscal 2024. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm))

- At the end of fiscal year 2024, NVIDIA had about 29,600 employees worldwide, and the company said 22,200 of those employees were engaged in research and development. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm))

- NVIDIA’s 2024 annual report states the company has invested over $45.3 billion in research and development since it was founded. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm))

- NVIDIA’s SEC filing shows $3,376 million in capitalized research and development expenditures recorded as deferred tax assets as of January 28, 2024. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm))

- NVIDIA publicly announced the Blackwell GPU architecture and GB200 chips in March 2024, and later announced Blackwell Ultra / GB300 products and rack systems in 2025. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2024/NVIDIA-Blackwell-Platform-Arrives-to-Power-a-New-Era-of-Computing/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA announced its next-generation Rubin (GPU) and Vera (CPU) products (called Vera Rubin) with expected shipping dates in the second half of 2026 and follow-on Rubin Ultra/Rubin Next products announced for later years. ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2025/03/18/nvidia-announces-blackwell-ultra-and-vera-rubin-ai-chips-.html?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA continues to release new GPU and system products across markets (examples: Hopper architecture in 2022, Blackwell family in 2024–2025, and new professional Blackwell-based cards announced at SIGGRAPH 2025). ([en.wikipedia.org](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hopper_%28microarchitecture%29?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA develops and maintains software and model toolkits used by developers and data centers, including CUDA (introduced in 2006, cited in company filings) and the NeMo framework and NeMo microservices for training and deploying large AI models. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm))

- NVIDIA’s public materials and third‑party reports show a large and growing patent portfolio (reported at roughly 15,553 patents in a 2024 patent database and about 17,324 patents in a 2025 patent database). ([insights.greyb.com](https://insights.greyb.com/nvidia-corporation-patents?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s 2024 annual report notes an in‑process research and development intangible asset of $630 million related to the company’s acquisition of Mellanox, which began amortization in fiscal 2023. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm))

- NVIDIA’s press releases and technical documentation show ongoing software releases and updates (for example, regular releases and documentation for the NeMo framework and versioned NeMo training containers in 2024–2025). ([docs.nvidia.com](https://docs.nvidia.com/nemo-framework/user-guide/latest/softwarecomponentversions.html?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 4 - Question 3

**Does the company's research and development appear to be focused on products related to its current business activities, or is it venturing into many unrelated fields? Focused innovation in related fields often yields better results than scattered efforts in unconnected industries.**

### Research Findings

- NVIDIA spent $12,914 million on research and development in fiscal year 2025 (year ended Jan 26, 2025). % of revenue for R&D was 9.9% in that year. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- At the end of fiscal 2025, NVIDIA reported about 36,000 total employees and said about 27,100 of them worked in research and development. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- The company says it uses a “platform” approach: a single programmable chip and common software stacks that can be used across several markets (for example gaming, data centers, autonomous vehicles, robotics, and digital twins). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- NVIDIA lists two main operating segments: “Compute & Networking” and “Graphics.” Many products and R&D descriptions are grouped under these segments. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- NVIDIA’s core software for developers is CUDA, a toolbox and programming environment that lets programmers use NVIDIA GPUs for many kinds of computing (scientific computing, AI training, data processing, etc.). ([developer.nvidia.com](https://developer.nvidia.com/cuda-toolkit?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA publishes and develops many software platforms and toolkits tied to its hardware, including:
  - Omniverse (a 3D/simulation and “digital twin” platform used for industry and simulation). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Omniverse-Physical-AI-Operating-System-Expands-to-More-Industries-and-Partners/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))
  - DGX systems and DGX Cloud (systems and cloud services for AI model training and deployment). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Fourth-Quarter-and-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))
  - NVIDIA AI Enterprise, TensorRT, cuDNN and other libraries that speed AI and graphics software on NVIDIA hardware. ([developer.nvidia.com](https://developer.nvidia.com/cuda-toolkit?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA develops products for autonomous driving under the DRIVE brand (examples: DRIVE AGX developer kits, DRIVE Thor platform). The DRIVE platform includes vehicle-grade chips, reference hardware, and software for driving, cockpit features, and safety. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-unveils-drive-thor-centralized-car-computer-unifying-cluster-infotainment-automated-driving-and-parking-in-a-single-cost-saving-system?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA builds edge and robotics computer modules under the Jetson brand and a robotics software stack called Isaac; it announced robotics-focused projects (Project GR00T) and Jetson/Isaac tools for training and running robots. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/foundation-model-isaac-robotics-platform?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA makes data-center CPUs and CPU–GPU modules (the Grace CPU family and Grace Hopper/Grace Superchip) designed to work tightly with its GPUs for large AI and high-performance computing tasks. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/data-center/grace-cpu-superchip/?utm_source=openai))

- Through its 2020 acquisition of Mellanox, NVIDIA added high-speed networking and SmartNIC/DPU technology (BlueField family), which NVIDIA now lists as part of its data-center infrastructure product line. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-completes-acquisition-of-mellanox-creating-major-force-driving-next-gen-data-centers?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA has bought or integrated smaller companies whose technology fits into its computing and AI stack, for example:
  - DeepMap (high-definition mapping for autonomous vehicles), acquired in 2021 and folded into DRIVE mapping products. ([blogs.nvidia.com](https://blogs.nvidia.com/blog/nvidia-deepmap-mapping-drive-platform/?utm_source=openai))
  - Run:ai (AI infrastructure/workload management), announced April 2024 and completed late 2024 — software that helps manage GPU workloads and that NVIDIA planned to integrate into its AI infrastructure offerings. ([techcrunch.com](https://techcrunch.com/2024/04/24/NVIDIA-acquires-ai-workload-management-startup-runai/?utm_source=openai))

- In 2024, media reports said NVIDIA deployed about $1 billion in investments and corporate deals to back AI start-ups and partners across industries (the company described these as ecosystem and technology partnerships in AI). ([ft.com](https://www.ft.com/content/f8acce90-9c4d-4433-b189-e79cad29f74e?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s financial reports and press releases show very large recent growth in data-center revenue and say data‑center compute and networking drove revenue growth in fiscal 2025 (for example: record data-center revenue and product rollouts to major cloud providers). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Fourth-Quarter-and-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s 2025 annual report (Form 10‑K) notes the company increased R&D spending drivers: higher compensation for R&D staff, much larger spending on compute and infrastructure used for development, and big increases in engineering development costs for new product introductions. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Examples of recent product/technology announcements tied to NVIDIA’s core areas:
  - New GPU and system releases aimed at large language models and generative AI (announcements in 2024–2025 about Blackwell-family GPUs and GB/GB200 systems for cloud customers). ([apnews.com](https://apnews.com/article/457e9260aa2a34c1bbcc07c98b7a0555?utm_source=openai))
  - Omniverse expansions and industry blueprints aiming to use simulation and synthetic data for industry and robotics. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Omniverse-Physical-AI-Operating-System-Expands-to-More-Industries-and-Partners/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s public materials repeatedly describe R&D that connects hardware design (GPUs, DPUs, CPUs, SoCs), software stacks (CUDA, libraries, developer tools), and industry platforms (data center, automotive DRIVE, robotics Jetson/Isaac, Omniverse), and they list customers and partners in those same fields. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

---

### Point 5 Criterion

Does the company have outstanding executive relations?

## Point 5 - Question 1

**Do executives have confidence in their president and/or board chairman?**

### Research Findings

- Company name and ticker: NVIDIA Corporation (ticker: NVDA). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Jensen Huang is listed by the company as President and Chief Executive Officer (he is also a member of the Board). (Proxy statement, May 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- The Board does not use a single “chairperson” role; instead it designates an independent Lead Director. The Lead Director named in the 2025 proxy is Stephen C. Neal. The proxy explains the Lead Director’s duties (for example: setting Board meeting schedules, advising the CEO on Board materials, presiding at meetings when the CEO is absent, and leading executive sessions of independent directors). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- The company filed its definitive proxy materials for the 2025 annual meeting (proxy filed May 13, 2025) and held the Annual Meeting on June 25, 2025. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- At the June 25, 2025 annual meeting, stockholders voted on management proposals including re-election of directors and an advisory (non-binding) vote on executive pay. The company reported that shareholders approved the advisory vote on executive compensation; reported vote totals were: For 14,806,756,684; Against 1,320,594,290; Abstaining 65,736,681; Broker non-votes 3,206,621,218. ([streetinsider.com](https://www.streetinsider.com/SEC%2BFilings/Form%2B8-K%2BNVIDIA%2BCORP%2BFor%3A%2BJun%2B25/25000593.html?utm_source=openai))

- News coverage and company materials reported that, at the 2025 meeting and in related filings, the board nominees were re-elected (the company’s proxy and press materials list the director slate and the meeting results). (See company proxy and news articles summarizing the June 25, 2025 meeting). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- The proxy states the Board has determined that, except for Mr. Huang, all directors are “independent” under Nasdaq rules. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- The proxy includes a Compensation Committee Report stating the Compensation Committee reviewed the company’s Compensation Discussion and Analysis and recommended it be included in the company’s Form 10‑K and proxy materials. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- The company disclosed in filings and press coverage that Jensen Huang’s total pay rose in the 2025 filing (reported total compensation figures and a base‑salary increase were disclosed in the proxy/SEC filing and covered by news outlets). ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2025/05/01/nvidia-ceo-jensen-huang-gets-first-salary-raise-in-a-decade.html?utm_source=openai))

- Several stockholder proposals about governance (for example, removing supermajority provisions and changing special meeting/board‑resignation policies) were presented at the 2025 meeting and were not adopted by stockholders; the company filed the detailed vote results in a Form 8‑K. (Example vote totals for Proposal 4 to remove supermajority provisions: For 16,018,866,893; Against 152,574,185; Abstaining 21,646,577; Broker non‑votes 3,206,621,218 — note some proposals required higher thresholds than a simple majority). ([streetinsider.com](https://www.streetinsider.com/SEC%2BFilings/Form%2B8-K%2BNVIDIA%2BCORP%2BFor%3A%2BJun%2B25/25000593.html?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 5 - Question 2

**Is there a general sense, from the lowest levels upward, that promotions are based on ability rather than factionalism or favoritism toward a ruling family?**

### Research Findings

- Company identity: NVIDIA Corporation (ticker NVDA) is an American technology company that designs and sells graphics processing units (GPUs) and related software and systems. (NVIDIA careers page; general company profile). ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/about-nvidia/careers/?utm_source=openai))

- Founder and chief executive: Jensen (Jen‑Hsun) Huang is a co‑founder and the company’s president and CEO. (NVIDIA leadership listings and company profiles). ([en.wikipedia.org](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nvidia?utm_source=openai))

- Founder ownership and family holdings (public filing): In NVIDIA’s SEC proxy filings, Jensen Huang is reported as a significant stockholder; filings list shares held directly and by related trusts and family members. The 2023 definitive proxy showed Huang’s total beneficial ownership reported around mid‑single digits of outstanding shares (filing numbers and tables). (SEC proxy statement filings). ([edgar.secdatabase.com](https://edgar.secdatabase.com/1068/104581023000080/filing-main.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Board and governance (public filing): NVIDIA’s annual proxy statements list the company’s board of directors and governance documents. Those filings show a board with multiple non‑employee directors and formal governance charters. (DEF 14A / proxy statements). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000104/nvda-20240514.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Company written policies: NVIDIA publishes a Code of Conduct, an Equal Employment Opportunity policy, an Anti‑Harassment policy, and other corporate policies (including a confidential “Speak Up” reporting channel). These documents state the company’s formal rules against discrimination and harassment and provide channels to report workplace problems. (Corporate policies page on NVIDIA’s website; policy PDFs). ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-in/about-nvidia/company-policies/?utm_source=openai))

- Public statements by the CEO about people development: Jensen Huang has publicly described preferring to develop employees rather than fire them, saying in interviews that he often pushes people hard and gives them chances to improve. These remarks appear in several published interviews and reporting. (Interviews and press coverage, 2024–2025). ([startuparchive.org](https://www.startuparchive.org/p/jensen-huang-on-why-he-rarely-fires-people-and-will-instead-torture-them-into-greatness?utm_source=openai))

- Reported internal culture and management style (press and employee accounts): Multiple news profiles (including Business Insider reporting in 2025) describe NVIDIA’s culture as high‑intensity, mission‑driven, and relatively flat in parts, with strong technical expectations, significant autonomy for engineers, and many managers reporting directly to senior leaders. Reporting notes low turnover and that many employees cite learning and heavy responsibility early in their tenure. (Business Insider; other press). ([businessinsider.com](https://www.businessinsider.com/nvidia-hardcore-intensity-culture-mission-driven-jensen-huang-2025-4?utm_source=openai))

- Job levels, promotion ladder, and compensation patterns (public crowd‑sourced and company data): Public compensation and career‑level sites (e.g., Levels.fyi) show NVIDIA uses an individual contributor (IC) level ladder (IC1, IC2, IC3, etc.) with defined median pay bands and typical promotion paths between levels. Those pages also document NVIDIA’s standard RSU (restricted stock unit) vesting patterns used in employee compensation. These sources are based on reported employee submissions. (Levels.fyi pages for NVIDIA). ([levels.fyi](https://www.levels.fyi/companies/nvidia/salaries/software-engineer?utm_source=openai))

- Employee survey / review site data: On Glassdoor, NVIDIA’s company page (reviews collected through mid‑2025) shows a high overall rating (around 4.6 out of 5) and very high CEO approval scores reported by reviewers. Glassdoor review text includes many positive comments about learning and leadership, and a small number of reviews list “favoritism” or uneven middle management as a negative. (Glassdoor company pages; NVIDIA statements about Glassdoor awards). ([glassdoor.com](https://www.glassdoor.com/Reviews/NVIDIA-nvidia-Reviews-EI_IE7633.0%2C6_KH7%2C13.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Public legal and regulatory record (search of major news and court filings): Public news and court‑filing searches from 2018 through Oct 7, 2025 show several litigation matters involving NVIDIA (for example, trade‑secret and intellectual‑property cases and shareholder securities litigation reported in major news outlets). Searches did not return major, widely reported government enforcement actions or large‑scale court judgments specifically alleging that NVIDIA’s promotions are controlled by a “ruling family” or that the company operates a system of formal, company‑wide promotions based on family favoritism (major news and SEC filings reviewed). (Representative news and court filing results; SEC filings and news coverage). ([law.justia.com](https://law.justia.com/cases/federal/district-courts/california/candce/5%3A2023cv05721/420527/179/?utm_source=openai))

- Formal employee channels for disputes and appeals (policy facts): NVIDIA’s policies describe formal HR and reporting routes (for example, internal complaint channels, anonymized reporting through a “Speak Up” line, and documented policies on equal employment). These documents indicate the company has written procedures employees can use to raise concerns about conduct or decisions. They do not, by themselves, describe the day‑to‑day mechanics of promotion decisions on every team. (NVIDIA corporate policies and Code of Conduct). ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-in/about-nvidia/company-policies/?utm_source=openai))

- Timing and sources: The facts above are drawn from NVIDIA’s public website (policies and careers pages), SEC proxy filings (DEF 14A filings), employee‑reported compensation and level sites (Levels.fyi), Glassdoor company pages and awards, and news reporting including Business Insider and other outlets. Dates and document years appear in the cited sources (proxy filings 2023–2025; press reporting 2024–2025; policy pages current on NVIDIA’s site as published). ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/about-nvidia/careers/?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 5 - Question 3

**Are salary adjustments reviewed regularly so that executives feel merited increases will be granted without having to be requested?**

### Research Findings

- Company: NVIDIA Corporation (ticker: NVDA). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000095/nvda-20250512.htm))

- Who decides executive pay: NVIDIA’s Board has a Compensation Committee (CC) that oversees and approves executive pay and related policies. The CC reviews and approves compensation for the CEO and other named executive officers. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000104/nvda-20240514.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Committee independence and meetings: The CC’s members are independent (they are not company officers or employees). In fiscal 2024 the CC met four times. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000104/nvda-20240514.htm?utm_source=openai))

- How decisions are made: The CC uses a formal process that includes selecting peer companies, reviewing market pay data, considering internal pay equity, assessing individual performance and unvested equity levels, and reviewing management’s recommendations. The CC also uses input from an independent compensation consultant. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000095/nvda-20250512.htm))

- Independent consultants: For the period covered, the CC used Exequity LLP as its independent compensation consultant and engaged Semler Brossy later in 2024; the CC evaluated whether those consultants posed conflicts of interest and concluded they did not. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000095/nvda-20250512.htm))

- Timing and frequency of the main review: The proxy says the CC’s compensation work is a multi-step process across months (examples listed include November and December of one year and March and April–May of the next). The proxy also states that, typically, the CC completes its annual executive compensation review, sets performance goals and target compensation, and grants equity awards in March. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000095/nvda-20250512.htm))

- Approval and certification: The CC approves all equity award grants to executive officers on or before the grant date, and the CC certifies achievement and payouts under the company’s variable cash and PSU plans when performance periods end. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000095/nvda-20250512.htm))

- Example of recent base-salary action: For fiscal 2025 the CC increased CEO Jensen Huang’s base salary from about $1,000,000 to $1,500,000 (a 50% increase), noting it was his first base-salary increase in about ten years; many other named executive officers’ base salaries were reported as unchanged for that fiscal year. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000095/nvda-20250512.htm))

- Elements considered when setting pay: The CC describes total target pay as the sum of (1) annual base salary, (2) target variable cash opportunity under the Variable Cash Plan, and (3) target equity opportunity; the CC compares those totals to peer-company data when setting targets. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000095/nvda-20250512.htm))

- Exceptions to the annual cycle: The proxy notes that the CC may grant equity awards outside the annual March cycle for new hires, promotions, recognition, retention or other purposes. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000095/nvda-20250512.htm))

---

## Point 5 - Question 4

**Are executive salaries at least in line with the industry and local standards?**

### Research Findings

- Company and period: NVIDIA Corporation (ticker NVDA). The figures below are for fiscal year 2025 (the fiscal year that ended January 26, 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Jensen (Jen‑Hsun) Huang, NVIDIA President and CEO, fiscal 2025:
  - Base salary (cash paid): $1,486,199. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Non‑equity cash bonus (variable cash): $6,000,000. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Stock awards (grant‑date accounting value of restricted/ performance stock units): $38,811,306. (This is an accounting value for equity grants, not cash paid at grant.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Other reported compensation (includes residential security, driver services, 401(k) match, life insurance): $3,568,746. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Total reported compensation for fiscal 2025: $49,866,251. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Other named executives (Named Executive Officers, fiscal 2025 totals and key parts):
  - Colette M. Kress (EVP and CFO): salary $893,739; stock awards $19,849,891; variable cash $600,000; total $21,362,532. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Ajay K. Puri (EVP, Worldwide Field Operations): salary $943,391; stock awards $19,277,046; variable cash $1,300,000; total $21,590,897. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Debora Shoquist (EVP, Operations): salary $844,087; stock awards $17,838,832; variable cash $500,000; total $19,217,903. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Timothy S. Teter (EVP, General Counsel & Secretary): salary $844,087; stock awards $17,838,832; variable cash $500,000; total $19,201,821. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- How much of pay is in stock awards (grant‑date accounting values, fiscal 2025):
  - Jensen Huang: $38.8M of $49.87M ≈ 78% reported as stock awards (grant‑date fair value). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Colette Kress: $19.85M of $21.36M ≈ 93% reported as stock awards (grant‑date fair value). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Ajay Puri: $19.28M of $21.59M ≈ 89% reported as stock awards (grant‑date fair value). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Debora Shoquist and Timothy Teter: each about $17.84M of ≈ $19.2M total ≈ 93% reported as stock awards (grant‑date fair value). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Note: the proxy clarifies that the “Stock Awards” amounts shown are the accounting (grant‑date fair) values, not the cash the person received at the time of grant. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Outstanding / unvested equity at January 26, 2025 (estimated value reported in proxy):
  - Jensen Huang — total estimated benefit from unvested RSUs/PSUs: $280,560,638 (based on the company’s reported valuation method). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Colette M. Kress — $118,082,229. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Ajay K. Puri — $113,837,858. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Debora Shoquist — $98,827,103. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Timothy S. Teter — $98,827,103. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Median NVIDIA employee pay and the company’s CEO‑to‑median pay ratio (fiscal 2025):
  - Median (middle) employee total compensation: $301,233 for fiscal 2025. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - NVIDIA’s reported CEO (Huang) total compensation: $49,866,251 for fiscal 2025. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Reported CEO‑to‑median employee pay ratio: 166:1 for fiscal 2025. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Where NVIDIA reports these figures: detailed compensation tables, the “Summary Compensation Table,” and the “Pay Ratio” disclosure are in NVIDIA’s fiscal 2025 proxy statement filed with the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission (Schedule 14A). The proxy was filed in May 2025 and covers fiscal year 2025 (year ended January 26, 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Examples of peer / industry CEO pay (for context, fiscal years as reported by each company):
  - Advanced Micro Devices (AMD), CEO Lisa Su: total compensation reported for fiscal 2024 ≈ $30,996,392. (AMD’s proxy / compensation table.) ([aflcio.org](https://aflcio.org/paywatch/AMD?utm_source=openai))
  - Intel Corporation, CEO total compensation reported for fiscal 2024 ≈ $27,429,900 (company disclosure / filings compiling fiscal 2024 data). ([intc.com](https://www.intc.com/filings-reports/all-sec-filings/content/0000050863-25-000054/intc-20250327.htm?utm_source=openai))
  - Alphabet (Google), CEO Sundar Pichai: total compensation reported for fiscal 2024 ≈ $10,730,000 (proxy disclosure; larger non‑cash items apply at different times). ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2025/04/28/google-increased-ceo-sundar-pichais-security-costs-by-22percent.html?utm_source=openai))

- S&P 500 / large U.S. company median CEO pay (for a high‑level industry benchmark):
  - Reporting by news/data services noted the median total pay for S&P 500 CEOs was about $16.3 million in the referenced recent year. (This is a cross‑company median, published by press analysis of executive pay surveys.) ([apnews.com](https://apnews.com/article/acf14f0a4dc4f8e64aabaa1f0e4632ef?utm_source=openai))

- Notes on how the company presents pay:
  - NVIDIA’s proxy shows several pay components: base salary (cash), variable cash bonuses, stock awards (grant‑date accounting values for restricted/performance units), and “all other” items (perks, security, retirement matches, insurance). The proxy also explains its method for calculating the company’s reported pay ratio and the accounting basis for stock awards. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

Sources (selected):
- NVIDIA Corporation, Proxy Statement (Schedule 14A), filed May 2025 — Summary Compensation Table, Pay Ratio, and related disclosures. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
- CNBC coverage of NVIDIA compensation and filing (summary of key figures). ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2025/05/01/nvidia-ceo-jensen-huang-gets-first-salary-raise-in-a-decade.html?utm_source=openai))
- AMD Proxy Statement and compensation tables (CEO Lisa Su). ([ir.amd.com](https://ir.amd.com/financial-information/sec-filings/content/0001193125-25-067170/d869673ddef14a.htm?utm_source=openai))
- Intel SEC filing and compiled compensation data (fiscal 2024 CEO pay). ([intc.com](https://www.intc.com/filings-reports/all-sec-filings/content/0000050863-25-000054/intc-20250327.htm?utm_source=openai))
- News analysis of S&P 500 CEO median pay. ([apnews.com](https://apnews.com/article/acf14f0a4dc4f8e64aabaa1f0e4632ef?utm_source=openai))

## Point 5 - Question 5

**Does executive management avoid bringing in outsiders for roles beyond entry-level positions unless there is no qualified internal candidate available?**

### Research Findings

- NVIDIA’s 2025 proxy statement says the board’s Nominating and Corporate Governance Committee (NCGC) “identifies, reviews, and evaluates candidates” for the board and handles board recruiting. The proxy does not set out a rule that senior jobs must go to internal candidates. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- NVIDIA’s public executive biography for Colette Kress says she joined NVIDIA as CFO in September 2013 after nearly 25 years at other large technology companies (Cisco, Microsoft, Texas Instruments). This is an example of an outside hire for a top executive role. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/about-nvidia/governance/management-team/colette-kress//?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s public executive biography for Debora Shoquist says she joined NVIDIA in 2007 from other firms (JDS Uniphase, Coherent, Quantum, HP) and later became Executive Vice President of Operations. This is another example of an outside executive hire who rose to a senior role. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/about-nvidia/governance/management-team/debora-shoquist/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA has publicly named outside leaders to its board of directors (for example, Ellen Ochoa was named to NVIDIA’s board on November 7, 2024). This shows the company brings external people into senior governance roles. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2024/NVIDIA-Names-Ellen-Ochoa-to-Board-of-Directors/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Multiple news reports note that NVIDIA’s CEO structure centers on founder Jensen Huang and that the company has not publicly named a clear successor; journalists and governance observers have said the company does not have a publicly disclosed, named CEO successor or a detailed succession plan. ([businessinsider.com](https://www.businessinsider.com/nvidia-ceo-jensen-huang-stephen-witt-thinking-machine-book-biography-2025-4?utm_source=openai))

- Reuters reported in September 2025 that NVIDIA spent more than $900 million to hire the CEO and other personnel from the startup Enfabrica and to license its technology—an example of NVIDIA paying to bring external senior technical talent into the company. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/technology/nvidia-spent-over-900-million-hire-enfabrica-ceo-license-technology-cnbc-reports-2025-09-18/?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 5 - Question 6

**Does top management acknowledge the inevitability of some factionalism and interpersonal friction, but refuse to tolerate individuals who disrupt team cooperation, thereby minimizing such issues?**

### Research Findings

- Jensen Huang (NVIDIA’s CEO) has said in public talks that he prefers to help people improve instead of firing them; he has been quoted saying he’d “rather improve you than give up on you” and joking that he would “torture you into greatness.” ([livemint.com](https://www.livemint.com/companies/people/nvidia-jensen-huang-doesnt-fire-people-cleaned-bathrooms-now-ceo-can-learn-need-opportunity-torture-you-into-greatness-11718165859454.html?utm_source=openai))

- Huang runs a very flat, hands-on management style: he has many direct reports, says “the mission is the boss,” and openly gives feedback in group settings so everyone hears it at once. ([businessinsider.com](https://www.businessinsider.com/nvidia-jensen-huang-management-leadership-advice-how-to-run-business-2024-6?utm_source=openai))

- Former and current employees told reporters (Bloomberg and others) that NVIDIA meetings can be intense and sometimes include shouting or fights; several people described a “pressure‑cooker” environment with long hours and heated meetings. ([finance.yahoo.com](https://finance.yahoo.com/news/nvidia-employees-often-seven-days-193653866.html?utm_source=openai))

- Reported comments from former staff and company observers say Jensen Huang “doesn’t tolerate bullshit” or self‑serving behavior; observers describe a culture that calls out people who act against the company mission. ([politicalriskwire.com](https://politicalriskwire.com/nvidias-hardcore-culture-how-ceo-jensen-huang-drives-accountability/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s official codes of conduct (for conferences and open‑source projects) explicitly forbid harassment, bullying, and sustained disruption; they say organizers will enforce rules and may warn, remove, or bar people who violate the rules. The company provides ways to report incidents and investigates complaints. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/gtc/code-of-conduct/?utm_source=openai))

---

### Point 6 Criterion

Does the company have outstanding labor and personnel relations?

## Point 6 - Question 1

**Does the company experience frequent or prolonged strikes or other major work stoppages?**

### Research Findings

- NVIDIA’s public filings and legal agreements state that, to the company’s knowledge, it is not party to any collective bargaining (union) agreements and, in the recent years covered by those documents, the company reported no strikes, slowdowns, work stoppages, lockouts or similar labor actions affecting its business. ([content.edgar-online.com](https://content.edgar-online.com/ExternalLink/EDGAR/0001045810-19-000031.html?dest=ex21mergeragreement_htm&hash=4a95f3b3546ebf5e02371d68f0fbb1c3e6552ac4bd3626dbd16d10568789e96a&utm_source=openai))

- In legal and merger-related disclosures NVIDIA has said there were no threatened or pending labor-organizing petitions or representation disputes involving its employees during the past several years covered by those filings. ([content.edgar-online.com](https://content.edgar-online.com/ExternalLink/EDGAR/0001045810-19-000031.html?dest=ex21mergeragreement_htm&hash=4a95f3b3546ebf5e02371d68f0fbb1c3e6552ac4bd3626dbd16d10568789e96a&utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s SEC filings and investor documents state the company relies on third parties (contract manufacturers and foundries) to manufacture, assemble, package and test its chips and products. This means NVIDIA’s supply and production can be affected by labor actions at its suppliers. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000124/nvda-20240428.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Major suppliers in the semiconductor supply chain have experienced strikes. For example, Samsung Electronics had a multi-day strike by semiconductor-related workers in July 2024; such supplier strikes can affect companies that buy chips or memory from those suppliers. ([ft.com](https://www.ft.com/content/62d4cbe1-6c0f-4803-99e1-4233b8b8eb87?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA uses outside foundries such as TSMC for chip manufacturing and has publicly discussed TSMC as a key manufacturing/packaging partner; disruptions at those foundries (for any reason, including labor disputes) could affect NVIDIA’s product supply. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/world/china/nvidia-orders-300000-h20-chips-tsmc-due-robust-china-demand-sources-say-2025-07-29/?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 6 - Question 2

**Is the workforce unionized? If it is, how cooperative and mutually respectful is the company’s relationship with the union? If it is not, is there evidence that constructive personnel policies account for the absence of union activity?**

### Research Findings

- Company and size: NVIDIA Corporation (ticker NVDA) reported about 36,000 employees in 38 countries at the end of fiscal year 2025. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Where employees work: In that filing NVIDIA said roughly 27,100 employees do research and development work and about 8,900 work in sales, marketing, operations, and administrative roles. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Statement about collective bargaining and unions (from company transaction documents): In recent merger/sale agreements NVIDIA represented that, except for items listed in the agreement schedules, neither the company nor its subsidiaries are parties to any collective bargaining agreement, and to the company’s knowledge no labor organization represents or is seeking to represent its current employees; the documents also state no union organizing activity has occurred in the recent years covered by the agreements. (text from NVIDIA transaction/merger disclosures). ([contracts.justia.com](https://contracts.justia.com/companies/nvidia-corporation-978/contract/128612/?utm_source=openai))

- Employee compensation program (company statements): NVIDIA says it gives employees equity awards (stock or stock-like grants) except where local rules prevent that, and those equity awards vest over time as part of pay and retention. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581023000080/nvda-20230508.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Median pay / pay statistics reported in company filings and media: NVIDIA’s public proxy filing for an earlier year reported a median employee annual compensation of about $228,078 (fiscal 2023, per the company’s proxy disclosure). Media reports citing company data and payroll analyses have noted that many NVIDIA employees earn well above typical industry medians. ([ih.advfn.com](https://ih.advfn.com/stock-market/NASDAQ/nvidia-NVDA/stock-news/90989639/proxy-statement-definitive-def-14a?utm_source=openai))

- Turnover and retention (company statements): NVIDIA reported a low overall employee turnover rate of 2.7% for fiscal 2024 and reported a 5.3% turnover rate for fiscal 2023 in its public filings. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000104/nvda-20240514.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Pay-parity and third‑party review (company statements): NVIDIA says it uses an independent, third‑party firm to analyze pay and promotion practices and reported it had achieved “pay parity” (no statistically significant differences in pay by gender, race, or ethnicity) in the years described in its filings. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000104/nvda-20240514.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Benefits and workplace programs (company statements): NVIDIA’s filings list benefits and programs including 401(k) and statutory pensions (where required outside the U.S.), an employee stock purchase program, tuition reimbursement, career coaching and mentoring programs, mental‑health and well‑being supports, a hybrid/ flexible work approach, a quarterly company “rest days” policy, a suggestion box, and an anonymous third‑party reporting platform. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581023000080/nvda-20230508.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Workforce composition (company statements): NVIDIA’s filings state the workforce is heavily technical (about 82% technical in the 2025 filing) and that a large share of employees hold advanced degrees. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Company statements about employee engagement and development: NVIDIA’s public filings describe training, learning paths, internal mobility, and promotion programs used to develop and retain employees. The filings say the company uses pulse surveys and other channels to measure employee sentiment. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000104/nvda-20240514.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Company disclosures about labor disputes: In the contracts and merger-related disclosures cited above, NVIDIA represented there were no strikes, work stoppages, pending labor disputes, or threatened labor disputes affecting the business in the periods covered by those disclosure statements. ([contracts.justia.com](https://contracts.justia.com/companies/nvidia-corporation-978/contract/128612/?utm_source=openai))

(End of facts.)

---

## Point 6 - Question 3

**How does the company’s labor-turnover rate compare with local or industry peers? Is there evidence of an unusually large pool of applicants seeking employment at the company?**

### Research Findings

- NVIDIA reported an overall employee turnover (annual attrition) rate of 2.7% for fiscal 2024 (fiscal year ended January 28, 2024). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000104/nvda-20240514.htm))

- NVIDIA reported an overall employee turnover (annual attrition) rate of 2.5% for fiscal 2025 (fiscal year ended January 26, 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- NVIDIA’s workforce size at the end of fiscal 2025 was about 36,000 employees, with about 27,100 in research & development and 8,900 in sales, marketing, operations, and administrative roles. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s proxy and sustainability disclosures say the company fills many roles by employee referral (about 40–41% of new hires in fiscal 2024–2025 came from referrals). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000104/nvda-20240514.htm))

- Intel reported an “undesired turnover” rate of 5.9% for 2024 (Intel’s Form 10‑K / SEC filing). ([intc.com](https://www.intc.com/filings-reports/all-sec-filings/content/0000050863-25-000009/intc-20241228.htm?utm_source=openai))

- TSMC reported an overall employee turnover rate of 6.7% in 2022 and reported a lower overall turnover rate of about 3.7% in 2023 and 3.35% in 2024 in its annual reports. ([investor.tsmc.com](https://investor.tsmc.com/static/annualReports/2022/english/ebook/files/basic-html/page118.html?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA had thousands of public job postings in recent years: a November 2023 report said about 1,810 open positions worldwide, and job-posting trackers showed NVIDIA listing roughly 1,700–3,000 open roles at various points in 2024–2025. ([businessinsider.com](https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-get-job-nvidia-ai-artificial-intelligence-skills-salary-2023-11?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA is highly ranked as an employer in public employee-review lists (for example, NVIDIA placed near the top of Glassdoor’s “Best Places to Work” lists in 2024 and 2025). ([forbes.com](https://www.forbes.com/sites/lucianapaulise/2024/01/10/glassdoor-unveils-the-best-places-to-work-in-2024/?utm_source=openai))

- Public filings and reports show NVIDIA actively recruits technical talent worldwide (NVIDIA describes its workforce as more than 80% technical and highlights college and professional recruiting programs in its disclosures). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000104/nvda-20240514.htm))

- Third‑party visa/employment data show substantial U.S. H‑1B / labor condition application activity by NVIDIA: aggregated filings and certifications in 2022–2024 number in the thousands (labor-condition-application summaries). ([myvisajobs.com](https://www.myvisajobs.com/employer/nvidia/?utm_source=openai))

- U.S. government labor statistics (JOLTS / BLS) show broader sector-level measures of churn and quits (for example, the national quits rate and quits/separations by industry are published monthly and annually by the Bureau of Labor Statistics). ([bls.gov](https://www.bls.gov/news.release/archives/jolts_03062024.htm?utm_source=openai))

Sources (selected): NVIDIA fiscal proxy/SEC filings (2024, 2025); TSMC annual reports; Intel Form 10‑K; Business Insider reporting on NVIDIA job openings; job-posting tracker summaries; Glassdoor/press coverage; MyVisaJobs H‑1B/LCA summaries; U.S. Bureau of Labor Statistics (JOLTS). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000104/nvda-20240514.htm))
