## Point 6 - Question 4

**Are employee grievances resolved promptly through established procedures, preventing small issues from escalating?**

### Research Findings

- NVIDIA posts a Code of Conduct, an Anti‑Harassment / Discrimination Policy, a Human Rights policy and other workplace policies on its public Company Policies page. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/about-nvidia/company-policies/))

- NVIDIA tells employees they can report problems confidentially using a “Speak Up Line.” The Speak Up link on NVIDIA’s policies page goes to a secure.ethicspoint.com address (an external reporting service). ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/about-nvidia/company-policies/))

- NVIDIA’s Anti‑Harassment Policy says employees who feel they were harassed, discriminated against, or retaliated against must report the matter to their HR Business Partner (HRBP) or, if they want to remain anonymous, they can use the anonymous Speak‑Up Line. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/content/dam/en-zz/Solutions/about-us/documents/NVIDIA_Anti-Harassment_Discrimination_Policy-Sep-2020.pdf))

- The Anti‑Harassment Policy requires managers who learn about harassment or discrimination to report it to HR immediately, even if the employee asked for confidentiality. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/content/dam/en-zz/Solutions/about-us/documents/NVIDIA_Anti-Harassment_Discrimination_Policy-Sep-2020.pdf))

- The Anti‑Harassment Policy says NVIDIA will “strive to conduct a prompt, thorough and impartial investigation” of complaints, and that all complaints will be documented and tracked. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/content/dam/en-zz/Solutions/about-us/documents/NVIDIA_Anti-Harassment_Discrimination_Policy-Sep-2020.pdf))

- The Anti‑Harassment Policy states NVIDIA will handle complaints “promptly and confidentially to the extent possible” and that it will take appropriate disciplinary action in a timely manner when policy violations are found. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/content/dam/en-zz/Solutions/about-us/documents/NVIDIA_Anti-Harassment_Discrimination_Policy-Sep-2020.pdf))

- The Anti‑Harassment Policy includes a clear “no retaliation” statement: employees will not be subject to retaliation for making a good‑faith report or for participating in an investigation, and alleged retaliation will be investigated. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/content/dam/en-zz/Solutions/about-us/documents/NVIDIA_Anti-Harassment_Discrimination_Policy-Sep-2020.pdf))

- NVIDIA’s public event Codes of Conduct (for events such as GTC and AI Days) explain how to report incidents at events and state that reports made during an event will be responded to within 24 hours and other reports in less than two weeks. These event pages show NVIDIA uses an anonymous third‑party hotline for reports. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/gtc/code-of-conduct/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s policies remind U.S. employees they may also file external complaints with the EEOC or state agencies (for example, California’s DFEH), and tell employees where to find that contact information. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/content/dam/en-zz/Solutions/about-us/documents/NVIDIA_Anti-Harassment_Discrimination_Policy-Sep-2020.pdf))

- NVIDIA’s policy documents note mandatory training: the Anti‑Harassment Policy requires all employees to take interactive harassment‑prevention training. NVIDIA posts its Code of Conduct and related policy documents publicly in multiple languages. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/content/dam/en-zz/Solutions/about-us/documents/NVIDIA_Anti-Harassment_Discrimination_Policy-Sep-2020.pdf))

---

## Point 6 - Question 5

**Do wages and benefits meet or exceed area and industry standards, or is profitability dependent on below-standard compensation?**

### Research Findings

- Company name: NVIDIA Corporation (ticker NVDA). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Fiscal year 2025 median (typical) employee total compensation: $301,233. Fiscal year 2025 CEO (Jensen Huang) total compensation: $49,866,251. CEO-to-median pay ratio: 166 to 1. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Number of employees (end of fiscal 2025): about 36,000 people in 38 countries. Of those, about 27,100 worked in research & development and about 8,900 worked in sales, marketing, operations, and administrative roles. The company states about 82% of its workforce is technical. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Fiscal year 2025 total revenue: $130.5 billion. Total operating expenses: $16,405 million. Operating income: $81,453 million. The company says operating-expense increases were driven by higher compensation and benefits (including stock-based compensation). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Stock-based compensation expense (FY2025): $4,737 million total. Breakdown included about $3,423 million in research & development, $1,136 million in sales, general & administrative, and $178 million in cost of revenue. Aggregate unearned (future) stock‑based compensation as of Jan 26, 2025: $11.6 billion (to be recognized over about 2.2 years). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Using the company’s reported numbers: stock‑based compensation ($4,737M) was about 28.9% of reported operating expenses ($16,405M) and about 3.6% of reported revenue ($130,497M) in FY2025. (Calculation based on company-reported figures.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- The company’s public filings say most employees receive equity awards (RSUs, PSUs, market‑based PSUs) when available and participate in the company’s employee stock purchase program. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s Employee Stock Purchase Plan (ESPP): purchases at a 15% discount, with a lookback feature and multi‑period offerings (example: 24‑month offering with four purchase periods). The public benefits pages describe ESPP terms and enrollment rules. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/benefits/money/espp/?utm_source=openai))

- Reported employee benefits (public company pages and filings): multiple medical plan options, employer retirement/401(k) programs in the U.S., health savings account contributions, parental and caregiver leave programs, family‑building support (fertility, adoption, surrogacy), tuition reimbursement, flexible time‑off policies, company‑wide rest days each quarter, and other well‑being programs. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/benefits/?utm_source=openai))

- Reported employee turnover (overall) in fiscal 2025: 2.5% (company‑reported). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Local (area) wage context — San Jose‑Sunnyvale‑Santa Clara, CA (May 2024 BLS): mean hourly wage for the broader “computer and mathematical” occupational group was $97.71 per hour; mean annual wage for software developers in that area was about $234,540 (May 2024). ([bls.gov](https://www.bls.gov/regions/west/news-release/2025/occupationalemploymentandwages_sanjose_20250501.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Industry wage context — U.S. semiconductor and other electronic component manufacturing (NAICS 3344) example from BLS industry data: an earlier BLS industry table (May 2020 industry‑specific OEWS) lists the industry’s overall annual mean wage at about $75,750 (industry averages vary widely by occupation and have different dates/methods). ([bls.gov](https://www.bls.gov/oes/2020/may/naics4_334400.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Company statement about compensation practice: NVIDIA describes its compensation program as “pay for performance” and says a substantial portion of executive and employee pay is equity‑based to align employees with shareholder value; the company also reports using third‑party pay analyses for internal pay reviews. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Company disclosure of equity-related cash effects and actions in FY2025: the company reported $34.0 billion in share repurchases in fiscal 2025 (repurchases can offset dilution from equity awards and affect share counts). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

Sources (selected filings and public pages):
- NVIDIA 2025 Proxy Statement (Schedule 14A) — pay ratio and median compensation. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
- NVIDIA Annual Report on Form 10‑K for fiscal year 2025 — employee counts, workforce breakdown, revenue, operating expenses, stock‑based compensation notes, turnover. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))
- NVIDIA public benefits pages and ESPP description. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/benefits/?utm_source=openai))
- U.S. Bureau of Labor Statistics — San Jose‑Sunnyvale‑Santa Clara area occupational wages (May 2024) and national/industry OEWS tables. ([bls.gov](https://www.bls.gov/regions/west/news-release/2025/occupationalemploymentandwages_sanjose_20250501.htm?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 6 - Question 6

**Does top management show a consistent sense of responsibility toward ordinary employees—for example, by avoiding mass layoffs prompted solely by short-term profit swings and by fostering dignity and inclusion in the workplace?**

### Research Findings

Search date: October 7, 2025.

Facts (each line is a single factual item; sources are listed at the end of that item):

- Nvidia’s headcount grew substantially from 2020 to 2025. 2020 ≈ 13,775 employees; 2023 ≈ 26,196; 2024 ≈ 29,600; fiscal 2025 ≈ 36,000. ([stockanalysis.com](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/nvda/employees/?utm_source=openai))

- Nvidia’s public annual reports and 10‑K filings describe the company as hiring many technical staff; in fiscal 2024 the company said about 22,200 employees worked in research and development and 7,400 in sales/operations; in fiscal 2025 the filing reported about 27,100 in R&D and 8,900 in sales/operations. ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/BC239FE0177447E4FEEA5C8C389B6E280A4BAD98?utm_source=openai))

- Nvidia’s public filings and investor materials say the company uses restricted stock units (RSUs) and performance stock units (PSUs) to pay and retain staff. The company’s standard RSU vesting schedules include multi‑year schedules (commonly a four‑year pattern with ~25% after one year then quarterly vesting). PSUs also typically vest over multi‑year schedules. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/R13.htm?utm_source=openai))

- In April 2024 Nvidia gave employees an extra equity award reported in the press as a one‑time “special Jensen grant” worth an additional ~25% of annual equity refreshers; reports said the extra awards were scheduled to vest over four years. ([businessinsider.com](https://www.businessinsider.com/nvidia-jensen-huang-stock-boost-employees-special-grant-2024-4?utm_source=openai))

- Nvidia’s public statements about acquisitions have included explicit promises about jobs. When Nvidia bought Mellanox in 2020, company leadership publicly said they did not plan layoffs at Mellanox and intended to keep employees. ([blogs.nvidia.com](https://blogs.nvidia.com/blog/invest-in-mellanox/?utm_source=openai))

- Nvidia’s long history includes at least one early, large staff reduction: public histories note that in 1996 Jensen Huang cut more than half of the company’s staff (reducing headcount from ~100 to ~40) as part of a business turnaround. ([en.wikipedia.org](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nvidia?utm_source=openai))

- Nvidia’s 2024 and 2025 public reports and its careers/diversity pages state commitments to diversity, inclusion, and “pay parity.” The company lists programs such as employee resource groups, external partnerships with diversity organizations, diversity recruiting efforts, manager training, and tracking of parity in retention, promotions and pay. The company’s public pages say it has “achieved pay parity for the past several years.” ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-eu/about-nvidia/careers/diversity-and-inclusion/?utm_source=openai))

- Nvidia’s public filings and reports provide workforce demographic numbers. For example, the company reported in fiscal 2024 roughly 79% male, 20% female, 1% not declared globally, and reported that about 6% of its U.S. workforce identified as Black or Hispanic/Latino. ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/BC239FE0177447E4FEEA5C8C389B6E280A4BAD98?utm_source=openai))

- Nvidia publicly describes a flexible work approach and employee wellbeing policies in filings and reports. For example, the company’s filings and FY reports mention flexible work options and company time‑off policies (the 10‑K and related reports reference programs to support balance and employee recharge days). ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/BC239FE0177447E4FEEA5C8C389B6E280A4BAD98?utm_source=openai))

- Nvidia’s corporate foundation and volunteer programs have high employee participation numbers in recent years. FY24 and FY25 foundation reports say tens of thousands of volunteer hours and sizable employee donation and matching programs (for example, FY24: ~40% employee participation and ~$16M donated; FY25: ~35% participation and larger totals reported). ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/es-la/foundation/reports/?utm_source=openai))

- External employee review sites and employer‑ranking lists show strong employee ratings for Nvidia in recent years. Glassdoor listings and Nvidia’s press posts cite high overall ratings, high CEO approval scores, and placements on Glassdoor “best” lists (e.g., Glassdoor Best Employers and Best‑Led Companies). Glassdoor category scores cited on public pages include strong marks for culture, pay, and diversity. ([glassdoor.com](https://www.glassdoor.com/Reviews/NVIDIA-work-life-balance-Reviews-EI_IE7633.0%2C6_KH7%2C24.htm?utm_source=openai))

- News and company reports from 2023–2025 show Nvidia expanding hiring in some regions (for example, additional hires in China in 2024) even while facing regulatory scrutiny in some markets; Reuters reported Nvidia hiring in Beijing in 2024 and noted an investigation in China about competition concerns. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/technology/artificial-intelligence/nvidia-steps-up-hiring-china-focus-ai-driven-cars-bloomberg-news-reports-2024-12-12/?utm_source=openai))

- I searched public news archives, Nvidia’s filings, NLRB summaries, and major labor‑organizing campaign trackers through October 7, 2025 and did not find major, widely reported union‑certification votes, large‑scale NLRB unfair‑labor‑practice cases, or major public labor strikes listing Nvidia as the employer through that date. (This is a statement about what public records and news articles showed in the searches I ran.) ([nlrb.gov](https://www.nlrb.gov/cases-decisions/weekly-summaries-decisions/summary-of-nlrb-decisions-for-week-of-october-21-25-2024?utm_source=openai))

- Public interviews and news stories record comments by Nvidia’s CEO Jensen Huang about employee management. Huang has been quoted saying he prefers to develop employees rather than fire them and has used phrases reported in multiple outlets (for example, variations of “I don’t like giving up on people” and “I’d rather ‘torture them into greatness’” in public remarks and interviews). ([benzinga.com](https://www.benzinga.com/startups/24/09/40692021/nvidia-ceo-jensen-huang-will-push-employees-to-their-limits-but-is-reluctant-to-let-them-go-ill-tort?utm_source=openai))

Sources used (selected): SEC / company filings and proxy materials; Nvidia corporate newsroom and diversity pages; Nvidia Foundation annual reports; Glassdoor and Nvidia blog posts; Macrotrends employee counts; Business Insider / Reuters / Business press coverage; press accounts of the Mellanox acquisition; public historical summaries. Specific source links used above are cited inline with each fact.

---

### Point 7 Criterion

Does the company have a long-range outlook in regard to profits?

## Point 7 - Question 1

**Does the company consistently seek the lowest possible price from vendors, or are there documented instances in which it is willing to pay above-contract costs in order to keep a dependable supply chain and build goodwill for the future?**

### Research Findings

- In NVIDIA’s public SEC filings (10‑K and 10‑Q), the company says it "has paid premiums and provided deposits to secure future supply and capacity." ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000124/nvda-20240428.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s filings show a line item called "Prepaid supply and capacity agreements" of about $2.9 billion on the balance sheet (for example, $2,927 million as of October 29, 2023). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581023000227/nvda-20231029.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s quarterly notes state the company "places non‑cancellable inventory orders for certain products in advance of our historical lead times" and that doing so can increase product costs. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA disclosed specific charges related to these supply commitments: in one quarter it recorded roughly $473 million, and in another quarter roughly $348 million, in cost of revenue for inventory purchase obligations in excess of demand, supplier charges and penalties for cancellations or under‑utilization. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581023000227/nvda-20231029.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Multiple industry press reports from late December 2023 say NVIDIA made large upfront/advance payments (hundreds of millions of dollars each) to HBM memory makers SK Hynix and Micron to secure future memory supply. These reports cite industry sources and supplier agreements. ([apps.digitimes.com](https://apps.digitimes.com/news/a20231227PD212/nvidia-sk-hynix-micron-hbm-supply.html?utm_source=openai))

- News reports (July 2025) say NVIDIA placed large, follow‑on orders with TSMC (for example, a reported order for 300,000 H20 chips) as demand and market conditions changed. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/world/china/nvidia-orders-300000-h20-chips-tsmc-due-robust-china-demand-sources-say-2025-07-29/?utm_source=openai))

- Public statements by NVIDIA’s CEO Jensen Huang in mid‑2024 indicate he has expressed support for TSMC charging higher prices for advanced manufacturing and packaging, saying the price increases reflect the value delivered. ([businessinsider.in](https://www.businessinsider.in/tech/news/nvidia-is-making-a-ton-of-money-now-main-supplier-tsmc-may-charge-jensen-huang-more-for-chips-/articleshow/110869201.cms?utm_source=openai))

- Trade and tech outlets have quoted NVIDIA communications and filings saying the company may "pay premiums and provide deposits to secure normal and incremental future supply and capacity" and that such actions have increased product costs in the past. ([tomshardware.com](https://www.tomshardware.com/news/tsmc-collects-huge-prepayments?utm_source=openai))

- Industry coverage documents cases where NVIDIA worked closely with suppliers (TSMC, SK Hynix, Micron, Samsung) on capacity and timing, including supplier investments and timetable changes to meet NVIDIA demand. These accounts come from Reuters, CNBC, and semiconductor trade press reporting on supplier cooperation and capacity commitments. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/technology/nvidias-huang-asked-sk-hynix-bring-forward-supply-hbm4-chips-by-6-months-sks-2024-11-04/?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 7 - Question 2

**When regular customers face unexpected difficulties, does the company incur additional effort and expense to assist them, even if that lowers profit on the specific transaction, in order to deepen the relationship and enhance long-term returns?**

### Research Findings

- NVIDIA sells dedicated enterprise support. Customers can open support cases 24/7 through an Enterprise Support portal and contact NVIDIA by phone. Enterprise support includes technical help, warranty checks, and case tracking. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-eu/support/enterprise/?utm_source=openai))

- For high-end systems (DGX), NVIDIA provides enterprise-grade support that can include remote hardware and software help, on-site engineers to replace field-replaceable parts, advanced return material authorizations (RMA/ARMAs), and options for a Technical Account Manager or site reliability engineers. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/data-center/dgx-support/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA offers advisory and professional services. These services send NVIDIA experts or partner experts to help customers plan, optimize, and deploy AI projects — for example, helping move models from prototype to production and giving tailored guidance for customers’ specific needs. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/support/enterprise/advisory-services/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA runs partner programs and ecosystems (the NVIDIA Partner Network) so customers can get help from trained system integrators, cloud partners, and service providers. These partners provide design, implementation, and ongoing services for NVIDIA-based solutions. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/about-nvidia/partners/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA runs the Inception startup program that gives startups free training credits, cloud credits from partners, and preferred pricing on some NVIDIA hardware and software. The program is free to join and provides these resources to help early-stage customers grow. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/startups/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s product and support offerings are presented as paid tiers or entitlements (some support is included with purchases; other support is sold separately or through partners). Enterprise support entitlements may be included with an initial purchase or purchased later from NVIDIA or authorized partners. ([docs.nvidia.com](https://docs.nvidia.com/enterprise-support-and-services-user-guide/nvidia-enterprise-support-overview/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s public filings say the company is investing in cloud, software, and services and that these new business models “may incur significant costs and may not achieve any significant revenue.” The same filings note the company has reduced average selling prices in the past because of channel pricing programs and other factors. (This shows NVIDIA recognizes it sometimes gives pricing or makes investments that affect near-term profit.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- NVIDIA publishes customer case examples and joint programs with large systems integrators and consultancies (for example, partnerships with Accenture and others) that aim to help end customers deploy NVIDIA technology at scale. These programs involve joint engineering, training, and deployment work by NVIDIA and partners. ([newsroom.accenture.com](https://newsroom.accenture.com/news/2024/accenture-and-nvidia-lead-enterprises-into-era-of-ai?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 7 - Question 3

**Can you identify clear examples where management deliberately curtailed maximum immediate profit to secure greater overall profits over a period of years (e.g., pricing policies, warranty extensions, or service commitments)?**

### Research Findings

- Ticker NVDA = NVIDIA Corporation (company name shown on the company’s SEC filings and annual reports). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm?utm_source=openai))

- In May 2021 NVIDIA added "Lite Hash Rate" (LHR) to new GeForce RTX 30-series gaming cards to cut their efficiency at mining the Ethereum cryptocurrency. NVIDIA said the change was to make more cards available to gamers rather than crypto miners. ([blogs.nvidia.com](https://blogs.nvidia.com/blog/lhr/?utm_source=openai))

- In February–March 2021 NVIDIA introduced a separate product line called "CMP" (Cryptocurrency Mining Processor). CMP cards were sold through partners and were aimed only at miners (no graphics), separating miner demand from the gaming product line. ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2021/02/18/nvidia-cryptocurrency-mining-processor-for-ether-announced.html?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA reported total CMP product revenue for 2021 and the CMP business was a small share of total company revenue (example reported CMP revenue: about $550 million for fiscal 2021, a small fraction of overall revenue that year). ([bitcoinethereumnews.com](https://bitcoinethereumnews.com/crypto/nvidia-crypto-mining-processor-revenue-slumps-77-to-24m-in-q4-2021/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA created CUDA (its parallel computing software platform) and released the CUDA SDK publicly in 2007. CUDA and related libraries (toolkits that let programmers run work on NVIDIA GPUs) were distributed so developers could build on NVIDIA hardware rather than paying per-use fees. This helped build a large developer base that uses NVIDIA GPUs and software. ([docs.nvidia.com](https://docs.nvidia.com/cuda/archive/12.9.0/cuda-c-programming-guide/index.html?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA publishes and supports many free or broadly available developer libraries (for example cuDNN, TensorRT and other CUDA libraries) on its developer site; these software investments give developers tools for NVIDIA GPUs. ([docs.nvidia.com](https://docs.nvidia.com/cudnn/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA runs the free "Inception" program for AI startups. The program gives startups training, developer tools, partner offers, cloud credits, and preferred pricing on some NVIDIA products; membership costs nothing. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/startups/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA sells enterprise software (NVIDIA AI Enterprise) with multi-year subscription and perpetual-license options that include multi-year support. Some high-end GPUs are sold with several years of AI software subscription included (example: certain H100 models include a five‑year NVIDIA AI Enterprise subscription). ([docs.nvidia.com](https://docs.nvidia.com/ai-enterprise/planning-resource/licensing-guide/latest/licensing.html?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s research and development (R&D) spending is large and has grown quickly: the company reported R&D expenses of $8,675 million for fiscal year 2024 and $12,914 million for fiscal year 2025 (figures pulled from its filings). These R&D expenses reduce near-term profit but fund product and software development for future years. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA advertises long-term software maintenance options for enterprise customers (for example, “long-term branch maintenance” and support options up to multi-year branches for NVIDIA AI Enterprise), which provide ongoing fixes and updates over years rather than only short-term patches. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-eu/data-center/products/ai-enterprise/faq/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA has explicitly said (in its public communications) that measures such as LHR were taken to “get more GeForce cards at better prices into the hands of gamers,” stating an aim to shift some short-term demand away from miners and toward its target consumer market. ([blogs.nvidia.com](https://blogs.nvidia.com/blog/lhr/?utm_source=openai))

- Public reporting and company filings show CMP/mining-focused sales were not a large, lasting revenue stream for NVIDIA (CMP revenue rose and fell across quarters in 2021 and was described as a small portion of total revenue in filings). ([bitcoinethereumnews.com](https://bitcoinethereumnews.com/crypto/nvidia-crypto-mining-processor-revenue-slumps-77-to-24m-in-q4-2021/?utm_source=openai))

---

### Point 8 Criterion

Does the management talk freely to investors about its affairs when things are going well AND when troubles occur?

## Point 8 - Question 1

**Do earnings-call transcripts of the company show forthright acknowledgment of problems and underperformance when they happen, or are difficult topics avoided or minimized?**

### Research Findings

Company: NVIDIA Corporation (ticker: NVDA).

Facts from earnings calls, in simple language (each item cites the source):

- May 28, 2025: NVIDIA said the U.S. told it a license was needed to export its H20 chip to China. The company took a $4.5 billion charge for unsellable H20 inventory and said it could not ship $2.5 billion of H20 sales that it had expected. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-First-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- On that same May 28, 2025 call, NVIDIA said the lost H20 sales would reduce near-term China revenue and that about $8 billion of planned H20 orders for the next quarter had to be scrapped. ([ae.marketscreener.com](https://ae.marketscreener.com/quote/stock/NVIDIA-CORPORATION-57355629/news/Transcript-NVIDIA-Corporation-Q1-2026-Earnings-Call-May-28-2025-50094557/?utm_source=openai))

- On the May 28, 2025 call Jensen Huang (CEO) said the China market was “effectively closed to U.S. industry” because of export controls, and he criticized the export rules as damaging U.S. market position. (reported in the earnings coverage and transcript). ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2025/05/28/nvidia-ceo-hammers-chip-controls-that-effectively-closed-china-.html?utm_source=openai))

- In 2018–2019 (following the cryptocurrency mining boom and bust), NVIDIA’s calls and filings noted a sharp fall in crypto-related GPU demand and the company recorded a charge (reported as about $57 million) for prior-generation parts tied to that drop. The company described channel inventory as a near-term headwind but said it did not change long-term fundamentals. ([nasdaq.com](https://www.nasdaq.com/articles/nvidia-corporation-nvda-q3-2019-earnings-conference-call-transcript-2018-11-16?utm_source=openai))

- At multiple calls (example: Q4 2023) management said some cloud customers “paused … to recalibrate their build plans” and described part of a slowdown as a “timing issue,” meaning they attributed weaker near-term sales to customers shifting the timing of orders rather than to permanent loss of demand. ([fool.com](https://www.fool.com/earnings/call-transcripts/2023/02/22/nvidia-nvda-q4-2023-earnings-call-transcript//?utm_source=openai))

- In several calls about supply and manufacturing (example: Q2 2024), NVIDIA said its supply partners were ramping capacity, described complex multi-part supply chains, and stated it expected supply to increase each quarter through the following year. These remarks explain shortages as production and ramping issues. ([finance.yahoo.com](https://finance.yahoo.com/news/nvidia-corporation-nasdaq-nvda-q2-151348854.html?utm_source=openai))

- In the May 2025 reporting and related call, NVIDIA quantified how export rules affected guidance: management said reported guidance would have been about $8 billion higher if not for lost China sales, and provided adjusted vs. non-adjusted gross-margin and EPS figures showing the financial impact of the H20 charge. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-First-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Transcript examples (publicly posted by Seeking Alpha, Nasdaq, Motley Fool, Marketscreener and others) show executives answering analyst questions on topics such as channel inventory, product pull-ins/push-outs, supply chain timing, China demand, and export-control impacts; the transcripts record both specific dollar effects (charges, lost shipments) and management language that frames those problems as either discrete events or timing-related. ([seekingalpha.com](https://seekingalpha.com/article/4222728-nvidia-corp-nvda-ceo-jen-hsun-huang-on-q3-2018-results-earnings-call-transcript?utm_source=openai))

- In more recent quarters (2024–2025), calls and press releases show NVIDIA distinguishing product lines and regions (for example, reporting data-center growth in the U.S. vs. weakness in China) and naming specific causes (customer pauses, export licensing changes, or supply constraints) when discussing revenue swings. These statements include numerical segment results (e.g., data-center revenue figures) alongside explanations. ([nasdaq.com](https://www.nasdaq.com/articles/nvidia-nvda-q2-2024-earnings-call-transcript?utm_source=openai))

- Media reports and analyst coverage of the calls (CNBC, Business Insider, Investopedia, The Guardian and others) summarize the same call details and quote management lines criticizing export policy or describing write-downs and lost shipments; these contemporaneous reports track how the company communicated the issues to investors and the public. ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2025/05/28/nvidia-ceo-hammers-chip-controls-that-effectively-closed-china-.html?utm_source=openai))

(End of factual items.)

---

## Point 8 - Question 2

**Are negative developments at the company disclosed through 8-K filings and press releases with sufficient context, or are such disclosures delayed, vague, or overly optimistic?**

### Research Findings

- What a Form 8‑K is and its timing rule:
  - Form 8‑K is a U.S. SEC form companies must use to tell the public about important events that happen between regular reports. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/rules-regulations/staff-guidance/compliance-disclosure-interpretations/exchange-act-form-8-k?utm_source=openai))
  - For most events, companies must file the Form 8‑K within four business days after the event. There are some exceptions (for example, certain Regulation FD items). ([hklaw.com](https://www.hklaw.com/en/insights/publications/2004/08/reminder-new-form-8k-requirements-with-accelerated?utm_source=openai))

- How Nvidia uses 8‑K filings and press releases:
  - Nvidia files many 8‑K reports on EDGAR. Its 8‑K filings often list press releases and related materials as exhibits (for example, company earnings press releases appear as Exhibit 99.1 and related CFO commentary as Exhibit 99.2). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000021/0001045810-25-000021-index.html?utm_source=openai))
  - Nvidia posts press releases on its investor relations site and those same press releases are often attached to the company’s 8‑K filings. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2024/NVIDIA-Blackwell-Platform-Arrives-to-Power-a-New-Era-of-Computing/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- The wording Nvidia uses in press releases:
  - Nvidia press releases typically include “forward‑looking” language that says future results may differ because of risks, and they point readers to the company’s SEC reports for details about risks. This language appears in Nvidia press releases tied to product announcements. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2024/NVIDIA-Blackwell-Platform-Arrives-to-Power-a-New-Era-of-Computing/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Example: reports about a Blackwell GPU production issue (media reports and Nvidia statements)
  - Media reports in early August 2024 said Nvidia’s next‑generation “Blackwell” AI chips faced a design problem and possible shipment delays. These reports cited anonymous sources. ([investopedia.com](https://www.investopedia.com/nvidia-stock-plummets-on-reported-delay-of-its-new-ai-chip-amid-global-sell-off-8690166?utm_source=openai))
  - Nvidia responded publicly with statements on its investor site and on earnings calls. Nvidia’s investor press material described a mask change to improve yields and said production ramp was scheduled for the fourth quarter, and company executives discussed fixes on an earnings call. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2024/NVIDIA-Blackwell-Platform-Arrives-to-Power-a-New-Era-of-Computing/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))
  - Reuters later reported (October 23, 2024) that Nvidia’s CEO said the Blackwell design flaw had been fixed and described the production status. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/technology/artificial-intelligence/nvidias-design-flaw-with-blackwell-ai-chips-now-fixed-ceo-says-2024-10-23/?utm_source=openai))

- Regulatory and litigation history that relate to disclosure practices:
  - In May 2022 the SEC issued an order finding that Nvidia did not adequately disclose that cryptomining helped drive large increases in its “gaming” revenue in fiscal 2018; Nvidia agreed to a cease‑and‑desist order and to pay $5.5 million, without admitting or denying the SEC’s findings. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/newsroom/press-releases/2022-79?utm_source=openai))
  - A long‑running shareholder class action that alleges disclosure problems related to past crypto‑era revenue has continued in the courts; U.S. news reports in late 2024 and early 2025 describe appellate and Supreme Court filings and rulings in that matter. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/legal/us-supreme-court-tosses-case-involving-securities-fraud-suit-against-nvidia-2024-12-11/?utm_source=openai))
  - In 2025 there were reports and shareholder inquiries about whether U.S. export controls were being circumvented for sales of Nvidia chips into China; at least one law firm announced an investor investigation in March 2025 citing news coverage. ([prnewswire.com](https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/nvda-investors-have-opportunity-to-join-nvidia-corporation-fraud-investigation-with-the-schall-law-firm-302392298.html?utm_source=openai))

- Examples showing how Nvidia places press material in SEC filings:
  - Nvidia’s February 26, 2025 and May 28, 2025 8‑K filings on EDGAR include linked press releases and CFO commentary as exhibit files (EX‑99.1 and EX‑99.2). The EDGAR filing pages list those exhibits and the Item numbers (for example, Item 2.02: Results of Operations and Financial Condition). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000021/0001045810-25-000021-index.html?utm_source=openai))

- Statements on the public record about disclosure controls and risk topics:
  - Nvidia’s SEC filings (10‑K / 8‑K excerpts) describe a variety of risks that could force disclosure, including supply chain disruptions, security incidents, and regulatory matters; the filings state that certain incidents may require notification to customers, regulators, or investors. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

Sources (selected):
- SEC guidance and rule summaries on Form 8‑K and the four‑business‑day rule. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/rules-regulations/staff-guidance/compliance-disclosure-interpretations/exchange-act-form-8-k?utm_source=openai))
- Nvidia 8‑K filings and EDGAR index pages showing press release exhibits and Item numbers (examples: filings dated 2025‑02‑26, 2025‑05‑28). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000021/0001045810-25-000021-index.html?utm_source=openai))
- Nvidia investor press release for the Blackwell platform (investor.nvidia.com). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2024/NVIDIA-Blackwell-Platform-Arrives-to-Power-a-New-Era-of-Computing/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))
- News reports about Blackwell delay reports (The Information / outlets reporting in August 2024) and later company statements / Reuters report. ([investopedia.com](https://www.investopedia.com/nvidia-stock-plummets-on-reported-delay-of-its-new-ai-chip-amid-global-sell-off-8690166?utm_source=openai))
- SEC press release and order about the 2022 enforcement action and $5.5M penalty related to cryptomining disclosures. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/newsroom/press-releases/2022-79?utm_source=openai))
- News reports and legal summaries about the shareholder class action and related appellate/Supreme Court activity. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/legal/us-supreme-court-tosses-case-involving-securities-fraud-suit-against-nvidia-2024-12-11/?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 8 - Question 3

**In MD&A or investor presentations, does the company address business risks, operational challenges, or strategy setbacks with meaningful detail?**

### Research Findings

- The ticker NVDA is NVIDIA Corporation. (Form 10‑K for fiscal year ended Jan 26, 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- NVIDIA’s MD&A is in Item 7 of its 2025 Form 10‑K (Management’s Discussion and Analysis of Financial Condition and Results of Operations). The filing compares fiscal 2025 to prior years and shows revenue, margins, and operating results tables. (Form 10‑K, Item 7, fiscal year ended Jan 26, 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- The MD&A and Risk Factors state that NVIDIA relies on third‑party foundries (for example TSMC and Samsung) to make its chips, and on contract manufacturers (for example Hon Hai/Foxconn, Wistron, Fabrinet) for assembly, testing and packaging. The company says its supply chain is mainly concentrated in the Asia‑Pacific region. (Form 10‑K, Business and Risk Factors / Item 1 and Item 7). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- The MD&A and Risk Factors state competition and rapid technology change are material risks; NVIDIA lists key competitive factors such as performance, product breadth, software support, manufacturing capability, and pricing. (Form 10‑K, Risk Factors and Business discussion). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- The MD&A identifies inventories as a critical accounting estimate. It explains how management makes judgments about excess or obsolete inventory and lists situations that can cause excess inventory: changes in demand, new product introductions, incorrect demand forecasts, ordering lead times, government regulations, and competitive actions. (Form 10‑K, Critical Accounting Estimates — Inventories). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- In the quarter ended Apr 27, 2025, NVIDIA reported total inventories of $11,333 million and disclosed large inventory provisions and excess inventory purchase obligation liabilities tied to certain products. The filing shows line‑item amounts for raw materials, work in process, finished goods, and excess inventory obligations. (Quarterly filing / balance sheet as of Apr 27, 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm?utm_source=openai))

- On April 9, 2025, the U.S. government informed NVIDIA that a license was required to export its H20 products to China. NVIDIA recorded a charge of $4.5 billion in Q1 fiscal 2026 tied to H20 excess inventory and purchase obligations because demand for H20 diminished after the licensing requirement. The company said it was unable to ship an additional $2.5 billion of H20 in the quarter. (Company Q1 disclosure and press release, May 28, 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm?utm_source=openai))

- The Apr 27, 2025 filing breaks the $4.5 billion charge into components: a $1.9 billion inventory provision for H20 product inventory and $2.6 billion recorded as excess inventory purchase obligation charges (part of the overall $4.5B). The filing shows how these amounts were recorded in cost of revenue and in liabilities. (Quarterly filing, Apr 27, 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s subsequent filings and releases note additional movements related to H20 provisions: for example, a $180 million provision release in a later quarter when some H20 inventory was sold outside China, and overall provisions and releases that affected gross margin percentages for the periods disclosed. (Subsequent quarterly disclosure). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm?utm_source=openai))

- The MD&A and Risk Factors explicitly warn that failure to estimate customer demand accurately has led, and could lead, to mismatches between supply and demand, which can cause excess inventory or write‑downs. (Form 10‑K, Item 1A Risk Factors and MD&A inventory discussion). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- NVIDIA’s MD&A discloses customer concentration metrics for recent periods (for example, three direct customers accounted for 27%, 18% and 12% of accounts receivable as of Apr 27, 2025), showing dependence on a small number of large customers in some periods. (Quarterly filing, Apr 27, 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm?utm_source=openai))

- The MD&A includes a Liquidity and Capital Resources section with cash and marketable securities totals and the company’s view of liquidity: as of Jan 26, 2025, NVIDIA reported $43.2 billion in cash, cash equivalents, and marketable securities and stated it believed it had sufficient liquidity to meet operating requirements for at least the next twelve months and the foreseeable future. (Form 10‑K, Liquidity and Capital Resources). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- The Risk Factors and MD&A note legal and intellectual property risks, including that litigation or adverse IP rulings could cause significant costs, injunctive relief, or require licensing; the 10‑K refers readers to the Legal Proceedings note for specifics. (Form 10‑K, Item 1A Risk Factors; Item 3 Legal Proceedings; Notes to Financial Statements). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- NVIDIA’s investor news and event materials (earnings releases, conference presentations, GTC/CES/GTC keynotes and investor event pages) describe strategic initiatives (Blackwell platform, Spectrum‑X networking, Omniverse, DRIVE, partnerships, AI factory efforts) and also include standard forward‑looking cautionary language that those initiatives are subject to the same risks listed in SEC filings (competition, manufacturing reliance, market acceptance, etc.). (Investor news releases and event pages, 2024–2025). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Blackwell-Ultra-AI-Factory-Platform-Paves-Way-for-Age-of-AI-Reasoning/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- The company’s public disclosures direct readers to its SEC filings (Form 10‑K and Form 10‑Q) for fuller detail on risks, contingencies, and the financial effects of events discussed in investor presentations and press releases; the 10‑K and quarterly filings contain the detailed numeric and narrative disclosures cited above. (Form 10‑K and quarterly filings; investor relations statements). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

---

## Point 8 - Question 4

**Is the tone of investor communication consistent across good and bad quarters, or does the company shift toward evasive language when performance weakens?**

### Research Findings

- Aug 8, 2022 — NVIDIA announced preliminary results for its second quarter of fiscal 2023. The company said preliminary revenue was about $6.70 billion, below its prior outlook of $8.10 billion, and that the shortfall was "primarily driven by weaker Gaming revenue." ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-preliminary-financial-resultsfor-second-quarter-fiscal-2023?utm_source=openai))

- Aug 24, 2022 — On the Q2 FY2023 earnings call, CEO Jensen Huang said: "Our expectations, our plans, were higher," and added that the company "did have to just take a rightsizing of that inventory." (earnings call transcript). ([fool.com](https://www.fool.com/earnings/call-transcripts/2022/08/24/nvidia-nvda-q2-2023-earnings-call-transcript/?utm_source=openai))

- Aug 23, 2023 — NVIDIA reported record revenue of $13.51 billion for second quarter fiscal 2024. In the company press release, CEO Jensen Huang said, in part, "A new computing era has begun." ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2023/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Second-Quarter-Fiscal-2024/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Aug 28, 2024 — For second quarter fiscal 2025 NVIDIA reported record revenue of $30.0 billion. The press release quoted CEO Jensen Huang saying, "Hopper demand remains strong, and the anticipation for Blackwell is incredible." ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2024/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Second-Quarter-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Feb 26, 2025 — NVIDIA reported revenue of $39.3 billion for fourth quarter and fiscal 2025. The press release described record Data Center revenue and quoted CEO Jensen Huang saying, in part, "Demand for Blackwell is amazing." ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2025?utm_source=openai))

- Across multiple quarterly press releases, NVIDIA gives numerical forward guidance in a standard form, e.g. "Revenue is expected to be $32.5 billion, plus or minus 2%." (example: Q3 FY2025 outlook in the Q2 FY2025 release). This is presented as a single-point forecast with a small percentage range. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2024/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Second-Quarter-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- The company has used the word "preliminary" in at least one public release (Aug 8, 2022) when reporting a large shortfall and followed that with a full earnings release and an earnings call several weeks later. The preliminary release identified the main cause (weaker Gaming sell-in) and the follow-up call discussed inventory rightsizing and margin effects. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-preliminary-financial-resultsfor-second-quarter-fiscal-2023?utm_source=openai))

- In the Aug 8, 2022 preliminary release, CFO Colette Kress said the quarter included "significant charges" tied to earlier purchase commitments and described actions like slowing operating expense growth while continuing share buybacks. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-preliminary-financial-resultsfor-second-quarter-fiscal-2023?utm_source=openai))

- Press releases for quarters with strong results (examples above from Aug 23, 2023; Aug 28, 2024; Feb 26, 2025) consistently use words such as "record" (to describe revenue or Data Center revenue) and highlight product names (H100, Hopper, Blackwell) and large customer deployments. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2023/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Second-Quarter-Fiscal-2024/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- The August 24, 2022 earnings call transcript includes executives answering analyst questions about inventory, gross margin and product mix, with executives naming specific causes (inventory rightsizing, mix shift away from high-end GPUs) rather than only using generic statements. ([fool.com](https://www.fool.com/earnings/call-transcripts/2022/08/24/nvidia-nvda-q2-2023-earnings-call-transcript/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA press releases and earnings materials routinely present segment-level numbers (for example, Gaming revenue, Data Center revenue) alongside company-wide totals, and they note year-over-year and quarter-over-quarter percentage changes for those segments. Examples: Q2 FY2024, Q2 FY2025, Q4 FY2025 releases. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2023/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Second-Quarter-Fiscal-2024/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- When a large variance occurred (Aug 2022), NVIDIA first issued a short "preliminary" release with the size of the miss and a brief cause, then held the formal earnings call and full release later in the month to provide more detail. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-preliminary-financial-resultsfor-second-quarter-fiscal-2023?utm_source=openai))

- Examples of short direct quoted phrases from official releases/calls:
  - "primarily driven by weaker Gaming revenue." (preliminary Q2 FY2023 release). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-preliminary-financial-resultsfor-second-quarter-fiscal-2023?utm_source=openai))
  - "Our expectations, our plans, were higher." (CEO Jensen Huang, Q2 FY2023 call). ([fool.com](https://www.fool.com/earnings/call-transcripts/2022/08/24/nvidia-nvda-q2-2023-earnings-call-transcript/?utm_source=openai))
  - "Hopper demand remains strong." (CEO Jensen Huang, Q2 FY2025 release). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2024/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Second-Quarter-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))
  - "Demand for Blackwell is amazing." (CEO Jensen Huang, Q4 FY2025 release). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2025?utm_source=openai))

(All quotes and figures come from NVIDIA press releases and the Q2 FY2023 earnings call transcript cited above.) ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-preliminary-financial-resultsfor-second-quarter-fiscal-2023?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 8 - Question 5

**During analyst calls or investor events, does management answer critical or difficult questions directly, or tend to deflect or avoid them?**

### Research Findings

- NVIDIA holds a live, company-hosted conference call after each quarterly earnings release. The call includes prepared remarks by executives followed by a live Q&A session that is limited to financial analysts and institutional investors. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Sets-Conference-Call-for-Fourth-Quarter-Financial-Results/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA also holds investor-focused events (for example, GTC and a separate financial-analyst Q&A at GTC). Those events include public keynotes and a separate Q&A/webcast for analysts or investors. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-ceo-jensen-huang-and-industry-visionaries-to-unveil-whats-next-in-ai-at-gtc-2025?utm_source=openai))

- Executives often speak directly and at length on technical and market topics during prepared remarks and the Q&A. Full earnings-call transcripts show Jensen Huang and CFO Colette Kress answering detailed questions about product ramps, architectures, and data-center demand. (Example: May 24, 2023 and May 29, 2024 earnings-call transcripts). ([seekingalpha.com](https://seekingalpha.com/article/4607199-nvidia-corp-nvda-q1-2024-earnings-call-transcript?utm_source=openai))

- Management has publicly given direct, specific comments about U.S. export controls and the effect on NVIDIA’s China business. For example, on an earnings call Jensen Huang said the China market was “effectively closed” and later called export controls a “failure.” These remarks were repeated in public interviews and news coverage in 2025. ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2025/05/28/nvidia-ceo-hammers-chip-controls-that-effectively-closed-china-.html?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA disclosed large financial hits tied to China export rules and unsold H20 inventory. Public filings and company statements reported a multi-billion-dollar charge related to H20 chips (reports mention figures such as $4.5 billion and $5.5 billion in different company announcements and news reports). ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2025/04/15/nvidia-says-it-will-record-5point5-billion-quarterly-charge-tied-to-h20-processors-exported-to-china.html?msockid=2aa612602f8969a733d504202e4c6814&utm_source=openai))

- At times executives have declined to give precise, public answers about the timing or scale of certain customer orders or specific commercial details. News coverage of March–July 2025 events recorded managers saying they would not give definitive order counts or exact timing for resuming shipments to China. ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2025/07/16/as-nvidia-gets-a-lifeline-in-china-jensen-huang-goes-on-the-charm-offensive-in-beijing.html?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s public filings (SEC 10‑K / 10‑Q) note ongoing regulatory and competition inquiries and state that the company receives broad requests for information from competition regulators; the filings list these requests and related risks. These filings make regulatory scrutiny and related disclosure limits a documented, formal risk. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Company press releases and investor pages show that NVIDIA provides written CFO commentary ahead of some earnings calls and posts webcasts and replays on its investor site. This creates multiple public channels (written, audio, video) where executives state facts and then answer analyst questions. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Sets-Conference-Call-for-Fourth-Quarter-Financial-Results/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Independent news transcripts and earnings-call transcripts show examples of executives answering technical questions with detailed explanations (for example, explanations of product architectures, supply-chain complexity, and how specific GPUs fit customer use cases). These transcripts record verbatim answers from CEO and CFO across multiple quarters. ([seekingalpha.com](https://seekingalpha.com/article/4607199-nvidia-corp-nvda-q1-2024-earnings-call-transcript?utm_source=openai))

- Academic research on earnings calls (published analyses) documents that managers across large firms sometimes give “non-responses” or avoid direct answers, and that such non-responses can be identified and measured; this provides a general method researchers use to classify whether answers are direct or evasive. (See a 2025 working paper that develops a measure of manager non-responses in earnings calls.) ([arxiv.org](https://arxiv.org/abs/2505.18419?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 8 - Question 6

**When prior goals or commitments of the company are missed, does management openly revisit them and explain the causes, or do they go unmentioned?**

### Research Findings

- On August 8, 2022 NVIDIA issued a preliminary results statement saying its revenue would be about $6.70 billion versus a prior outlook of $8.10 billion, and that the shortfall was “primarily driven by weaker than forecasted Gaming revenue.” ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-preliminary-financial-resultsfor-second-quarter-fiscal-2023?utm_source=openai))

- On the August 24, 2022 earnings call NVIDIA’s finance chief said the revenue shortfall was caused by “macroeconomic headwinds” that reduced consumer demand for gaming products; management discussed the reasons on the call. ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2022/08/24/nvidia-reports-slowing-growth-after-earlier-warning.html?utm_source=openai))

- On August 28, 2024 NVIDIA’s CEO publicly confirmed a delay in the ramp of its next‑generation “Blackwell” chips into the fourth quarter and described design/timing changes and ramp issues when answering analysts’ questions. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/technology/nvidia-forecasts-third-quarter-revenue-above-estimates-2024-08-28/))

- On May 28, 2025 NVIDIA’s official results and prepared commentary said the company was told on April 9, 2025 that a U.S. export license would be required for its H20 products to China; NVIDIA reported a $4.5 billion charge for excess H20 inventory and said it was unable to ship about $2.5 billion of H20 revenue as a result. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-First-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- The May 28, 2025 earnings call transcript shows NVIDIA executives (CEO Jensen Huang and CFO Colette Kress) discussed the H20 export‑license issue and its financial effects during prepared remarks and the analyst Q&A. ([seekingalpha.com](https://seekingalpha.com/article/4790673-nvidia-corporation-nvda-q1-2026-earnings-call-transcript?utm_source=openai))

- In NVIDIA’s February 26, 2025 quarterly results and investor commentary, management said it was accelerating production of the new Blackwell systems, explained that early ramp costs affected near‑term gross margins, and gave forward guidance while describing the ramp plan. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2025?utm_source=openai))

- Academic research on earnings‑call behavior finds that managers sometimes give “non‑responses” to analyst questions, and that such non‑responses are linked to greater analyst forecast uncertainty; this is a general finding about some firms’ calls, not a statement about NVIDIA alone. ([arxiv.org](https://arxiv.org/abs/2505.18419?utm_source=openai))
