### Point 9 Criterion

Are there other aspects of the business, somewhat peculiar to the industry involved, which make the company outstanding relative to the competition?

## Point 9 - Question 1

**Are there other aspects of the business, somewhat peculiar to the industry involved, which will give the investor important clues as to how outstanding the company may be in relation to its competition? In industries where leasing is material (e.g., retail), do the company’s lease terms and related occupancy costs compare favorably with peers, indicating superior site selection and negotiation skill? Does the company maintain lower credit losses or demonstrate more disciplined credit policies than competitors, suggesting more effective risk control? Where insurance is a significant expense, are total insurance costs (relative to sales or assets) materially lower than industry averages, reflecting stronger control of accidents, damage, and waste? If the company is a large firm, does a strong but not over-relied-upon patent portfolio broaden profit margins? For smaller firms with unique products, is the patent protection sufficiently broad to deter larger rivals? Does continuous product or process improvement, rather than static patent protection alone, provide the primary competitive edge? Based on the company’s business model, operating environment, or sector characteristics, are there any other distinctive aspects (e.g., logistics, supply chain strategy, regulatory positioning, customer switching costs) that may offer a significant competitive advantage or disadvantage? Provide all relevant information found ONLY; don’t answer the question directly and do not add any context in your final output other than the information presented.**

### Research Findings

- NVIDIA designs chips but does not own large factories; it uses outside foundries and assembly partners to make and package its products. ([secinfo.com](https://www.secinfo.com/dvT9t.g5.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA relies heavily on Taiwan Semiconductor Manufacturing Company (TSMC) for advanced wafer making and on advanced packaging technologies such as TSMC’s CoWoS to build its high-end AI modules. ([prnewswire.com](https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/nvidia-ceo-reiterates-solid-partnership-with-tsmc-302096782.html?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA uses very high‑bandwidth memory (HBM) and advanced multi‑chip packaging for its top data‑center GPUs; those memory and packaging steps are special supply points that can limit output and raise cost. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2024/NVIDIA-Blackwell-Platform-Arrives-to-Power-a-New-Era-of-Computing/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA is a “fabless” company (it outsources wafer fabrication, assembly, testing and packaging), which lowers capital spending but makes it dependent on outside suppliers for capacity and yields. ([secinfo.com](https://www.secinfo.com/dvT9t.g5.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA has bought companies to add networking and storage technology; the 2020 acquisition of Mellanox brought high‑speed interconnects (InfiniBand and Ethernet) into NVIDIA’s product mix. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-to-acquire-mellanox-for-6-9-billion?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA sells integrated systems (for example DGX and HGX racks and SuperPODs) that combine its GPUs and networking hardware; those complete systems are sold to large cloud and enterprise customers. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2024/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-First-Quarter-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA maintains a large patent portfolio across graphics, AI, and related computing areas; public analyses report many thousands of patents and active applications worldwide. ([iiprd.com](https://www.iiprd.com/nvidia-patent-portfolio-exemplary-landscape-overview/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s patent filings concentrate in computing and image/graphics classifications (for example CPC classes G06F and G06T), showing focus on graphics and AI processing methods. ([iiprd.com](https://www.iiprd.com/nvidia-patent-portfolio-exemplary-landscape-overview/?utm_source=openai))

- Public patent analyses show NVIDIA filing activity rose in recent years and that the company uses continuation filings to extend and broaden protection around core technologies. ([patent-i.com](https://patent-i.com/report/us_en/applicant/NVIDIA%20CORPORATION/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA supplies a full software stack (CUDA, cuDNN, TensorRT, NVIDIA AI Enterprise, NIMs, Omniverse, SDKs) that many developers and companies use to run AI and graphics workloads. ([docs.nvidia.com](https://docs.nvidia.com/hpc-sdk/archive/25.5/hpc-sdk-release-notes/index.html?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s CUDA software platform has millions of developers using it; several news and industry reports cite a developer base in the multiple‑millions, which creates switching costs for customers who build code around NVIDIA libraries. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/technology/behind-plot-break-nvidias-grip-ai-by-targeting-software-2024-03-25/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA has moved to a faster product cadence, saying it will produce new chip architectures on about a one‑year rhythm, increasing the pace of hardware refreshes and related software updates. ([theverge.com](https://www.theverge.com/2024/5/22/24162860/nvidia-ai-chip-every-year-blackwell-rubin?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s product roadmap includes regular new GPU architectures (examples: Ampere, Hopper, Blackwell, and later Rubin/Vera Rubin), each aimed at higher AI performance or energy efficiency. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-hopper-architecture-the-next-generation-of-accelerated-computing?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s business mix is heavily weighted to data‑center AI systems; recent company reports show the bulk of revenue coming from data‑center products. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-First-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Market research and news reports indicate NVIDIA holds a very large share of the high‑end AI GPU market and add‑in‑board GPU shipments in recent quarters (various analyst and industry group estimates put NVIDIA’s share in the high‑percent range for key segments). ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2024/06/02/nvidia-dominates-the-ai-chip-market-but-theres-rising-competition-.html?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s “full‑stack” approach (chips, networking from Mellanox, and software) is used by hyperscalers and large AI customers, who often buy whole systems rather than single chips. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-to-acquire-mellanox-for-6-9-billion?utm_source=openai))

- U.S. export controls and other government rules have restricted shipments of some high‑performance NVIDIA data‑center products to China and other markets; the company reported related inventory charges tied to restricted products. ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2023/10/17/us-bans-export-of-more-ai-chips-including-nvidia-h800-to-china.html?utm_source=openai))

- Government and competition authorities in multiple jurisdictions have opened probes or sought information about NVIDIA’s market practices; U.S. authorities (Justice Department) and Chinese regulators (SAMR) have investigated or opened inquiries in recent years. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/legal/nvidia-hit-with-subpoena-us-justice-department-bloomberg-news-reports-2024-09-03/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s supply chain has seen tightness at advanced packaging and memory steps; industry reports and company statements note that packaging capacity and memory availability have been limiting factors for shipment volumes. ([trendforce.com](https://www.trendforce.com/news/2024/01/31/news-nvidia-expands-advanced-packaging-supply-chain-with-intels-inclusion-diverting-orders-from-tsmc?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s sales strategy includes long‑term purchase commitments and supply agreements; the company reports significant purchase obligations and prepaid supply arrangements in its SEC filings and annual reports. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000104/nvda-20240514.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA has expanded offerings beyond raw chips into networking, software, full systems, and industry platforms (for example automotive DRIVE and cloud/enterprise AI platforms), broadening where it competes and earns revenue. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2024/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-First-Quarter-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Analysts and industry reports show competitors (AMD, Intel, Google TPUs and custom chips) are developing alternatives, and some customers and consortia are working on software or standards to make switching away from NVIDIA easier. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/technology/behind-plot-break-nvidias-grip-ai-by-targeting-software-2024-03-25/?utm_source=openai))

- Public records and news show NVIDIA has pursued and sometimes abandoned large acquisitions (for example the attempted Arm purchase was terminated after regulatory challenges), which affected strategic options for owning broader CPU or architecture technology. ([ftc.gov](https://www.ftc.gov/news-events/news/press-releases/2022/02/statement-regarding-termination-nvidia-corps-attempted-acquisition-arm-ltd?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA emphasizes continuous product and software updates (new GPU generations, SDK updates, and platform releases) as part of its competitive approach rather than relying only on existing patents. ([theverge.com](https://www.theverge.com/2024/5/22/24162860/nvidia-ai-chip-every-year-blackwell-rubin?utm_source=openai))

---

### Point 10 Criterion

In the foreseeable future will the growth of the company NOT require sufficient equity financing so that the larger number of shares then outstanding will largely cancel the existing stockholders’ benefit from this anticipated growth?

## Point 10 - Question 1

**What level of external capital will be needed over the next several years based on management’s disclosed capital-expenditure plans, acquisitions, and growth initiatives? Given current cash, projected operating cash flow, and prudent borrowing capacity (using industry-standard leverage norms), could these needs be met without issuing new equity?**

### Research Findings

- Cash and short-term investments (company report): NVIDIA reported cash and cash equivalents of $11,639 million and marketable securities of $45,152 million, for total cash + marketable securities of $56,791 million as of July 27, 2025. This is the company’s liquid money and easily-sold investments. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))

- Shorter-term cash figure (company report): NVIDIA reported cash and cash equivalents of $8,589 million and marketable securities of $34,621 million, for total cash + marketable securities of $43,210 million as of January 26, 2025. ([fintel.io](https://fintel.io/doc/sec-nvidia-corp-1045810-10k-2025-february-26-20145-3358))

- Operating cash flow (recent twelve months and interim): NVIDIA reported net cash provided by operating activities of $64,089 million for fiscal year 2025 (year ended Jan 26, 2025). For the six months ended July 27, 2025, the company reported net cash provided by operating activities of $42,779 million. These numbers show cash generated by running the business. ([fintel.io](https://fintel.io/doc/sec-nvidia-corp-1045810-10k-2025-february-26-20145-3358))

- Capital spending (company actuals): NVIDIA reported purchases related to property and equipment and intangible assets of $3,236 million for fiscal 2025 (year ended Jan 26, 2025). For the six months ended July 27, 2025, purchases related to property and equipment and intangible assets were $3,122 million. These are the company’s reported capital expenditures (money spent to buy buildings, equipment, and similar items). ([fintel.io](https://fintel.io/doc/sec-nvidia-corp-1045810-10k-2025-february-26-20145-3358))

- Investing and financing cash flows (recent): NVIDIA’s net cash used in investing activities was $(20,421) million for fiscal 2025 and $(12,343) million for the six months ended July 27, 2025. Net cash used in financing activities was $(42,359) million for fiscal 2025 and $(27,386) million for the six months ended July 27, 2025. These show how much cash left the company for investments and for financing (buybacks, debt repayments, dividends). ([fintel.io](https://fintel.io/doc/sec-nvidia-corp-1045810-10k-2025-february-26-20145-3358))

- Total reported debt (company report): NVIDIA’s net long-term carrying amount of debt was $8,463 million as of January 26, 2025, and $8,466 million as of July 27, 2025. The company’s listed debt maturities by time bucket are shown in its filings. This is the company’s formal interest-bearing debt on the balance sheet. ([fintel.io](https://fintel.io/doc/sec-nvidia-corp-1045810-10k-2025-february-26-20145-3358))

- Commercial paper program (company report): NVIDIA has a $575 million commercial paper program and reported no commercial paper outstanding as of July 27, 2025 and as of January 26, 2025. This is a short-term borrowing facility the company can use if needed. ([fintel.io](https://fintel.io/doc/sec-nvidia-corp-1045810-10k-2025-february-26-20145-3358))

- Net cash position (simple subtraction of company numbers): 
  - As of July 27, 2025: cash + marketable securities $56,791M minus debt $8,466M = net cash ≈ $48,325M. 
  - As of January 26, 2025: cash + marketable securities $43,210M minus debt $8,463M = net cash ≈ $34,747M. 
  These are company cash and debt numbers minus one another; a positive result means the company held more cash and marketable investments than interest-bearing debt. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))

- Purchase and supply commitments (company report): As of July 27, 2025, NVIDIA disclosed future purchase and other commitments totalling $45,774 million (this includes inventory purchase and long-term supply/capacity agreements and other contract commitments). As of January 26, 2025, inventory purchase and long-term supply and capacity obligations were reported as $30.8 billion, plus other non-inventory obligations of $14.3 billion. These are contractual cash commitments the company has to pay in future periods. ([br.advfn.com](https://br.advfn.com/noticias/EDGAR2/2025/artigo/96714207?utm_source=openai))

- Reported acquisitions and acquisition cash flows (company report and media): NVIDIA reported acquisitions, net of cash acquired, of $1,007 million for fiscal 2025, and $677 million for the six months ended July 27, 2025. Separately, Reuters reported NVIDIA closed the Run:ai acquisition for $700 million (deal closed Dec 30, 2024). These are cash amounts the company has used to buy companies or equity stakes. ([fintel.io](https://fintel.io/doc/sec-nvidia-corp-1045810-10k-2025-february-26-20145-3358))

- Recent strategic investment commitments announced by NVIDIA (company press releases): 
  - NVIDIA and OpenAI announced a strategic partnership (Sept 22, 2025) under which NVIDIA said it intends to invest up to $100 billion in OpenAI progressively as each gigawatt of OpenAI deployment is completed. This is a company-announced possible future investment tied to joint deployments. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/OpenAI-and-NVIDIA-Announce-Strategic-Partnership-to-Deploy-10-Gigawatts-of-NVIDIA-Systems/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))
  - NVIDIA and Intel announced a collaboration (Sept 18, 2025) in which NVIDIA will invest $5 billion in Intel common stock as part of the collaboration announcement. This is an announced equity investment commitment. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-and-Intel-to-Develop-AI-Infrastructure-and-Personal-Computing-Products/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))
  - NVIDIA announced a strategic partnership with HUMAIN (May 13, 2025) and related Saudi Arabia deployments (May–Sept 2025 press materials) where partners plan AI data-center capacity of up to 500 megawatts and multi-phase GPU deployments (e.g., first phase described as an 18,000-GB300 system). These initiatives involve customer/partner capital plans and likely large system deployments using NVIDIA hardware. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/HUMAIN-and-NVIDIA-Announce-Strategic-Partnership-to-Build-AI-Factories-of-the-Future-in-Saudi-Arabia/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Share repurchases and authorizations (company report and filings): NVIDIA repurchased $33,706 million of common stock in fiscal 2025. During the first half of fiscal 2026 the company repurchased $24,200 million; in the second quarter alone it repurchased $9,700 million (67 million shares), as reported in the company filings for the half-year ended July 27, 2025. NVIDIA’s Board approved an additional $60.0 billion share-repurchase authorization on August 26, 2025. These are large cash uses the company has disclosed for returning capital to shareholders. ([fintel.io](https://fintel.io/doc/sec-nvidia-corp-1045810-10k-2025-february-26-20145-3358))

- Unrecognized tax and other contingent liabilities (company report): NVIDIA reported unrecognized tax benefits of $2.9 billion (including interest and penalties) recorded in non-current income tax payable as of July 27, 2025. This is a potential future cash requirement if tax positions are settled unfavorably. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Debt coupon costs (company report): NVIDIA reported interest expense of $247 million for fiscal 2025. This is the company’s reported cash interest cost for the year on its debt. ([fintel.io](https://fintel.io/doc/sec-nvidia-corp-1045810-10k-2025-february-26-20145-3358))

- Earnings and EBITDA components (company report and simple sum): For fiscal 2025 NVIDIA reported net income of $72,880 million, income tax expense of $11,146 million, depreciation and amortization of $1,864 million, and interest expense of $247 million. Adding those items gives an approximate EBITDA of $86,137 million for fiscal 2025 (EBITDA = net income + interest + taxes + depreciation & amortization). EBITDA is a rough measure of operating earnings before some non-cash and financing items. ([fintel.io](https://fintel.io/doc/sec-nvidia-corp-1045810-10k-2025-february-26-20145-3358))

- Company-stated near-term outlook items (management guidance): For the third quarter of fiscal 2026 (outlook given Aug 27, 2025) NVIDIA expected revenue of $54.0 billion ±2%. The company expected GAAP operating expenses of about $5.9 billion and non-GAAP operating expenses of about $4.2 billion for that quarter, and said full-year fiscal 2026 operating expense growth would be in the high-30% range. These are management’s reported near-term revenue and expense outlook numbers. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-second-quarter-fiscal-2026?utm_source=openai))

- Company capital-return statement in filings: NVIDIA’s filings state the company believes it had sufficient liquidity to meet operating requirements for at least the next twelve months and thereafter for the foreseeable future, describing cash, cash equivalents and marketable securities and operating cash flow as primary liquidity sources (company statements in 10-Q and 10-K). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))

- Industry / credit-metric context for leverage (third-party sources): 
  - S&P Global reported the median debt-to-EBITDA ratio for investment-grade companies was about 2.69 (a broad market median used by credit analysts). This gives a reference point for leverage commonly seen in rated, investment-grade firms. ([spglobal.com](https://www.spglobal.com/market-intelligence/en/news-insights/articles/2024/12/total-debt-for-rated-us-companies-reaches-new-high-86683893?utm_source=openai))
  - Financial-education sources state common rule-of-thumb ranges: net-debt-to-EBITDA below 1 is generally considered very low leverage, while net-debt-to-EBITDA above about 3 is often viewed as higher leverage and may raise credit concerns; acceptable ranges vary by industry and ratings agency. These are commonly cited benchmarks used by analysts and lenders. ([investopedia.com](https://www.investopedia.com/terms/n/net-debt-to-ebitda-ratio.asp?utm_source=openai))

- Examples of loan covenant / leverage thresholds observed in practice (external example): Some company loan agreements and covenants set maximum net-debt-to-EBITDA or debt-to-EBITDA thresholds in the range of about 3.5x (example from a public company loan covenant disclosure). This shows one type of limit that lenders sometimes impose; actual covenant levels differ by borrower and deal. ([mundurek.com](https://mundurek.com/article/net-debt-ebitda-ratio?utm_source=openai))

- Material long-term supply or capacity obligations and timing (company report): NVIDIA reported purchase obligations by year (as of July 27, 2025) with large near-term amounts (for example, about $30,930 million shown for fiscal 2026 excluding the first half of fiscal 2026 in the company’s commitments table). These scheduled purchase obligations represent cash the company has contractually agreed to pay over coming years. ([br.advfn.com](https://br.advfn.com/noticias/EDGAR2/2025/artigo/96714207?utm_source=openai))

- Recent announced product and infrastructure programs (company releases): NVIDIA has announced large product and infrastructure programs (examples: Blackwell data-center product shipments, Spectrum-X networking, Omniverse deployments, and the Boston Accelerated Quantum Research Center). These initiatives are described in company press releases and imply continued investment in product development, partnerships, and customer deployments. The press releases give program descriptions and intended scope (technical and deployment scale), but not always full dollar budgets. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-first-quarter-fiscal-2026?utm_source=openai))

(End of facts.)

## Point 10 - Question 2

**Does management indicate—by statement or past practice—that it will exhaust reasonable debt capacity before turning to equity, and has it historically followed this approach?**

### Research Findings

- NVDA is the ticker for NVIDIA Corporation, a publicly listed company on the Nasdaq. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000118/forms-arsmay2025.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Management says the company has an active capital‑return program and that it is a key part of capital allocation. (Example: CFO Colette Kress: “Our capital return program continues to be a key element of our capital allocation strategy.”) ([ng.investing.com](https://ng.investing.com/news/transcripts/earnings-call-transcript-nvidia-beats-q1-2025-expectations-stock-up-43-1942255?utm_source=openai))

- The Board has repeatedly authorized very large share‑repurchase programs. On August 26, 2024 the Board approved an additional $50.0 billion in repurchase authority (no expiration). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000316/nvda-20241027.htm?utm_source=openai))

- The Board approved another large repurchase increase on August 26, 2025: an additional $60.0 billion, without expiration. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Second-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Recent repurchase activity (selected amounts reported by the company): fiscal year 2025 repurchases — 310 million shares for $34.0 billion; fiscal year 2024 repurchases — $9.7 billion; fiscal year 2023 repurchases — $10.04 billion. The company has described continuing plans to repurchase shares as it weighs market factors and other investment opportunities. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- The company started paying a regular cash dividend in 2024 and increased the quarterly amount in May 2024; cash dividends paid in fiscal 2025 totaled $834 million. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000124/nvda-20240428.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s filings state that the repurchase program is intended to offset dilution from shares issued to employees, and that repurchases may be suspended at management’s discretion. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA reports and discloses its access to external capital and says it “continuously evaluate[s] our liquidity and capital resources, including our access to external capital.” (Liquidity and capital resources section of its Form 10‑K / 10‑Q.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- The company has an active shelf registration that allows it to offer debt securities, common stock, preferred stock and other securities from time to time (automatic shelf registration statement filed May 28, 2025). ([d18rn0p25nwr6d.cloudfront.net](https://d18rn0p25nwr6d.cloudfront.net/CIK-0001045810/163ce92a-81bb-4200-84b0-1edceefdd719.html?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA has used the public debt market multiple times. It has issued unsecured senior notes across several years (examples include long‑dated notes such as 3.50% notes due 2050 and 3.70% notes due 2060) and the company’s filings list the outstanding note amounts and maturities. The notes are unsecured senior obligations and the filings describe the company’s compliance with covenants for those notes. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581023000175/nvda-20230730.htm?utm_source=openai))

- In earlier debt offerings (example: 2016 notes), NVIDIA stated it intended to use net proceeds for general corporate purposes, which included share repurchases and prefunding repayment of convertible notes. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-pricing-of-2-0-billion-notes-offering?utm_source=openai))

- At the end of the fiscal year reported in the 2025 filing (January 26, 2025), NVIDIA reported cash, cash equivalents and marketable securities of $43,210 million and reported net long‑term carrying amount of debt of $8,463 million (debt maturities schedule and related notes are disclosed in the filings). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- The company operates a $575 million commercial paper program for general corporate purposes but reported no commercial paper outstanding as of the January 26, 2025 filing date. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581023000227/nvda-20231029.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Shares outstanding have been broadly stable or reduced over recent years (quarterly share counts reported in public data show shares outstanding after the 2024 forward split remained roughly in the mid‑20 billion share range and have changed modestly quarter to quarter). ([macrotrends.net](https://macrotrends.net/stocks/charts/NVDA/nvidia/shares-outstanding?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA issues shares for employee compensation and issues small amounts of stock in acquisition‑related transactions; the filings show net share settlements for RSUs and specific small issuances tied to an acquisition. ([filings.assets.koyfin.com](https://filings.assets.koyfin.com/filings/52416c2a744598786274125b6494c6d7/1045810/000104581024000124/nvda-20240428.htm?utm_source=openai))

## Point 10 - Question 3

**Are there shelf registration statements, announced equity offerings, or other signals that material share issuance is planned within the foreseeable period? If so, what is the expected magnitude relative to the existing share count?**

### Research Findings

- NVIDIA filed a new shelf registration statement (Form S-3) with the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission on May 28, 2025. The prospectus for that shelf is dated May 28, 2025. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000118/forms-arsmay2025.htm))

- The May 28, 2025 prospectus says NVIDIA may sell, from time to time and in one or more offerings, any combination of securities including common stock (the company’s ordinary shares), preferred stock, depositary shares, debt securities, warrants, and stock purchase contracts or units. Each actual sale would be described in a separate prospectus supplement. (Plain meaning: the shelf lets the company issue shares or other securities later, but each specific sale needs its own supplement with details.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000118/forms-arsmay2025.htm))

- The May 28, 2025 shelf registration replaces NVIDIA’s prior registration statement from 2023. The new filing says the earlier (2023) registration will be terminated when the May 28, 2025 registration becomes effective. (Plain meaning: the company updated and renewed its shelf in 2025.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000118/forms-arsmay2025.htm))

- NVIDIA reported the number of shares of common stock outstanding as 24.4 billion as of February 21, 2025 (this same 24.4 billion figure is also reported as of May 23, 2025 in the company’s Form 10-Q). (Plain meaning: about 24.4 billion shares existed at those dates.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s Form 10-K for fiscal 2025 discloses that during fiscal year 2025 the company withheld about 59 million shares to cover taxes on restricted stock unit (RSU) vesting (net-share settlements). (Plain meaning: the company transferred about 59 million shares to itself to pay employee tax withholdings on stock awards in that fiscal year.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- The same Form 10-K discloses two small issuances in late 2024 related to acquired-company employees: 94,560 shares issued on December 6, 2024 and 205,110 shares issued on December 29, 2024 (both described as issuances in connection with acquisitions and not public offerings). (Plain meaning: the company issued a few hundred thousand shares to employees of acquired companies, not as a public offering.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- The May 28, 2025 prospectus states that any sale of securities under the shelf will be made only by means of a prospectus supplement that will describe the specific terms, amounts and timing of any particular offering. (Plain meaning: the shelf itself does not state how many shares will be sold; each sale needs a separate document with the exact numbers and timing.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000118/forms-arsmay2025.htm))

- I searched NVIDIA’s SEC filings and the company’s press releases through October 7, 2025 for a prospectus supplement or an SEC Form 8‑K by NVIDIA announcing a specific registered offering of common stock under the May 28, 2025 shelf; I did not find a filed prospectus supplement or an 8‑K by NVIDIA that announces a public offering of common stock under that May 28, 2025 shelf. (Plain meaning: the shelf is in place, but I found no SEC filing from NVIDIA that gives the exact terms and size of a public share sale under that shelf as of Oct 7, 2025.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000118/forms-arsmay2025.htm))

Sources and documents cited above:
- NVIDIA Form S-3 (shelf registration), prospectus dated May 28, 2025. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000118/forms-arsmay2025.htm))
- NVIDIA Form 10-K for fiscal year ended January 26, 2025 (shares outstanding and RSU withholding disclosures). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))
- NVIDIA Form 10-Q for quarter ended April 27, 2025 (shares outstanding as of May 23, 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm?utm_source=openai))
- NVIDIA investor press release / financial results page (for recent press releases reference). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-First-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

## Point 10 - Question 4

**After accounting for all outstanding options, warrants, convertibles, and any reasonably expected new equity, what is the estimated fully diluted share count, and how would this affect prospective per-share earnings and the economic benefit to current shareholders?**

### Research Findings

- Company identity and filings used: NVIDIA Corporation (ticker NVDA). Facts below come from NVIDIA’s public SEC filings: Annual Report on Form 10-K for fiscal year ended January 26, 2025, and Quarterly Reports on Form 10-Q for the periods ended April 27, 2025 and July 27, 2025, and NVIDIA’s 2025 proxy materials. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Basic shares outstanding (common stock) on NVIDIA’s 2025 meeting record date: 24,387,557,065 shares outstanding as of April 28, 2025. (This is the count of shares that existed and could vote on that date.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Shares outstanding reported in 10-Q filings near mid-2025:
  - As of May 23, 2025: about 24.4 billion shares outstanding. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm?utm_source=openai))
  - As of August 22, 2025: about 24.3 billion shares outstanding. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Weighted-average shares used in per-share (EPS) calculations (company’s GAAP figures):
  - Fiscal year ended Jan 26, 2025 — Basic weighted average shares: 24,555 million (i.e., 24.555 billion). Diluted weighted average shares: 24,804 million (24.804 billion). The reported dilutive impact from outstanding equity awards for that year was 249 million shares. (These are the company’s calculated “diluted” share counts that were used to compute GAAP diluted EPS for FY2025.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))
  - Quarter / six months ended Jul 27, 2025 — Basic and diluted weighted averages for the periods are reported (example: six months diluted weighted average = 24,571 million, with a dilutive impact of 167 million). (These show the more recent per-share denominators used by NVIDIA for interim EPS.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))

- Equity awards and “shares issuable” (stock awards that can become shares):
  - Number of securities to be issued upon exercise of outstanding options, warrants, and rights (aggregate reported as of Jan 26, 2025): 274,212,251 shares. This line in the equity plan table represents shares underlying outstanding RSUs/PSUs/rights (options were not outstanding). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - RSUs, PSUs and market-based PSUs outstanding (detailed movement): balance was 274 million shares as of Jan 26, 2025; during the period NVIDIA granted ~48 million, vested ~78 million, canceled/forfeited ~5 million, leaving a balance of ~239 million shares outstanding as of Jul 27, 2025. (This shows the recent count of unvested/unpaid stock awards that could convert into shares.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))
  - The company reported unearned stock‑based compensation tied to these awards of about $14.0 billion (aggregate future expense), expected to vest over a weighted average period (~2.2 years for RSUs/PSUs). (This indicates multi-year vesting that would convert to shares over time if awards vest.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))

- Stock options and similar instruments:
  - NVIDIA’s filings state the company “has not had any stock options outstanding since the end of Fiscal 2024.” (That means there were no outstanding stock options to exercise into shares as of the report date; outstanding share-convertible instruments are primarily RSUs/PSUs/other rights.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Employee Stock Purchase Plan (ESPP) and shares available under plans:
  - As of Jan 26, 2025, the number of shares remaining available for future issuance under equity compensation plans (aggregate of the 2007 Plan and ESPP) was 3,628,661,705 shares (about 3.629 billion). The company also reported that under the ESPP, up to ~3.38 million shares might be purchased in the then-current purchase period (this is limited by participant contribution and the IRS $25,000 limit). (This shows the pool of shares legally available to be issued in future awards or purchases.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Recent real issuances under equity plans (examples of how many new shares are actually issued):
  - In fiscal 2025 the company granted an aggregate of 82,467,905 shares under the 2007 Plan (counting PSUs at maximum). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - During fiscal 2025, employees purchased ~30,121,348 shares under the ESPP. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - During fiscal 2025, NVIDIA withheld approximately 59 million shares to cover tax obligations when RSUs vested (net‑settlement withholding). (Net settlement reduces how many new shares remain outstanding after an award vests.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Warrants, convertible debt, and other convertible securities:
  - NVIDIA’s debt disclosures list unsecured senior notes and other standard debt; the company’s equity-plan table shows the number of securities issuable on exercise of outstanding options/warrants/rights as 274,212,251 (see above). NVIDIA’s filings do not disclose any separate outstanding convertible notes or public warrants that would convert into common stock. (No convertible securities or public warrants are shown in the debt or equity plan notes in the 10-K / 10-Q disclosures.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Share repurchases and program authorizations (these reduce shares outstanding and offset dilution when executed):
  - On August 26, 2024, NVIDIA’s Board approved an additional $50 billion to its repurchase authorization (no expiration). In fiscal 2025 the company repurchased ~310 million shares for $34.0 billion. As of Jan 26, 2025, the company had remaining repurchase authorization (subject to specifications) of about $38.7 billion; as of Jul 27, 2025 the company reported remaining approximate dollar capacity of $14.7 billion under its program after repurchases in fiscal 2026 first half. NVIDIA repurchased 67 million shares in Q2 FY2026 (and 193 million shares in the first half of FY2026). (Share repurchases lower the number of shares outstanding when executed.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Company authorization to issue common stock (charter limits):
  - NVIDIA’s amended certificate of incorporation (post stock split) shows the company is authorized to issue up to 80,002,000,000 shares in total, of which 80,000,000,000 are common stock. (This is the legal ceiling on shares the company could issue without further charter amendments.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- How the company reports and treats dilution for EPS calculations (method used in filings):
  - NVIDIA computes diluted EPS using the treasury stock method and reports the dilutive impact of outstanding equity awards (for example, 249 million for fiscal 2025 and 167 million for the six months ended July 27, 2025). Anti‑dilutive awards (those that would reduce EPS if included) are excluded. (This explains which instruments the company already counts in its published “diluted” share totals.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Small recent equity issuances noted in filings:
  - The company reported issuing small numbers of shares in connection with acquisitions/employee grants (examples: 94,560 shares on Dec 6, 2024; 205,110 shares on Dec 29, 2024 — these were not public offerings). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Key numeric summary (from the company’s filings, simple numbers you can use to build a dilution calculation):
  - Basic shares outstanding (record-based counts around mid‑2025): ~24.3–24.4 billion shares. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Company-reported diluted weighted-average shares (used for FY2025 EPS): 24.804 billion (dilutive impact = +249 million). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))
  - Outstanding RSUs/PSUs and rights (amounts that can become shares): ~274.2 million (Jan 26, 2025 table) and reported balance of ~239 million outstanding RSU/PSU units as of Jul 27, 2025 after activity. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Shares available for future issuance under equity plans (as of Jan 26, 2025): ~3.6287 billion. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
  - Shares withheld for tax on RSU vesting in FY2025: ~59 million (net share settlement). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))
  - Repurchased shares in recent periods: FY2025 repurchases ~310 million shares; first half FY2026 repurchases ~193 million shares (Q2 FY2026 repurchases ~67 million). Board authorized an additional $50 billion repurchase capacity in Aug 2024 (remaining program capacity changed as repurchases occurred). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

(use these cited numbers to compute a fully diluted share count by adding outstanding shares plus shares issuable from awards and any other dilutive instruments; note the company’s own “diluted weighted average shares” figures already reflect the awards the company treated as dilutive under GAAP for the reported periods). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Locations in the filings where the above figures are found (to check or pull exact lines yourself):
  - FY2025 Form 10-K (NVIDIA Corporation) — Note 4 (Net Income Per Share) and Item 5 / Item 15 (equity plan tables, repurchases, RSU withholding). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))
  - Form 10-Q for quarter ended Jul 27, 2025 — equity award table, net income per share section showing recent diluted weighted averages and dilutive impacts. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm?utm_source=openai))
  - NVIDIA 2025 Proxy Statement (preliminary/proxy) — outstanding equity awards tables and charter/authorized shares language. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

(End of facts.)

### Point 11 Criterion

Does the company have a worthwhile operating profit margin?

## Point 11 - Question 1

**To consistently calculate and compare operating profit margins without inconsistency, YOU MUST USE the following standardized approach. THE MOST IMPORTANT PART OF YOUR RESEARCH IS THAT Begin by defining Operating Profit Margin as GAAP Operating Income divided by GAAP Operating Revenues, expressed as a percentage. These figures should come directly from a company’s audited financial statements—specifically the Consolidated Statement of Income in its Form 10-K or 10-Q. First, locate the Operating Income line item. It may appear as “Operating Income” or “Income from Operations.” Do not use “adjusted” or “non-GAAP” versions such as “operating earnings,” “core EBIT,” or “segment EBIT,” even if they are highlighted in earnings presentations or third-party sites. These adjusted metrics often exclude depreciation, hedge marks, impairments, or restructuring charges, and are not suitable for consistent peer comparison. Next, identify the Operating Revenues (sometimes labeled “Net Sales”) for the same fiscal period. Ensure that both operating income and revenue figures are taken from the same report and are stated in matching units (e.g., both in millions or thousands of dollars). Then compute the margin by dividing operating income by operating revenues and multiplying by 100 to get a percentage. Use this GAAP-based formula without adjustments. Even if the company experienced unusual events like asset sales, fuel hedging losses, or storm recovery costs, these should remain in the calculation. They may be discussed qualitatively as sources of volatility, but they must not be excluded from the margin formula. To compare margins across years or companies, repeat the exact same method using only fiscal-year GAAP data. Do not substitute trailing-twelve-month numbers or selectively adjusted periods. By applying this consistent definition—GAAP operating income divided by GAAP operating revenues without exclusions—you ensure that your operating margin comparisons are clean, comparable, and grounded in audited, standardized financial reporting. The point of the above approach is to provide the relevant information need to answer these questions, but do not actually answer them or include any context about your answer in your final output other than the information. What has been the company’s operating profit margin (operating income ÷ net sales) for each of the past five fiscal years, and what is the multi-year average? How does that margin rank versus direct industry peers over the same period (top tier, middle, or bottom)? During the most recent industry up-cycle and down-cycle, did the company’s margin fluctuate less sharply than lower-margin competitors (indicating structural strength) or more sharply (indicative of a marginal cost position)? If the current margin is narrow, do regulatory filings or management comments show that this is the result of deliberately elevated spending on R&D, sales promotion, or other growth investments rather than an entrenched cost disadvantage? Is there clear evidence—such as sustained cost leadership, pricing power, or proprietary products—that could enable the company to maintain or widen its margin over the long run?**

### Research Findings

Definition (use this GAAP formula only)
- Operating profit margin = (GAAP Operating Income ÷ GAAP Operating Revenues (Net sales)) × 100. Take both numbers from the Consolidated Statement(s) of Income in the company’s audited Form 10‑K (or the matching fiscal-period 10‑Q). Use the line labeled “Operating Income” or “Income from Operations.” Do not use adjusted/non‑GAAP operating measures. (Source: NVIDIA Form 10‑K filings — see citations below). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

NVIDIA (ticker: NVDA) — GAAP figures and computed margins (five fiscal years)
- Fiscal year definitions used below: NVIDIA fiscal year ends on the last Sunday in January. I list each fiscal year by its fiscal year‑end date (as shown in NVIDIA’s Form 10‑K).

1) Fiscal year ended January 26, 2025 (FY2025)
- GAAP Net sales (Revenue): $130,497 million. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))
- GAAP Operating Income (Income from operations): $81,453 million. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))
- Operating profit margin = 81,453 ÷ 130,497 = 62.45%. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

2) Fiscal year ended January 28, 2024 (FY2024)
- GAAP Net sales (Revenue): $60,922 million. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))
- GAAP Operating Income (Income from operations): $32,972 million. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))
- Operating profit margin = 32,972 ÷ 60,922 = 54.13%. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

3) Fiscal year ended January 29, 2023 (FY2023)
- GAAP Net sales (Revenue): $26,974 million. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581023000017/nvda-20230129.htm?utm_source=openai))
- GAAP Operating Income (Income from operations): $4,224 million. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581023000017/nvda-20230129.htm?utm_source=openai))
- Operating profit margin = 4,224 ÷ 26,974 = 15.66%. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581023000017/nvda-20230129.htm?utm_source=openai))

4) Fiscal year ended January 30, 2022 (FY2022)
- GAAP Net sales (Revenue): $26,914 million. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2022/?utm_source=openai))
- GAAP Operating Income (Income from operations): $10,041 million. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2022/?utm_source=openai))
- Operating profit margin = 10,041 ÷ 26,914 = 37.33%. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2022/?utm_source=openai))

5) Fiscal year ended January 31, 2021 (FY2021)
- GAAP Net sales (Revenue): $16,675 million. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2022/?utm_source=openai))
- GAAP Operating Income (Income from operations): $4,532 million. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2022/?utm_source=openai))
- Operating profit margin = 4,532 ÷ 16,675 = 27.17%. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2022/?utm_source=openai))

Multi‑year average (simple arithmetic mean of the five annual GAAP margins above)
- Average operating profit margin = (62.45% + 54.13% + 15.66% + 37.33% + 27.17%) ÷ 5 = 39.35%. (Computed from the GAAP figures cited above). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

Underlying GAAP operating‑expense and R&D facts (to assess whether narrow margins reflect elevated investment)
- Total GAAP operating expenses (R&D + SG&A) by fiscal year (from NVIDIA Consolidated Statements of Income / notes):
  - FY2025 total operating expenses: $16,405 million (Research & development: $12,914M; Sales, general & administrative: $3,491M). ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/5EBFB425AD1D43945A255B6E3A1E3927B06A7141?utm_source=openai))
  - FY2024 total operating expenses: $11,329 million (Research & development: $8,675M; Sales, general & administrative: $2,654M). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))
  - FY2023 total operating expenses: $11,132 million (R&D $7,339M; SG&A $2,440M; acquisition termination cost $1,353M recorded in FY2023). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581023000017/nvda-20230129.htm?utm_source=openai))
  - FY2022 total operating expenses: $7,434 million (R&D $5,268M; SG&A $1,940M). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2022/?utm_source=openai))
  - FY2021 total operating expenses: $5,864 million (R&D and SG&A breakdown in FY2021 consolidated statements). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2022/?utm_source=openai))

Unusual items, reserves, and specific charges disclosed in SEC filings (GAAP amounts, not adjustments)
- Inventory provisions and excess‑inventory purchase obligation items:
  - FY2025: Provisions for inventory and excess inventory purchase obligations totaled $3.7 billion; release of prior provisions totaled $689 million (net effect disclosed in 10‑K). ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/5EBFB425AD1D43945A255B6E3A1E3927B06A7141?utm_source=openai))
  - FY2024: Provisions/charge and releases disclosed as $2.2 billion of excess inventory purchase obligations and releases of $540 million (disclosed in FY2024/ FY2025 10‑K commentary). ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/5EBFB425AD1D43945A255B6E3A1E3927B06A7141?utm_source=openai))
- Q1 FY2026 (first quarter of fiscal 2026) charge disclosed in the Q1 2026 Form 10‑Q (quarter ended April 27, 2025): a $4.5 billion charge associated with H20 excess inventory/purchase obligations (reported in the quarter’s Condensed Consolidated Statements of Income and segment notes). This is a GAAP charge in the Q1 FY2026 10‑Q. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm))

Segment-level GAAP facts (useful to judge margin drivers)
- FY2025 segment revenue and operating income (Consolidated 10‑K / segment tables):
  - Compute & Networking revenue (FY2025): $116,117 million; Compute & Networking operating income (FY2025): $82,870 million (segment operating income as reported). ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/5EBFB425AD1D43945A255B6E3A1E3927B06A7141?utm_source=openai))
  - Graphics revenue (FY2025): $14,380 million; Graphics operating income (FY2025): $5,083 million (segment operating income as reported). ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/5EBFB425AD1D43945A255B6E3A1E3927B06A7141?utm_source=openai))

Selected management / regulatory statements in audited filings and earnings releases (direct quotes or GAAP facts)
- Management’s GAAP statements about demand and product ramp (examples from NVIDIA filings/press releases):
  - In the FY2025 Form 10‑K and FY2025 earnings release, management stated strong demand for Blackwell and large Data Center sales; the earnings release and 10‑K present the GAAP revenue and operating income figures above. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Fourth-Quarter-and-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))
- Management disclosure of R&D strategy and amounts:
  - FY2025 R&D expense (GAAP): $12,914 million (reported in the FY2025 10‑K). ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/5EBFB425AD1D43945A255B6E3A1E3927B06A7141?utm_source=openai))

GAAP sources (where the above numbers were taken from)

### Point 12 Criterion

Does the company have depth to its management—that is, a broad base of capable leaders, effective delegation, and a culture that develops and retains executive talent beyond one or two key individuals?

## Point 12 - Question 1

**Is there clear evidence of a formal succession plan for top management and a well-developed leadership bench that mitigates key-person risk?**

### Research Findings

- Jensen Huang is the company’s co‑founder, president and chief executive officer. He has led NVIDIA since he started the company in 1993. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/about-nvidia/board-of-directors/jensen-huang//?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s 2025 preliminary proxy was filed with the SEC for the June 25, 2025 annual meeting and describes the company’s board, its committees, and senior management in detail. The proxy identifies a Lead Independent Director role and says the CEO has “primary responsibility for the operational leadership and strategic direction of the Company.” ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- The proxy describes the Nominating and Corporate Governance Committee (NCGC). The NCGC’s listed duties include identifying and recommending director candidates, recommending committee assignments, assessing board performance, and reviewing corporate governance matters. The proxy notes the NCGC met three times in fiscal 2025 and that its agenda included “Board recruiting” among other topics. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- The 2025 proxy statement does not contain a section titled “Succession” or “Succession Planning” and does not present a named CEO successor in the proxy materials. (Source: NVIDIA’s 2025 proxy statement filed with the SEC.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Outside reporting and a 2025 biography of Jensen Huang state that the company has not publicly named a successor. The author Stephen Witt reports that when asked NVIDIA said it had no succession plan and quotes Huang as saying “I don’t have a successor.” ([penguinrandomhouse.com](https://www.penguinrandomhouse.com/books/757558/the-thinking-machine-by-stephen-witt/?utm_source=openai))

- Senior, long‑tenured executives and technical leaders at NVIDIA include (examples): Colette Kress — Executive Vice President and Chief Financial Officer; Debora Shoquist — Executive Vice President, Operations; Tim Teter — Executive Vice President, General Counsel and Secretary; and technical leaders such as Ian Buck (vice president responsible for CUDA and hyperscale/HPC work). These named executives appear on NVIDIA’s management pages and in company and press materials. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/governance/management-team/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- The proxy emphasizes active board oversight of risk management, regular executive sessions of independent directors, annual board and committee self‑assessments, and annual stockholder outreach — governance practices the company presents as supporting oversight of senior management. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Independent reporting has highlighted both NVIDIA’s deep technical bench (examples above) and concerns about centralization of decision‑making around Jensen Huang. Reviews of NVIDIA’s leadership note Huang’s direct oversight of many senior reports and raise questions about whether a formal, named succession plan has been made public. ([businessinsider.com](https://www.businessinsider.com/ian-buck-nvidia-moat-cuda-2025-6?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s investor and corporate web pages list current executive officers and board members by name and role; those pages provide the company’s official roster of senior leaders as of 2025. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/governance/management-team/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 12 - Question 2

**What are the tenure, turnover, and functional diversity of the top management team and board, and do these factors indicate stability and breadth of expertise?**

### Research Findings

Top management (named executive officers listed in NVIDIA’s 2025 proxy)
- Jen‑Hsun (Jensen) Huang — President and Chief Executive Officer. Founder of NVIDIA in 1993; has served as CEO and on the board since 1993 (about 32 years at the company as of 2025). Source: NVIDIA 2025 proxy. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
- Colette M. Kress — Executive Vice President and Chief Financial Officer. Joined NVIDIA in September 2013 (about 12 years at the company as of 2025). Source: NVIDIA bio and 2013 press release. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/bios/colette-kress?utm_source=openai))
- Ajay K. (Jay) Puri — Executive Vice President, Worldwide Field Operations. Joined NVIDIA in 2005 (about 20 years at the company as of 2025). Source: NVIDIA bio. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/bios/jay-puri?utm_source=openai))
- Debora Shoquist — Executive Vice President, Operations. Joined NVIDIA in 2007 and was named to her current role in 2009 (about 18 years at the company, and about 16 years in current role, as of 2025). Source: NVIDIA management page. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/about-nvidia/governance/management-team/debora-shoquist/?utm_source=openai))
- Timothy S. Teter — Executive Vice President, General Counsel and Secretary. Joined NVIDIA in January 2017 (about 8 years at the company as of 2025). Source: NVIDIA bio and 2017 press release. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/bios/tim-teter?utm_source=openai))
- (Proxy lists these five as the Fiscal 2025 NEOs: Huang, Kress, Puri, Shoquist, Teter.) Source: NVIDIA 2025 proxy. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

Board of directors (as reported in NVIDIA’s 2025 proxy; “Director Since” and short background)
- Number of director nominees up for election in 2025: 13. Source: NVIDIA 2025 proxy. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- Stephen C. Neal — Director since 2019 (≈6 years). Background: law and corporate governance (served as lead director). Source: proxy. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
- John O. Dabiri — Director since 2020 (≈5 years). Background: academic engineering / fluid mechanics and research. Source: proxy. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
- Aarti Shah — Director since 2020 (≈5 years). Background: information technology, digital transformation, and data sciences. Source: proxy. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
- Melissa B. Lora — Director since 2023 (≈2 years). Background: consumer business operations and finance. Source: proxy. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
- Ellen Ochoa — Director since 2024 (≈1 year). Background: aerospace, advanced technology, and STEM leadership (former NASA Johnson Space Center Director). Source: proxy. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

Board turnover and dates
- NVIDIA’s proxy states that, since 2020, the board “has brought in four new directors, and [had] the retirement of three directors.” Source: NVIDIA 2025 proxy (board narrative). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
- The four directors who joined in or after 2020 and are listed in the 2025 proxy: John O. Dabiri (2020), Aarti Shah (2020), Melissa B. Lora (2023), and Ellen Ochoa (2024). Each “Director Since” year is shown in the proxy. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

Functional backgrounds — short summary facts (from the 2025 proxy biographies)
- Technology / engineering / research / academia: Jensen Huang; John O. Dabiri; Persis Drell; Mark A. Stevens; Ellen Ochoa. (Proxy biographies show technical and industry experience for these directors.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
- Finance / accounting / financial community: A. Brooke Seawell; Melissa B. Lora; Tench Coxe; (proxy marks financial expertise and audit‑committee roles where applicable). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
- Legal / governance: Stephen C. Neal (legal counsel; governance experience). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
- Marketing / consumer / brand: Dawn Hudson; Melissa B. Lora (consumer operations + finance). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
- Information technology / data / digital transformation: Aarti Shah (long career in IT and digital roles). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
- Senior management / operations / semiconductor industry expertise: Robert K. Burgess; Harvey C. Jones; Mark A. Stevens (biographies describe senior operating roles and semiconductor/technology experience). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

Additional data points from official filings and company bios
- The proxy identifies the company’s Fiscal 2025 NEOs as: Jen‑Hsun Huang, Colette M. Kress, Ajay K. Puri, Debora Shoquist, and Timothy S. Teter. Source: NVIDIA 2025 proxy (Compensation Discussion & Analysis). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))
- Executive join dates and short bios (company pages / press releases): Colette Kress joined in September 2013; Jay Puri joined in 2005; Debora Shoquist joined in 2007; Tim Teter joined in January 2017. These join dates and role descriptions appear on NVIDIA’s official executive biography pages and NVIDIA press releases. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/bios/colette-kress?utm_source=openai))

(End of facts.)

## Point 12 - Question 3

**Does the company exhibit a consistent pattern of promoting from within, demonstrating its ability to develop executive talent internally?**

### Research Findings

- Jensen Huang co-founded NVIDIA and has been the company’s president and chief executive officer since he started the company in 1993. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/bios/jensen-huang?utm_source=openai))

- Debora Shoquist joined NVIDIA in 2007 as senior vice president of operations and was promoted to executive vice president of operations in 2009. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/bios/debora-shoquist?utm_source=openai))

- David Shannon joined NVIDIA as vice president and general counsel, became senior vice president and company secretary in 2005, was promoted to executive vice president in 2009, and became chief administrative officer in 2014. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-cao-david-shannon-to-retire-at-year-s-end-6622426?utm_source=openai))

- Tim Teter joined NVIDIA as senior vice president, general counsel in January 2017 and was promoted to executive vice president, general counsel and secretary in February 2018. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-names-tim-teter-as-general-counsel?utm_source=openai))

- Colette Kress was appointed NVIDIA’s executive vice president and chief financial officer in September 2013; she joined NVIDIA from prior senior finance roles at Cisco and Microsoft (an external hire). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-appoints-colette-kress-as-chief-financial-officer?utm_source=openai))

- Jay Puri joined NVIDIA in 2005 from Sun Microsystems and later became executive vice president of worldwide field operations. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/bios/jay-puri?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s public filings and proxy materials say the company works to recruit, develop and retain talent, and report a low overall employee turnover rate of 2.5% for fiscal 2025. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000095/nvda-20250512.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA runs university-focused programs (for example, a Graduate Fellowship program for PhD students) and internships aimed at bringing early-career technical talent into the company. ([research.nvidia.com](https://research.nvidia.com/graduate-fellowships?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s newsroom and press releases show a mix of career paths for senior leaders: some executives were hired from outside the company into senior roles, while others were hired at lower or mid-level roles and later promoted to top roles. (Examples above: Colette Kress and Jay Puri = external hires; Debora Shoquist, David Shannon, Tim Teter = internal promotions or promotions after joining.) ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-appoints-colette-kress-as-chief-financial-officer?utm_source=openai))
