## Point 12 - Question 4

**Are authority and decision-making responsibilities effectively delegated across divisions or functions, rather than centralized in the CEO or a small inner circle?**

### Research Findings

- The ticker NVDA is NVIDIA Corporation. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Jensen (Jen‑Hsun) Huang is the company’s co‑founder, president and chief executive officer and is a member of NVIDIA’s board. ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-eu/about-nvidia/governance/management-team/jensen-huang/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s most recent public filings say the board uses an independent “Lead Director” instead of a board chair, and that the Lead Director provides independent oversight of management. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- The proxy filing states that “our CEO has primary responsibility for the operational leadership and strategic direction of the Company,” and that the Lead Director facilitates the board’s independent oversight. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- The board is described in the proxy as mostly independent; the board determined that all directors are independent except for the CEO. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- The board has three standing committees (Audit, Compensation, and Nominating & Corporate Governance) that the proxy says are used to oversee specific topics and risks. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm))

- NVIDIA’s Form 10‑K lists the company’s named executive officers and top corporate officers, including Jensen Huang (President & CEO), Colette M. Kress (Executive Vice President and Chief Financial Officer), Ajay K. Puri (Executive Vice President, Worldwide Field Operations), Debora Shoquist (Executive Vice President, Operations), and Timothy S. Teter (Executive Vice President and General Counsel). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- The company reports two operating segments called “Compute & Networking” and “Graphics.” It also describes four main market platforms it serves: Data Center, Gaming, Professional Visualization, and Automotive. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s public executive bios show named leaders who run large functions: for example, Jay Puri is described as responsible for worldwide sales, business development, partner alliances, solution architecture and engineering, program management, and support services. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/bios/jay-puri?utm_source=openai))

- Debora Shoquist’s public bio says she is responsible for operations and supply‑chain functions, including manufacturing product and test engineering, foundry operations, supplier management, supply planning, logistics, and quality systems. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/bios/debora-shoquist?utm_source=openai))

- Colette Kress’s public bio describes her role as chief financial officer and says she leads the company’s finance functions, including financial strategy, planning, and reporting. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/bios/colette-kress?utm_source=openai))

- The data‑center and hyperscale business is led by a named executive (Ian Buck), who is described in NVIDIA materials as vice president of hyperscale and high‑performance computing and as the leader for NVIDIA’s data‑center hardware and software products. ([blogs.nvidia.com](https://blogs.nvidia.com/blog/author/ian-buck/?utm_source=openai))

- GPU engineering is led by a named senior executive (Jonah Alben), described publicly as senior vice president of GPU engineering and head of GPU architecture and engineering. ([businessinsider.com](https://www.businessinsider.com/nvidia-power-players-leaders-ai-chip-giant-success-2024-7?utm_source=openai))

- Omniverse and simulation technology are led by a named vice president (Rev Lebaredian), who is described as leading product, engineering, and research teams for the Omniverse platform. ([blogs.nvidia.com](https://blogs.nvidia.com/blog/author/revlebaredian/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA press releases and filings show product teams and platform groups (for Blackwell, Grace, DRIVE, Omniverse, NIM and similar offerings) named in product announcements, with specific vice presidents or general managers cited as spokespeople or leaders for those platforms. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2025?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 12 - Question 5

**Do disclosures or commentary from management indicate an executive climate that rewards merit, minimizes factionalism, and encourages collaboration and upward-flowing ideas?**

### Research Findings

- Jensen Huang asks many employees to send a short weekly note called a “Top 5 Things” (T5T). He says he reads these notes to see what people at the edges of the company are working on. ([stripe.com](https://stripe.com/au/sessions/2024/a-conversation-with-nvidias-jensen-huang?utm_source=openai))

- Company and news reports say Huang discourages private one‑on‑one meetings with direct reports; he says he prefers to share information and give feedback to groups so everyone can learn together. ([stripe.com](https://stripe.com/au/sessions/2024/a-conversation-with-nvidias-jensen-huang?utm_source=openai))

- Reports say Huang spends time eating and talking with employees in company spaces, and that he has a large number of direct reports (about 60), which he uses to reduce layers between him and other staff. ([businessinsider.com](https://www.businessinsider.com/jensen-huang-nvidia-routine-management-leadership-style-ceo-founder-2024-4?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s public policies page posts a formal Code of Conduct and tells people how to report concerns confidentially through a “Speak Up” line (a third‑party confidential reporting channel). ([nvidia.com](https://www.nvidia.com/en-in/about-nvidia/company-policies/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s U.S. SEC filings (Form 10‑K / proxy) say the Board’s Compensation Committee helps oversee human‑capital matters (hiring, development, retention, diversity and culture). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm?utm_source=openai))

- SEC filings list employee counts at year‑end (for example, about 36,000 employees worldwide as of the end of fiscal 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s proxy and filings state the company offers equity to most employees (RSUs, PSUs and market‑based PSUs). RSUs usually vest over four years; PSUs vest over periods that depend on service and meeting pre‑set performance or market targets. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- The company’s proxy filings describe a “pay‑for‑performance” approach for executives: a large share of executive pay is tied to performance metrics and long‑term equity that vests only if goals or market targets are met. The filings say a very high percentage of the CEO’s target pay is performance‑dependent. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s proxy materials state the company’s compensation program is designed to “reward performance” and to align employee interests with shareholders by giving equity that vests over time. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s filings report low overall turnover in recent years (the proxy says overall turnover was about 2.5% in fiscal 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000086/nvda-20250501.htm?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s filings say many new hires come from employee referrals (the company reported over 40% of new hires in Fiscal 2024 were employee referrals). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000104/nvda-20240514.htm?utm_source=openai))

- In public interviews and conference talks, Jensen Huang describes practices he says promote transparency and information flow (brevity in email, frequent company‑wide communication, reading many employees’ T5T notes, and explaining his reasoning publicly so others can learn). ([businessinsider.com](https://www.businessinsider.com/nvidia-ceo-jensen-huang-sends-hundreds-emails-staff-daily-2023-11?utm_source=openai))

---

### Point 13 Criterion

Is the company doing enough to maintain or improve profit margins?

## Point 13 - Question 1

**How have gross, operating, and net profit margins trended over the past five years, and what explanations has management given for these movements?**

### Research Findings

Company: NVIDIA Corporation (ticker: NVDA)

Fiscal years shown are NVIDIA’s fiscal years (year ended on the last Sunday in January). Sources are company filings and earnings releases.

1) Reported margins — five fiscal years
- FY2021 (fiscal year ended January 31, 2021)
  - Gross margin: 62.3%. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2021/?utm_source=openai))  
  - Operating margin (income from operations ÷ revenue): 27.2% (operating income $4,532m on revenue $16,675m). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2021/?utm_source=openai))  
  - Net margin (net income ÷ revenue): 26.0% (net income $4,332m). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2021/?utm_source=openai))

- FY2022 (fiscal year ended January 30, 2022)
  - Gross margin: 64.9%. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581022000036/nvda-20220130.htm))  
  - Operating margin: 37.3% (operating income $10,041m on revenue $26,914m). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2022/?utm_source=openai))  
  - Net margin: 36.2% (net income $9,752m). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2022/?utm_source=openai))

- FY2023 (fiscal year ended January 29, 2023)
  - Gross margin: 56.9%. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2023/))  
  - Operating margin: 15.7% (operating income $4,224m on revenue $26,974m). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2023/))  
  - Net margin: 16.2% (net income $4,368m). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2023/))

- FY2024 (fiscal year ended January 28, 2024)
  - Gross margin: 72.7%. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2024/))  
  - Operating margin: 54.1% (operating income $32,972m on revenue $60,922m). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2024/))  
  - Net margin: 48.9% (net income $29,760m). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2024/))

- FY2025 (fiscal year ended January 26, 2025)
  - Gross margin: 75.0%. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
  - Operating margin: 62.4% (operating income $81,453m on revenue $130,497m). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
  - Net margin: 55.8% (net income $72,880m). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

2) What management said (company explanations in filings and earnings releases)
- FY2021 (management statements about FY2021 results)
  - Management said the company had record revenue for Gaming and Data Center in FY2021, and highlighted that the Mellanox acquisition expanded NVIDIA’s footprint in the data center. (CEO and press release summary). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2021/?utm_source=openai))

- FY2022 (management explanations for changes in margins)
  - Management said gross margin rose in FY2022 mainly because there were lower Mellanox acquisition-related charges compared with FY2021 (FY2021 included a one-time inventory step-up charge), and because of a higher-end mix within Graphics (Gaming). Management also said a mix shift in Compute & Networking (Data Center) partially offset those benefits. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581022000036/nvda-20220130.htm))  
  - Management said operating expenses increased in FY2022 mainly from stock-based compensation, higher headcount/compensation, and higher infrastructure costs. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581022000036/nvda-20220130.htm))

- FY2023 (management explanations for changes in margins)
  - Management said gross margin fell in FY2023 versus FY2022. The company reported higher cost of revenue and changes in product mix; management also disclosed a significant one-time acquisition termination cost charged in FY2023 that raised operating expenses. Management highlighted that Data Center and Gaming trends and inventory provisions affected margins. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2023/))  
  - Management discussed that R&D and other operating expenses rose in absolute dollars and as a percentage of revenue in FY2023, which reduced operating margin. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2023/))

- FY2024 (management explanations for changes in margins)
  - Management said gross margin and operating margin widened sharply in FY2024 because Data Center revenue grew a lot (management cited very large Data Center demand and product launches such as Hopper/H100), improving the company’s product mix toward higher‑margin sales. Management also noted lower relative inventory provisions versus the prior year. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2024/))

- FY2025 (management explanations for changes in margins)
  - Management said gross margin increased in FY2025 “driven by a higher mix of Data Center revenue.” The FY2025 Form 10‑K also shows cost of revenue as a smaller share of revenue (25.0% in FY2025 vs 27.3% in FY2024) and shows research & development and SG&A rose in dollars but fell as a percentage of revenue (R&D 9.9% of revenue in FY2025 vs 14.2% in FY2024), which management described as operating leverage from much larger revenue. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
  - In the FY2025 earnings release, management (CEO) said demand for the new Blackwell family of AI products was “amazing” and cited ramping massive-scale production as a key driver of revenue and margins. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2025?utm_source=openai))

3) Additional company facts related to margins (from filings)
- Inventory provisions and related reserve releases affected gross margin in multiple years; NVIDIA disclosed inventory provisions and releases and the net percentage effects in its MD&A for FY2024 and FY2025. (Examples: net unfavorable impact on gross margin of ~2–3% in FY2024 and FY2025 from inventory provisions and related items as disclosed by the company.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

Sources (selected company filings and earnings releases used above)
- NVIDIA Form 10‑K for fiscal year ended January 26, 2025 (FY2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
- NVIDIA press release / earnings release for fourth quarter and fiscal 2025 (Feb 26, 2025). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2025?utm_source=openai))  
- NVIDIA press release / earnings release for fourth quarter and fiscal 2024 (Feb 21, 2024). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2024/))  
- NVIDIA press release / earnings release for fourth quarter and fiscal 2023 (Feb 22, 2023). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2023/))  
- NVIDIA Form 10‑K for fiscal year ended January 30, 2022 (FY2022). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581022000036/nvda-20220130.htm))  
- NVIDIA press release / earnings release for fourth quarter and fiscal 2021 (Feb 24, 2021). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2021/?utm_source=openai))

If you want, I can (a) put these numbers into a simple table, (b) extract the exact sentences/quotes management used from the filings and transcripts, or (c) show the calculations that convert the reported dollar amounts into the operating and net margin percentages.

---

## Point 13 - Question 2

**What specific cost-reduction or efficiency programs (automation, supply-chain optimization, capital-improvement projects, product-engineering initiatives) has management disclosed to offset rising labor, material, or tax expenses?**

### Research Findings

- NVIDIA says its Blackwell GPU architecture and related systems cut operating cost and energy for AI inference and training by large multiples versus the prior generation (NVIDIA’s announcement states “up to 25x” less cost and energy in some workloads). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2024/NVIDIA-Blackwell-Platform-Arrives-to-Power-a-New-Era-of-Computing/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- CEO Jensen Huang told reporters that making faster chips is NVIDIA’s primary way to lower the cost of running AI; he said faster chips reduce the cost per unit of AI work (for example, cost per token). ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2025/03/19/nvidias-huang-says-faster-chips-are-the-best-way-to-reduce-ai-costs-.html?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA announced new networking and photonics products (Spectrum‑X / Quantum‑X) that the company says reduce data‑center energy use and operating cost (the press release cites ~3.5× energy savings for certain configurations). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Spectrum-X-Photonics-Co-Packaged-Optics-Networking-Switches-to-Scale-AI-Factories-to-Millions-of-GPUs/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA describes Omniverse and “physical AI” tools as ways to let manufacturers build digital twins and simulations that speed factory setup, cut manual work, and improve operational efficiency. NVIDIA and partners say these tools let factory customers automate workflows and reduce hours in real operations. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Expands-Omniverse-With-Generative-Physical-AI/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA says partners such as Foxconn are using NVIDIA Omniverse and industrial AI to speed factory bring‑up and improve efficiency; public comments and transcripts cite Foxconn expecting large reductions in manual hours (one cited example: a Foxconn facility reporting a ~30% reduction in annual hours after using digital‑twin/automation tools). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/Foxconn-Builds-AI-Factory-in-Partnership-With-Taiwan-and-NVIDIA/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA has made large purchase and capacity commitments to secure supply for new products. Its 2025 Form 10‑K discloses $30.8 billion of outstanding inventory purchase and long‑term supply and capacity obligations, and it says some of those commitments raise product costs. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- The 10‑K also says NVIDIA has paid premiums, provided deposits, and entered long‑term supply agreements and capacity commitments to secure future supply and capacity, and that those actions have increased its product costs. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- NVIDIA’s 2025 annual filing shows capital spending rose (the company spent $3.4 billion on capital expenditures in fiscal 2025 versus $1.1 billion in fiscal 2024) and states it expects to increase capital expenditures in fiscal 2026 to support growth. These capital projects fund things like infrastructure, compute, and supply‑chain capacity. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- NVIDIA has disclosed multi‑party projects and partnerships to build “AI factories” and regional infrastructure (examples: announced partnerships to build AI factory projects with Foxconn and with Saudi partners). These projects are positioned as large capital and supply‑chain efforts to scale production, improve resilience, and enable automation. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/Foxconn-Builds-AI-Factory-in-Partnership-With-Taiwan-and-NVIDIA/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Public reporting (press and analyst coverage of company remarks) says NVIDIA’s management is planning large investments in U.S. supply‑chain capacity and sourcing to create more resilience. Management framed this as a supply‑chain optimization step even though building local capacity can raise near‑term costs. ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/technology/nvidia-invest-billions-us-chip-production-over-four-years-ft-reports-2025-03-20/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA has disclosed tax‑related items in filings: its 2025 annual report shows $2.2 billion of unrecognized tax benefits recorded as non‑current income tax payable (the filing notes timing and uncertainty of these tax liabilities). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- NVIDIA has warned in its 10‑K that higher costs for wafers, components, logistics, employees, facilities, and new regulations (including carbon or energy taxes) have reduced, and could continue to reduce, its margins; the filing links these cost pressures to supply commitments, capital spending, and regulatory changes. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- NVIDIA and industry sources report NVIDIA holds very large shares of advanced packaging capacity (reports cite NVIDIA securing a majority share of some TSMC CoWoS packaging capacity for 2025), which management uses to support product ramps and supply continuity. Securing that capacity is part of NVIDIA’s supply‑chain approach. ([site.financialmodelingprep.com](https://site.financialmodelingprep.com/market-news/nvidia-nasdaqnvda-secures-over--of-tsmcs-advanced-chip-packaging-capacity-for-?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s public materials repeatedly present product engineering (faster, more power‑efficient chips and system designs) and software (inference microservices, Omniverse simulation tools) as levers to lower customers’ operating costs and to improve system efficiency; management points to those engineering gains as a way to reduce total cost of ownership for AI workloads. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2024/NVIDIA-Blackwell-Platform-Arrives-to-Power-a-New-Era-of-Computing/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

---

## Point 13 - Question 3

**To what extent has management preserved margins through price increases, and how sustainable is this strategy given current and expected competitive capacity?**

### Research Findings

- NVIDIA’s reported full‑year fiscal 2025 gross margin was 75.0% (GAAP) compared with 72.7% in fiscal 2024 — a rise of 2.3 percentage points. (NVIDIA press release, Feb 26, 2025). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Fourth-Quarter-and-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx))

- In the quarter ended Aug 26, 2025 (Q2 fiscal 2026), NVIDIA reported gross margin of 72.4% (GAAP) and guided to mid‑70% range for full‑year margins as its Blackwell product family ramps. (NVIDIA Q2 FY26 press release, Aug 26, 2025). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Second-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s data‑center business (the part that sells GPUs and related systems) was about $115.2 billion of $130.5 billion in revenue for fiscal 2025 — roughly 88% of total revenue — showing that high‑value data‑center products drive most sales. (NVIDIA fiscal 2025 results, Feb 26, 2025). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Fourth-Quarter-and-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx))

- Company management has said the new Blackwell family (B/GB/GB200 series) is a premium product mix and that the Blackwell ramp is a main reason for current margin levels; they have also said margins are temporarily in the low‑70s during the ramp and should improve to the mid‑70s as yields and production scale. (NVIDIA earnings transcripts and CFO commentary, 2025). ([nasdaq.com](https://www.nasdaq.com/articles/nvidia-nvda-q4-2025-earnings-call-transcript?utm_source=openai))

- Public and analyst estimates put the average selling prices (ASPs) for recent NVIDIA data‑center GPUs in the tens of thousands of dollars per unit: H100/A100 family estimates commonly reported in 2024–2025 center around $25,000–$40,000 per high‑end GPU; early Blackwell/GB200 estimates by analysts put some Blackwell configurations in similar or higher ranges. These are analyst and press estimates, not official list prices. (CNBC, Reuters, analyst reports May 2024–2025). ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2024/03/18/nvidia-announces-gb200-blackwell-ai-chip-launching-later-this-year.html?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA has been selling more complete systems and rack solutions (not only individual chips), and management has pointed to higher margins from selling full systems and custom configurations. (NVIDIA investor materials and earnings comments, 2024–2025). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Fourth-Quarter-and-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx))

- Cloud providers and other buyers have negotiated large contracts and deployments that affect demand and pricing. On Sept 22, 2025 NVIDIA and OpenAI announced a letter of intent for a partnership to deploy at least 10 gigawatts of NVIDIA systems, with NVIDIA saying it may invest up to $100 billion as systems are deployed. (NVIDIA and OpenAI press releases, Sept 22, 2025). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/OpenAI-and-NVIDIA-Announce-Strategic-Partnership-to-Deploy-10-Gigawatts-of-NVIDIA-Systems/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- On Oct 6, 2025 AMD and OpenAI announced a separate multi‑year agreement for AMD to supply up to 6 gigawatts of AMD Instinct GPUs (starting with a 1‑gigawatt deployment in second half of 2026). This is a material new source of large‑scale GPU capacity from a competitor. (AMD and OpenAI press release, Oct 6, 2025). ([amd.com](https://www.amd.com/en/newsroom/press-releases/2025-10-6-amd-and-openai-announce-strategic-partnership-to-d.html?utm_source=openai))

- Major cloud providers have introduced substantial price cuts for GPU instances in 2025; for example, AWS announced reductions of up to about 44% for some H100 instances and up to 33% for some A100 instances effective June 2025. Public cloud list‑price moves affect how much customers pay per hour to use GPUs. (AWS blog; coverage June 2025). ([aws.amazon.com](https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/aws/announcing-up-to-45-price-reduction-for-amazon-ec2-nvidia-gpu-accelerated-instances/?utm_source=openai))

- Independent market studies and analysts reported that NVIDIA held an extremely large share of data‑center GPU shipments in recent years (TechInsights reported NVIDIA shipped ~3.76 million datacenter GPUs in 2023 and estimated a very high market share, ~98% by unit shipments in 2023). That dominance means competitors had small installed bases but were expanding in 2024–2025. (TechInsights reported coverage, June 2024). ([hpcwire.com](https://www.hpcwire.com/2024/06/10/nvidia-shipped-3-76-million-data-center-gpus-in-2023-according-to-study/?utm_source=openai))

- Competitors with growing supply or alternative chips in 2024–2025 include: AMD (Instinct MI300/MI350 and planned MI450), Intel (Habana Gaudi2/Greco family and other accelerators), and hyperscaler custom chips (Google TPUs, AWS Trainium/Inferentia). Each supplier has announced product roadmaps and some cloud deployments during 2024–2025. (AMD, Intel, Google product announcements and press coverage). ([amd.com](https://www.amd.com/en/newsroom/press-releases/2025-10-6-amd-and-openai-announce-strategic-partnership-to-d.html?utm_source=openai))

- Foundry and advanced‑packaging capacity are an important physical constraint for high‑end GPUs. Industry reports through 2024–2025 said TSMC and its advanced packaging (CoWoS/CoWoS‑L) capacity was being expanded and that NVIDIA had booked a very large share of advanced packaging capacity for its Blackwell chips; reporters and industry trackers described NVIDIA as taking a majority share of advanced packaging capacity in 2024–2025. (TrendForce, industry reporting 2024–2025; Reuters reporting on packaging demand). ([trendforce.com](https://www.trendforce.com/news/2024/05/06/news-tsmcs-advanced-packaging-capacity-fully-booked-by-nvidia-and-amd-through-next-year/?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA has reported inventory and export‑control impacts to sales in China (e.g., charges and lost shipments related to H20 restrictions) and has said it is introducing lower‑spec chips for China; such geopolitical constraints affected which products could be sold and where in 2024–2025. (Reuters May 24, 2025; NVIDIA earnings commentary). ([reuters.com](https://www.reuters.com/world/china/nvidia-launch-cheaper-blackwell-ai-chip-china-after-us-export-curbs-sources-say-2025-05-24/?utm_source=openai))

- Public cloud per‑hour prices, analyst ASP estimates, and company revenue/margin disclosures are the primary public evidence for how much price or product‑mix changes have contributed to NVIDIA’s overall margins; NVIDIA’s public filings and earnings calls for fiscal 2024–2026 provide the company’s stated revenue mix, gross margins, and management comments about ramp, yields, and margin outlooks. (NVIDIA investor releases and earnings call transcripts, 2024–2025). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Fourth-Quarter-and-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx))

- Reported supply‑and‑demand actions in 2025 included hyperscalers increasing deployments of NVIDIA Blackwell systems (NVIDIA and cloud partners announced multi‑rack and pod deployments) while other large buyers started to contract with AMD and use non‑NVIDIA accelerators — these moves change future competitive capacity and buying options. (NVIDIA, AMD, OpenAI, and cloud provider announcements Sept–Oct 2025). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/OpenAI-and-NVIDIA-Announce-Strategic-Partnership-to-Deploy-10-Gigawatts-of-NVIDIA-Systems/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Analyst and media price estimates for specific chips vary across sources; official, per‑unit list prices are not always published by sellers for the highest‑end datacenter GPUs, so press and analyst figures (e.g., $25k–$70k ranges reported for H100/Blackwell variants by various outlets and analysts) are estimates based on system pricing, reseller listings, and analyst models. (CNBC, Tom’s Hardware, HSBC analyst notes, 2024–2025). ([cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2024/03/18/nvidia-announces-gb200-blackwell-ai-chip-launching-later-this-year.html?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s own published guidance and CFO commentary (multiple 2024–2025 quarters) tie margin trends to product mix (data center systems, Blackwell ramp) and to manufacturing yields and packaging costs; NVIDIA has said margins dipped during early Blackwell deliveries and were expected to recover toward the mid‑70% range as production scales and costs improve. (NVIDIA earnings releases and transcripts, 2024–2025). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Fourth-Quarter-and-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx))

- Public articles and market reports in 2024–2025 show the industry actively expanding capacity (foundries, packaging, hyperscaler builds) and some large new supplier deals (AMD with OpenAI, NVIDIA with OpenAI) that change the expected supply of high‑performance accelerators over 2026 and beyond. Dates and providers for these announcements: NVIDIA–OpenAI (Sept 22, 2025); AMD–OpenAI (Oct 6, 2025); AWS price cuts announced June 2025. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/OpenAI-and-NVIDIA-Announce-Strategic-Partnership-to-Deploy-10-Gigawatts-of-NVIDIA-Systems/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

(End of facts.)

---

## Point 13 - Question 4

**Where margins are presently narrow, is this due to consciously elevated investment in R&D, sales promotion, or other growth-oriented spending, and has management articulated when margins should expand as these investments mature?**

### Research Findings

- Company and documents cited: NVIDIA Corporation (ticker NVDA). Facts below come from the company’s filings, quarterly reports, earnings transcripts, and investor press releases. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Fiscal year totals (year ended Jan 26, 2025): revenue $130.497 billion; gross margin 75.0%; operating expenses $16.405 billion (operating expenses were up 45% from the prior year). (These are the audited annual numbers the company filed with the SEC.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Research & development (R&D) spending (fiscal year ended Jan 26, 2025): R&D expense was $12.914 billion, equal to 9.9% of revenue. The prior fiscal year (ended Jan 28, 2024) R&D was $8.675 billion and was 14.2% of revenue. (Shows R&D dollars rose and the R&D share of revenue fell because revenue grew a lot.) ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/5EBFB425AD1D43945A255B6E3A1E3927B06A7141?utm_source=openai))

- Sales, general & administrative (SG&A) spending (fiscal year ended Jan 26, 2025): SG&A expense was $3.491 billion versus $2.654 billion the prior year (a 32% increase in dollars). ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/5EBFB425AD1D43945A255B6E3A1E3927B06A7141?utm_source=openai))

- Operating-expense guidance and management language: management said they are “accelerating investments in the business to address the magnitude of growth opportunities,” and guided higher operating expenses (stating operating expenses are expected to grow in the high‑thirties percent year-over-year versus prior expectations). The company gave projected GAAP and non‑GAAP operating expense amounts for the year in public guidance. ([ph.investing.com](https://ph.investing.com/news/transcripts/earnings-call-transcript-nvidia-q2-2025-strong-earnings-beat-drives-stock-uptick-93CH-1974978?utm_source=openai))

- Capital expenditures: the company spent $3.4 billion on capital expenditures in fiscal 2025 versus $1.1 billion in fiscal 2024, and said it expects to increase capital expenditures in fiscal 2026 to support future growth. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Inventory and related charges affecting margins: the 2025 10‑K reports provisions for inventory and excess inventory purchase obligations of $3.7 billion in fiscal 2025 (and $2.2 billion in fiscal 2024). The company said these items had an unfavorable effect on gross margin (noting a net unfavorable impact of about 2.3 percentage points on gross margin in fiscal 2025). ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/5EBFB425AD1D43945A255B6E3A1E3927B06A7141?utm_source=openai))

- Q1 Fiscal 2026 special charge and short‑term margin effect: on April 9, 2025 the U.S. government told NVIDIA that an export license was required for H20 products to China. NVIDIA recorded a $4.5 billion charge in Q1 FY2026 related to excess H20 inventory and purchase obligations. That quarter’s GAAP gross margin fell to 60.5%; excluding the H20 charge the company reported a gross margin of about 71.3% for the quarter. (The company disclosed this in its Q1 FY2026 press release.) ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-First-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Management comments about product ramp and margins: company executives (including CFO Colette Kress) said that during the ramp of the company’s next‑generation Blackwell products gross margins would be lower (described as “low‑70s” in comments) while manufacturing and system ramp costs are being incurred. They said once Blackwell production fully ramps, gross margins should improve to the mid‑70% range later in the fiscal year. CEO Jensen Huang and other executives also described accelerating manufacturing to meet demand and said investments in infrastructure give a strong return. These statements were made in recent earnings calls and public remarks. ([webull.com](https://www.webull.com/news/12380837088819200?utm_source=openai))

- Recent quarter operating‑expense percentages (quarter ended Jul 27, 2025): R&D was 9.2% of revenue and SG&A was 2.4% of revenue for the three months ended Jul 27, 2025 (company consolidated results in the filed quarterly report). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Company statement on margin targets: in public guidance and on earnings calls the company has stated a target or expectation to “exit the year” with non‑GAAP gross margins in the mid‑70% range, after current product ramps and one‑time inventory impacts are resolved. ([ph.investing.com](https://ph.investing.com/news/transcripts/earnings-call-transcript-nvidia-q2-2025-strong-earnings-beat-drives-stock-uptick-93CH-1974978?utm_source=openai))

- Where margin pressure has come from (as reported by the company): the filings and releases list higher manufacturing costs during product ramps, inventory provisions and excess purchase obligations, charges tied to H20 export/license developments, and higher absolute operating expenses as drivers that have weighed on margins in the near term. ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/5EBFB425AD1D43945A255B6E3A1E3927B06A7141?utm_source=openai))


---

## Point 13 - Question 5

**Does the company set explicit margin or cost-savings targets and regularly report progress, indicating an institutionalized commitment to margin management?**

### Research Findings

- NVIDIA’s quarterly earnings press releases always show its reported GAAP and non‑GAAP gross margin and operating‑expense numbers, and they publish a numerical outlook (guidance) for next quarter gross margin and operating expenses. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2025?utm_source=openai))

- In the earnings outlook for the quarter reported May 28, 2025, NVIDIA said it was “continuing to work toward achieving gross margins in the mid‑70% range late this year.” (This is an explicit, public statement about a margin level the company is trying to reach.) ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-First-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- In later quarterly outlooks NVIDIA restated a similar aim, saying it “continues to expect to exit the year with non‑GAAP gross margins in the mid‑70% range.” (That repeats the same target across quarters.) ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Second-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s quarterly releases and SEC filings show it reports both GAAP and non‑GAAP margins and often publish reconciliations that exclude specific one‑time charges (for example, “gross margin excluding H20 charge”). Those reconciliations appear in the company’s press releases and outlook tables. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-First-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s Form 10‑K (fiscal year ended January 26, 2025) reports its fiscal‑year gross margin (75.0% for FY2025) and explains drivers of margin changes (for example, product mix and inventory provisions) in the Management’s Discussion and Analysis. ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/5EBFB425AD1D43945A255B6E3A1E3927B06A7141?utm_source=openai))

- Example reported numbers showing the company tracks margin progress quarter‑to‑quarter: Q4 FY2025 GAAP gross margin was reported as 73.0%, and full‑year FY2025 GAAP gross margin was 75.0% (both published in NVIDIA’s official results). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2025?utm_source=openai))

- NVIDIA’s quarterly outlooks also give explicit guidance for operating expenses (both GAAP and non‑GAAP) for the coming quarter and comment on expected full‑year operating‑expense growth ranges, showing the company publicly sets and reports expense plans as well as margin plans. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-First-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

---

### Point 14 Criterion

Is the company’s financial management and skill good?

## Point 14 - Question 1

**How effectively does management allocate capital—measured by return on invested capital (ROIC), disciplined capital-expenditure decisions, and avoidance of low-return projects?**

### Research Findings

- Company and fiscal period cited in the facts below: NVIDIA Corporation (ticker NVDA). Fiscal year 2025 ended January 26, 2025. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Revenue (what the company sold) for fiscal 2025: $130,497 million. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Fourth-Quarter-and-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Operating income (profit from running the business, before interest and taxes) for fiscal 2025: $81,453 million. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Fourth-Quarter-and-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))

- Income before income tax and income tax expense for fiscal 2025: income before tax $84,026 million; income tax expense $11,146 million (effective tax rate 13.3%). (You can use these to convert operating profit into after-tax operating profit.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Research & development expense for fiscal 2025: $12,914 million. (R&D is money spent to make new products and improve existing ones.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Capital expenditures (money spent on buildings, equipment, servers, factory tools) by fiscal year:
  - Fiscal 2025: $3.4 billion.
  - Fiscal 2024: $1.1 billion.
  - The company stated it expects capital expenditures to increase in fiscal 2026 versus fiscal 2025 to support growth. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Cash and short‑term marketable securities (money the company can quickly use) as of January 26, 2025: $43,210 million. (This is cash the company could use instead of raising new money.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Balance sheet size and capital-structure items as of January 26, 2025:
  - Total assets: $111,601 million.
  - Total shareholders’ equity: $79,327 million.
  - Long-term debt (net carrying amount): $8,463 million. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Two simple ways to measure “invested capital” from the 10‑K numbers (different ROIC calculations use different definitions):
  - Total assets minus cash and marketable securities = $111,601m − $43,210m = $68,391 million. (This treats cash as non‑operating and measures the asset base used in the business.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))
  - Total debt plus shareholders’ equity minus cash and marketable securities = ($8,463m + $79,327m) − $43,210m = $44,580 million. (This measures capital supplied by creditors and owners, less excess cash.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- A simple ROIC calculation building blocks (formula and where to find the numbers above):
  - After‑tax operating profit (NOPAT) ≈ operating income × (1 − effective tax rate). (Use operating income and the tax expense/effective tax rate above.) ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Fourth-Quarter-and-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))
  - Invested capital can be measured as either (a) total assets − cash & marketable securities, or (b) total debt + shareholders’ equity − cash & marketable securities, using the balance‑sheet numbers above. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))
  - (Definition reference for ROIC concept and why people use NOPAT and invested capital in the formula.) ([investopedia.com](https://www.investopedia.com/articles/fundamental/03/050603.asp?utm_source=openai))

- Share repurchases and dividend facts (capital returned to shareholders) for fiscal 2025 and related authorizations:
  - On August 26, 2024 the Board approved an additional $50 billion for share repurchases (no expiration). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))
  - In fiscal 2025 the company repurchased 310 million shares for $34.0 billion. As of January 26, 2025, the company was authorized (subject to limits) to repurchase up to $38.7 billion of common stock. From January 27, 2025 through February 21, 2025 the company repurchased 29 million shares for $3.7 billion pursuant to a trading plan. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))
  - Cash dividends paid in fiscal 2025: $834 million (dividend per share reported as $0.034 for the year). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Other capital commitments and obligations that affect capital use (as of January 26, 2025):
  - Inventory purchase and long-term supply/capacity obligations totaling $30.8 billion (commitments to buy components, capacity, and other goods/services). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Notes about investment discipline and project selection stated in filings (exact company wording, fiscal 2025 10‑K):
  - The company said its share repurchase program “aims to offset dilution from shares issued to employees while maintaining adequate liquidity to meet our operating requirements” and that repurchases “may be suspended at any time at our discretion.” ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))
  - The 10‑K warns that acquisitions and strategic investments carry risks including diversion of capital and management attention and that the company evaluates liquidity and capital resources to finance future capital requirements. (These are disclosures about how the company approaches investments and risks.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Example raw numbers you can use directly to compute ROIC for fiscal 2025:
  - Operating income (FY2025): $81,453 million; effective tax rate: 13.3% (income tax expense $11,146m on income before tax $84,026m). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Fourth-Quarter-and-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))
  - Two invested‑capital choices: $68,391 million (assets − cash/marketable securities) or $44,580 million (debt + equity − cash/marketable securities). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- Source documents used for the facts above:
  - NVIDIA Corporation Annual Report on Form 10‑K for the fiscal year ended January 26, 2025 (NVIDIA’s SEC filing). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))
  - NVIDIA press release summarizing fiscal 2025 results (company investor relations). ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Fourth-Quarter-and-Fiscal-2025/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))
  - General ROIC definition reference. ([investopedia.com](https://www.investopedia.com/articles/fundamental/03/050603.asp?utm_source=openai))

## Point 14 - Question 2

**How well are working-capital elements such as receivables and inventory controlled compared with industry peers, and what commentary explains observed trends?**

### Research Findings

Company and documents used
- Company: NVIDIA Corporation (ticker: NVDA). Source: NVIDIA filings and earnings releases. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))

Balances (facts from NVIDIA filings)
- Accounts receivable, net:
  - $23,065 million as of January 26, 2025. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))
  - $27,808 million as of July 27, 2025. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))

- Inventories (components and totals):
  - As of January 26, 2025: raw materials $3,408M; work in process $3,399M; finished goods $3,273M; total $10,080M. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))
  - As of July 27, 2025: raw materials $1,843M; work in process $4,411M; finished goods $8,708M; total $14,962M. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))

- Change between Jan 26, 2025 and Jul 27, 2025:
  - Accounts receivable increased by $4,743M (from $23,065M to $27,808M). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))
  - Inventories increased by $4,882M (from $10,080M to $14,962M). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))

Inventory provisions and related charges (company disclosures)
- NVIDIA recorded a $4.5 billion charge tied to H20 product excess inventory and related purchase obligations in the first quarter of fiscal 2026 (this was disclosed as an inventory and purchase-obligation charge). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm))
- First-quarter fiscal 2026 detail (from the April 27, 2025 filing): NVIDIA recorded an inventory provision of $2.3 billion in cost of revenue for Q1 FY2026, including $1.9 billion for H20 product inventory; NVIDIA also recorded $3.0 billion of excess inventory purchase-obligation charges in Q1 (including $2.6 billion for H20 orders). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm))
- Second-quarter fiscal 2026 detail (from the July 27, 2025 filing): NVIDIA recorded an inventory provision of $886 million in the second quarter and $3.2 billion for the first half of fiscal 2026 in cost of revenue. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))
- Q2 fiscal 2026 press release: NVIDIA reported a $180 million release of previously reserved H20 inventory (sale outside China) in Q2. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Second-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))
- The filings show excess-inventory purchase obligation balances and related accruals (examples: excess inventory purchase obligations reported $4,310M as of April 27, 2025 vs $2,095M as of January 26, 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm))

Accounts-receivable concentration (customer exposure)
- As of July 27, 2025, three direct customers made up 23%, 19%, and 14% of NVIDIA’s accounts receivable balance. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))
- As of January 26, 2025, two direct customers made up 17% and 16% of accounts receivable. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

Quarterly revenues and costs used as sources for the following calculations
- Revenue by quarter (company releases / filings):
  - Q3 FY25 (quarter ended Oct 27, 2024) revenue $35,082M; cost of revenue $8,926M. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-third-quarter-fiscal-2025))
  - Q4 FY25 (quarter ended Jan 26, 2025) revenue $39,331M; cost of revenue $10,608M. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-fourth-quarter-and-fiscal-2025?utm_source=openai))
  - Q1 FY26 (quarter ended Apr 27, 2025) revenue $44,062M; cost of revenue $17,394M. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm))
  - Q2 FY26 (quarter ended Jul 27, 2025) revenue $46,743M; cost of revenue $12,890M. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))

Computed working-capital metrics (explicit calculations; each number below is a simple arithmetic calculation using the cited filings)
- Method note: “Days” = (balance ÷ relevant 12‑month total) × 365. The revenue totals and cost-of-revenue totals used are the sum of the four most-recent reported quarters listed above. The source numbers used for each calculation are cited immediately after the result.

- NVIDIA — using year-end balances (January 26, 2025):
  - DSO (approximate) = (Accounts receivable $23,065M ÷ FY2025 revenue $130,497M) × 365 ≈ 64.5 days. Source balances and revenue: accounts receivable $23,065M; FY2025 revenue $130,497M. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))
  - DIO (approximate) = (Inventories $10,080M ÷ FY2025 cost of revenue $32,639M) × 365 ≈ 112.7 days. Source balances and cost of revenue: inventories $10,080M; FY2025 cost of revenue $32,639M. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))

- NVIDIA — using balances and trailing‑12‑month (LTM) totals ending July 27, 2025:
  - LTM revenue used = Q3 FY25 + Q4 FY25 + Q1 FY26 + Q2 FY26 = $35,082M + $39,331M + $44,062M + $46,743M = $165,218M. Sources: quarterly revenues. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-third-quarter-fiscal-2025))
  - LTM cost of revenue used = Q3 + Q4 + Q1 + Q2 cost of revenue = $8,926M + $10,608M + $17,394M + $12,890M = $49,818M. Sources: quarterly cost of revenue amounts. ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-third-quarter-fiscal-2025))
  - DSO (approximate, LTM basis) = (Accounts receivable $27,808M ÷ LTM revenue $165,218M) × 365 ≈ 61.4 days. Source: accounts receivable $27,808M and the LTM revenue above. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))
  - DIO (approximate, LTM basis) = (Inventories $14,962M ÷ LTM cost of revenue $49,818M) × 365 ≈ 109.6 days. Source: inventories $14,962M and the LTM cost of revenue above. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))

Company commentary and public statements explaining trends (direct facts from filings and earnings materials)
- NVIDIA’s filings and CFO/CEO remarks state that gross margins and cost of revenue in Q1 FY2026 were materially affected by a $4.5B charge tied to H20 product excess inventory and purchase obligations. The filing says gross margin decreased in Q1 FY2026 “primarily due to a $4.5 billion charge associated with H20 excess inventory and purchase obligations.” ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm))
- NVIDIA’s first-quarter filing says the $4.5B charge included inventory provisions and excess inventory purchase-obligation charges (Q1 inventory provision $2.3B including $1.9B for H20; Q1 excess purchase-obligation charges $3.0B including $2.6B for H20). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm))
- NVIDIA disclosed that there were no H20 sales to China-based customers in Q2 FY2026, and that NVIDIA recognized a $180M release of previously reserved H20 inventory from sales to a customer outside China in Q2 FY2026. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Second-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))
- The company disclosed increases in certain working-capital items tied to its business activity and commitments, for example reporting excess inventory purchase obligations and customer advances in its quarterly notes. (Examples: excess inventory purchase obligations $4,310M as of Apr 27, 2025; deferred revenue additions / customer advances in first half FY2026). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm))

Peer data — simple, cited reference numbers for comparison (selected peers; numbers are the reported or commonly published “days” metrics for recent periods)
- Advanced Micro Devices (AMD) — published measures for 2024:
  - Days Sales Outstanding (DSO) ≈ 95.9 days (calendar 2024 figure reported by financial-data sites based on AMD data). ([stock-data.online](https://stock-data.online/stock/amd/activity-ratio/days-of-sales-outstanding?utm_source=openai))
  - Days Inventory On Hand (DIO) ≈ 109.2 days (calendar 2024 figure). ([stock-data.online](https://stock-data.online/stock/amd/liquidity-ratio/cash-conversion-cycle?utm_source=openai))

- Intel Corporation — published measures for 2024 (approximate):
  - DSO ≈ 41.4 days (calendar 2024 figure). ([stock-data.online](https://stock-data.online/stock/intc/activity-ratio/days-of-sales-outstanding?utm_source=openai))
  - DIO (quarterly measures reported around 2024–2025) typically in the ~120–140 day range in recent quarters (example quarterly DIO ≈ 131.3 days for a recent quarter). ([discoverci.com](https://www.discoverci.com/companies/INTC/days-inventory-outstanding-dio?utm_source=openai))

- Broadcom Inc. — published measures (recent quarters):
  - DSO ≈ 31–35 days in recent quarters (example: 31.25 days). ([stock-data.online](https://stock-data.online/stock/avgo/activity-ratio?utm_source=openai))
  - DIO ≈ 33–38 days in recent quarters (example: 33.70 days). ([stock-data.online](https://stock-data.online/stock/avgo/activity-ratio/quarter?utm_source=openai))

Selected analyst and news facts (statements in public media about the same trends)
- Media and analyst reports around May–August 2025 described NVIDIA’s large H20-related inventory and purchase-obligation charge and its possible impact on China sales; these reports quote company disclosures that the H20-related actions could affect quarters’ revenues and margins. (Examples: Business Insider, CNBC, Investopedia coverage of the May 28, 2025 and Aug 27, 2025 results). ([businessinsider.com](https://www.businessinsider.com/nvidia-earnings-call-report-nvda-stock-live-updates-2025-5?utm_source=openai))

Source list (primary filings and press releases cited above)
- NVIDIA Form 10-Q, quarter ended July 27, 2025 (condensed consolidated financial statements and notes). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000209/nvda-20250727.htm))
- NVIDIA Form 10-Q, quarter ended April 27, 2025 (notes on H20 charges and excess purchase obligations). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000116/nvda-20250427.htm))
- NVIDIA Form 10-K for fiscal year ended January 26, 2025 (annual figures: FY2025 revenue, FY2025 cost of revenue, inventories as of Jan 26, 2025). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))
- NVIDIA press release — Q2 FY2026 results, Aug 27, 2025. ([investor.nvidia.com](https://investor.nvidia.com/news/press-release-details/2025/NVIDIA-Announces-Financial-Results-for-Second-Quarter-Fiscal-2026/default.aspx?utm_source=openai))
- NVIDIA press releases — Q3 FY25 and Q4 FY25 results (for quarterly revenue/cost figures used in LTM totals). ([nvidianews.nvidia.com](https://nvidianews.nvidia.com/news/nvidia-announces-financial-results-for-third-quarter-fiscal-2025))
- Peer data: AMD, Intel, Broadcom activity‑ratio pages and company filings/financial-data providers used for the “days” figures. ([stock-data.online](https://stock-data.online/stock/amd/activity-ratio/days-of-sales-outstanding?utm_source=openai))

(End of facts.)

## Point 14 - Question 3

**Have independent auditors, regulators, or the company itself identified material weaknesses, restatements, or other accounting issues that call financial controls into question?**

### Research Findings

- April 2002 / September 11, 2003 — The U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) found that NVIDIA had reported a quarter (April 30, 2000) with sales that were too high because the company recorded a $3.3 million supplier credit but did not record the company’s obligation to repay that credit later. The SEC said NVIDIA’s books and internal accounting controls were not adequate for that period and issued a cease-and-desist order. The SEC reported that the quarter’s gross profit was overstated by 6.4%, net income by 15.3%, and earnings per share by 14.8%. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/enforcement-litigation/administrative-proceedings/34-48480?utm_source=openai))

- September 11, 2003 — The SEC filed a separate enforcement action against NVIDIA’s former chief financial officer, Christine B. Hoberg, saying she failed to record the $3.3 million repayment obligation to the supplier. Hoberg consented to pay penalties and disgorgement (about $671,695) and was barred from serving as an officer or director of a public company for five years. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/enforcement-litigation/litigation-releases/lr-18343?utm_source=openai))

- 2006 (internal review completed November 13, 2006) — NVIDIA’s audit committee investigated company stock-option grant practices. The committee found some grants used incorrect measurement dates for accounting. NVIDIA amended (restated) prior financial statements for certain years and took non-cash charges (reported around $127 million) to correct stock-based compensation accounting. The company said the restatements were required because of those control deficiencies. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000119312506243226/d10qa.htm?utm_source=openai))

- As of January 29, 2006 (disclosed in the company’s filings) — NVIDIA’s management concluded that the control problems that led to the option-related restatements did not constitute a “material weakness” as of that date, because management said effective controls were in place at that time to prevent or detect a material misstatement. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000119312506243224/d10ka.htm?utm_source=openai))

- May 6, 2022 — The SEC charged NVIDIA for failing to disclose that growth in its “gaming” revenue in certain 2017 quarters was driven significantly by customers using GPUs for cryptomining. The SEC found NVIDIA had inadequate disclosure controls and procedures for that matter. NVIDIA agreed to a cease-and-desist order and to pay a $5.5 million civil penalty. The SEC said the company had violated disclosure rules and failed to maintain adequate disclosure controls. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/newsroom/press-releases/2022-79?utm_source=openai))

- February 21, 2024 and February 26, 2025 (Annual reports / Form 10-K) — NVIDIA’s independent registered public accounting firm, PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP (PwC), issued audit reports that expressed unqualified opinions on NVIDIA’s consolidated financial statements and stated that, as of January 28, 2024 and January 26, 2025 respectively, NVIDIA maintained effective internal control over financial reporting “in all material respects.” (The Form 10‑K filings include PwC’s audit reports and PwC’s consent to those reports.) ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/BC239FE0177447E4FEEA5C8C389B6E280A4BAD98?utm_source=openai))

- March–April 2025 (company disclosure) — NVIDIA disclosed that U.S. export license requirements put limits on certain products and said the company expected its first fiscal quarter of 2026 to include charges (inventory, purchase commitments, and related reserves) that could be up to approximately $5.5 billion. The company filed this information in an SEC Form 8‑K in April 2025. (This is a company disclosure about large charges and reserves; it does not itself state a control failure or restatement.) ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000082/nvda-20250409.htm?utm_source=openai))

- Summary of company and regulator actions in plain language:
  - Regulators (the SEC) have in the past found that NVIDIA’s past financial reports were incorrect and ordered remedies (2002/2003). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/enforcement-litigation/administrative-proceedings/34-48480?utm_source=openai))
  - NVIDIA’s own audit committee and management have investigated and restated prior results for stock-option accounting problems (2006) and disclosed the corrections. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000119312506243226/d10qa.htm?utm_source=openai))
  - The SEC separately fined NVIDIA in 2022 for not disclosing that cryptomining had driven parts of its gaming revenue and said NVIDIA’s disclosure controls were inadequate for that issue. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/newsroom/press-releases/2022-79?utm_source=openai))
  - In recent annual audits (2024 and 2025), the company’s auditor (PwC) issued clean (unqualified) audit opinions and said NVIDIA’s internal controls over financial reporting were effective as of the reported audit dates. ([publicnow.com](https://www.publicnow.com/view/BC239FE0177447E4FEEA5C8C389B6E280A4BAD98?utm_source=openai))

(End of facts.)

### Point 15 Criterion

How effective are the company’s research and development efforts in relation to its size?

## Point 15 - Question 1

**How has R&D spending (absolute dollars and as a percentage of sales) trended over the past five years, and how does this compare with close industry peers after adjusting for differences in what each firm classifies as R&D?**

### Research Findings

NVIDIA (ticker NVDA) — fiscal-year R&D totals and R&D as a percent of sales
- Fiscal year ended Jan 26, 2025: R&D expense $12,914 million; R&D = 9.9% of revenue. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
- Fiscal year ended Jan 28, 2024: R&D expense $8,675 million; R&D = 14.2% of revenue. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm))  
- Fiscal year ended Jan 29, 2023: R&D expense $7,339 million; R&D = 27.2% of revenue. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581023000017/nvda-20230129.htm))  
- Fiscal year ended Jan 30, 2022: R&D expense $5,268 million; R&D = 19.6% of revenue. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm))  
- Fiscal year ended Jan 31, 2021: R&D expense $2,071 million; (company revenue for that year shown in filings). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581023000017/nvda-20230129.htm))

Notes from NVIDIA’s filings about what is included or reported separately
- NVIDIA reports stock‑based compensation inside operating expenses (including amounts allocated to R&D), and it shows amounts of research-related costs that the company has capitalized for tax/financial reporting purposes (the company discloses a growing balance described as “capitalized research and development expenditure” on its deferred tax note). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm))  
- NVIDIA’s reported “capitalized research and development expenditure” (a balance reported in the tax/deferred‑tax note) rose to $6,256 million as of Jan 26, 2025 and was $3,376 million as of Jan 28, 2024. These balances indicate amounts of R&D-related costs that the company has on its books as capitalized (tax/balance‑sheet) amounts. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
- NVIDIA’s filings call attention to the U.S. tax rules (TCJA) that require certain R&D expenditures to be capitalized for tax purposes beginning in the relevant fiscal period; the company discloses the tax impact in its filings. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581023000017/nvda-20230129.htm))

Peer: Advanced Micro Devices (AMD) — fiscal R&D totals and percent of sales (selected years)
- Fiscal year ended Dec 28, 2024: R&D expense $6,456 million; net revenue $25,785 million → R&D ≈ 25.0% of revenue. ([ir.amd.com](https://ir.amd.com/financial-information/sec-filings/content/0000002488-25-000012/amd-20241228.htm))  
- Fiscal year ended Dec 30, 2023: R&D expense $5,872 million; net revenue $22,680 million → R&D ≈ 25.9% of revenue. ([ir.amd.com](https://ir.amd.com/financial-information/sec-filings/content/0000002488-25-000012/amd-20241228.htm))  
- Fiscal year ended Dec 31, 2022: R&D expense $5,005 million; net revenue $23,601 million → R&D ≈ 21.2% of revenue. ([ir.amd.com](https://ir.amd.com/financial-information/sec-filings/content/0000002488-25-000012/amd-20241228.htm))  
- Fiscal year 2021 (calendar/fiscal): R&D expense (annual) $2,845 million (public historical dataset). ([pro.macrotrends.net](https://pro.macrotrends.net/stocks/charts/AMD/amd/research-development-expenses?utm_source=openai))  
- Fiscal year 2020 (annual): R&D expense (annual) $1,983 million (public historical dataset). ([pro.macrotrends.net](https://pro.macrotrends.net/stocks/charts/AMD/amd/research-development-expenses?utm_source=openai))

Notes from AMD’s filings about classification
- AMD shows stock‑based compensation included in R&D (the filing discloses the portion of stock‑based comp allocated to R&D). AMD’s public filings do not present large balances like NVIDIA’s “capitalized research and development expenditure” in the same way; AMD discusses the tax treatment change under U.S. rules that affects how some R&D is treated for tax purposes, but AMD’s consolidated statements show R&D as operating expense amounts. ([ir.amd.com](https://ir.amd.com/financial-information/sec-filings/content/0000002488-25-000012/amd-20241228.htm))

Peer: Intel Corporation — fiscal R&D totals and percent of sales (selected years)
- Fiscal year ended Dec 28, 2024: R&D expense $16,546 million; net revenue $53,101 million → R&D ≈ 31.2% of revenue. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/50863/000005086325000009/intc-20241228.htm))  
- Fiscal year ended Dec 30, 2023: R&D expense $16,046 million; net revenue $54,228 million → R&D ≈ 29.6% of revenue. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/50863/000005086325000009/intc-20241228.htm))  
- Fiscal year ended Dec 31, 2022: R&D expense $17,528 million; net revenue $63,054 million → R&D ≈ 27.8% of revenue. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/50863/000005086325000009/intc-20241228.htm))  
- Fiscal year 2021 (annual): R&D expense (annual) $15,190 million (public historical dataset). ([macrotrends.net](https://macrotrends.net/stocks/charts/INTC/intel/research-development-expenses?utm_source=openai))  
- Fiscal year 2020 (annual): R&D expense (annual) $13,556 million (public historical dataset). ([macrotrends.net](https://macrotrends.net/stocks/charts/INTC/intel/research-development-expenses?utm_source=openai))

Notes from Intel’s filings about classification and comparability
- Intel’s filings show very large R&D spending driven in part by investments in process technology and manufacturing R&D. Intel’s consolidated statements also include acquisition‑related intangible items (including in‑process R&D recorded on acquisitions) and show interest capitalized on certain long‑lived assets; Intel’s R&D line in the consolidated statements is the operating expense labeled “Research and development.” These elements (process/foundry investments, acquisition IPR&D, capitalized interest, and where costs are recorded) mean Intel’s R&D number reflects a different business model mix (including foundry and heavy process‑technology investment) compared with fabless peers. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/50863/000005086325000009/intc-20241228.htm))

Other facts that affect apples‑to‑apples comparisons
- Some companies (including NVIDIA) disclose amounts of R&D costs that are capitalized (shown in deferred tax notes and balance‑sheet related notes). Capitalized development costs can be recorded on the balance sheet and then amortized; those capitalized amounts are not fully visible in the single “R&D expense” line unless the company discloses additions and amortization. NVIDIA’s deferred‑tax note shows a large and rising balance labeled “Capitalized research and development expenditure.” ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
- Tax rules (U.S. TCJA changes referenced in company filings) required certain R&D costs to be capitalized for tax purposes starting in the relevant years; companies’ filings note the tax impact separately from GAAP R&D expense. This affects the tax presentation and deferred tax items even when GAAP R&D expense is reported in the income statement. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581023000017/nvda-20230129.htm))  
- Companies differ in whether and how they (a) capitalize internal‑use software or engineering development costs, (b) record in‑process R&D from acquisitions as intangible assets, and (c) allocate stock‑based compensation into R&D. These differences appear in the notes to each company’s consolidated financial statements and affect whether a simple “R&D expense” line is directly comparable across firms. Example disclosures: NVIDIA and AMD show stock‑based compensation amounts allocated to R&D; NVIDIA and AMD disclose capitalized R&D/tax balances in notes; Intel discloses large process‑technology investments and acquisition‑related IPR&D in its notes. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm))

Sources (company filings and public financial datasets used above)
- NVIDIA Corporation, Annual Reports / Form 10‑K (fiscal years shown): NVDA filings and consolidated statements. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
- NVIDIA — deferred tax / capitalized R&D note in 10‑K (capitalized research and development expenditure balances). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581025000023/nvda-20250126.htm))  
- Advanced Micro Devices, Inc., Form 10‑K (fiscal 2024 filing; consolidated statements). ([ir.amd.com](https://ir.amd.com/financial-information/sec-filings/content/0000002488-25-000012/amd-20241228.htm))  
- AMD historical R&D and earlier-year numbers (public financial data). ([pro.macrotrends.net](https://pro.macrotrends.net/stocks/charts/AMD/amd/research-development-expenses?utm_source=openai))  
- Intel Corporation, Form 10‑K (fiscal 2024 filing; consolidated statements and MD&A). ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/50863/000005086325000009/intc-20241228.htm))  
- Intel historical R&D and earlier-year numbers (public financial data). ([macrotrends.net](https://macrotrends.net/stocks/charts/INTC/intel/research-development-expenses?utm_source=openai))

(End of facts.)

---

## Point 15 - Question 2

**What evidence shows that the company converts its R&D outlays into commercially successful products, processes, or cost savings large enough to justify the spending relative to company scale?**

### Research Findings

- R&D spending (company report): NVIDIA spent $12,914 million on research and development in fiscal year 2025 (the year ended Jan 26, 2025). This was 9.9% of the company’s revenue that year. ([fintel.io](https://fintel.io/doc/sec-nvidia-corp-1045810-10k-2025-february-26-20145-3358))

- R&D spending (prior year): NVIDIA spent $8,675 million on research and development in fiscal year 2024 (the year ended Jan 28, 2024). This was 14.2% of revenue that year. ([sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1045810/000104581024000029/nvda-20240128.htm))
